401 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Smith


Court of Appeals No. 08CA2071


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SIX


312 P.3d 1173; 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 1226



September 2, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 30, 2010. As Amended October 14, 2010.
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part People v. Smith, 2011 Colo. LEXIS 363 (Colo., Apr. 25, 2011)
Reversed by, Remanded by People v. Smith, 2014 Colo. LEXIS 58 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Larimer County District Court No. 08CR633. Honorable Terence A. Gilmore, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, ORDER REVERSED, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Larimer County District Court, Colorado, denied defendant's motion to suppress, and a jury found him guilty of first degree criminal trespass. The trial court awarded defendant 60 days of presentence confinement credit for 89 days in jail prior to trial and sentencing. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals found no error in the denial of defendant's motion to suppress. An officer who was investigating an altercation between defendant and another individual did not exceed the level of force permissible under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Colo. Const. art. II, § 7 during an investigatory stop. When the officer arrived, he faced a difficult and dangerous challenge. The scene was dark, and the officer was not able to tell if others, besides defendant and the other individual in the altercation, were present. The situation worsened when the officer saw defendant toss aside a guitar case and defendant told the officer that there was an unsecured shotgun at the scene. The officer drew his gun and ordered defendant and the other individual to lie face down on the ground and waited less than a minute for another officer to arrive. The court also held that defendant was not in custody during a patrol car interview, and therefore that U.S. Const. amend. V did not require suppression of his statements. The officer explicitly told defendant that he was not under arrest and asked whether defendant wanted to sit in the back of the patrol car because it was cold.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction, reversed the trial court's denial of a portion of defendant's presentence confinement credit, and remanded with directions.

 

402 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Whiting Oil & Gas Corp. v. Atl. Richfield Co.


Court of Appeals No. 09CA1081


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


321 P.3d 500; 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 1223; 178 Oil & Gas Rep. 625



September 2, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari granted Atlantic Richfield Co. v. Whiting Oil & Gas Corp., 2011 Colo. LEXIS 630 (Colo., Aug. 1, 2011)
affirmed on other grounds by Atl. Richfield Co. v. Whiting Oil & Gas Corp., 320 P.3d 1179, 2014 Colo. LEXIS 142 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Rio Blanco County District Court No. 06CV37. Honorable James B. Boyd, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant seller appealed a judgment from the Rio Blanco County District Court (Colorado), which reformed a contractual option to purchase real property, concluded that plaintiff buyer was entitled to specific performance of the reformed option, and imposed a constructive trust on the seller's interest in the property until the seller delivered the deed required by the trial court's judgment.


OVERVIEW: The parties entered into an agreement to conduct an oil shale research and development project on the property, which they jointly owned. An amended provision gave the buyer an option to purchase the seller's interest in the property. After the buyer attempted to exercise the option more than 21 years later, the seller contended that it was unenforceable. The trial court found that the option violated the common law rule against perpetuities because it named no life in being and could be exercised more than 21 years after the parties entered into the amendment. The trial court further found that although the buyer had breached some of its duties under the agreement, the breaches were not material. The court concluded that the record supported the trial court's finding that the breaches were not material because the oil shale industry had become unprofitable. Reformation of the option was authorized under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 15-11-1106(2) (2009), which was not limited to probate instruments. The application of § 15-11-1106(2) was not unconstitutionally retrospective. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in rejecting the seller's unclean hands defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

403 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Morris-Schindler, LLC v. City & County of Denver


Court of Appeals No. 09CA1997


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


251 P.3d 1076; 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 1216



September 2, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 08CV5124. Honorable Catherine A. Lemon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff licensee appealed an order of the District Court of the City and County of Denver, Colorado, upholding the nonrenewal of its hotel and restaurant liquor license by defendant city.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that the city's director of excise and licenses abused her discretion by applying a strict liability standard for violations of the Colorado Liquor Code. Each provision of the Code cited by the director as a violation by the licensee, which formed the basis for good cause not to renew, contains the word "permit," which requires some level of knowledge, rather than strict liability. There was no competent evidence in the record to establish that the licensee had actual or constructive knowledge of an undercover narcotics transaction inside the premises. However, there was competent evidence concerning the regular presence of overserved, intoxicated patrons loitering in front of the establishment in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-47-901(5)(a) (2009). The licensee did not dispute incidents of serving underage customers in violation of § 12-47-901(1)(a.5). The court rejected the licensee's argument that the renewal process under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-47-302 (2009) is parallel to the sanction process under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-47-601 (2009). It also rejected the licensee's argument that § 12-47-302 is unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed as to the findings of serving underage customers and intoxicated patrons but was otherwise reversed, and the case was remanded to the district court with orders to remand to the director for further proceedings.

 

404 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Frye


Court of Appeals No. 08CA2321


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


277 P.3d 825; 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 854



June 24, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari granted, Vacated by, Remanded by People v. Frye, 2011 Colo. LEXIS 890 (Colo., Nov. 14, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Arapahoe County District Court No. 06CR3642. Honorable Charles M. Pratt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a first degree murder case, the State appealed an order of the Arapahoe County District Court, Colorado, excluding the testimony of defendant's sister under Colo. R. Evid. 807, the residual exception to the rule against hearsay. As a result of that order, the case was dismissed at the prosecution's request. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's sister testified that their mother had told her that defendant had confessed to killing his wife. The State wanted to appeal an evidentiary ruling of a kind other than that allowed under the interlocutory appeal provisions of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-12-102(2) (2009) and Colo. App. R. 4.1. The appellate court concluded that lacked jurisdiction to hear the appeal. The trial court's granting of the State's request for dismissal of the case did not constitute a final judgment from which an appeal of a question of law could be taken under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-12-102(1). The State's remedy, if any, from the trial court's evidentiary ruling lay in an original proceeding, brought pursuant to Colo. App. R. 21 in the Colorado Supreme Court prior to any dismissal of the case. The State unsuccessfully attempted that route. Because the State was not entitled to review from the appellate court, the appeal was subject to dismissal.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

405 of 734 DOCUMENTS


In re J.M.A.


Court of Appeals No. 09CA2620


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


240 P.3d 547; 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 810



June 10, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Clear Creek County District Court No. 09JR12. Honorable Russell H. Granger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Clear Creek County District Court, Colorado, denied appellant father's Colo. R. Civ. P. 60(b) motion for relief from the March 25, 2009, order terminating his parental rights after the child's birth mother relinquished custody of the child pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-5-103.5 (2009). The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that he was denied due process when the district court declined to consider his request for relief from the termination of his parental rights. The appellate court did not have to consider his argument that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-5-105(4) (2009) was unconstitutional on its face because he did not make it in the district court. It could consider his contention that applying the ninety-day limitations period set forth in § 19-5-105(4) unconstitutionally deprived him of due process in the circumstances of the case. The appellate court found that the statute should not be interpreted so as to bar a due process challenge to the termination of a parent's rights when the parent alleged a lack of notice or insufficient notice of the proceedings resulting from the other parent's failure to refusal to identify him as a possible parent. Nothing the father did or did not do deprived him of the right to be given notice that the mother had initiated a proceeding in which his parental rights could be terminated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded for a hearing on the father's motion for relief from the order terminating his parental rights.

 

406 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Colo. Consumer Health Initiative v. Colo. Bd. of Health


Court of Appeals No. 09CA0822


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


240 P.3d 525; 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 819



June 10, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 08CV2375. Honorable Herbert L. Stern, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The City and County of Denver District Court, Colorado, granted summary judgment in favor of defendant, the Colorado Board of Health (Board) in plaintiff organization's declaratory judgment action challenging the Board's "patient copy" rule. The organization appealed.


OVERVIEW: The organization argued that, because the patient copy rule did not comply with the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act (HIPAA), the trial court erred in entering summary judgment for the Board and against the organization. The appellate court noted that because HIPAA was not in effect until 2003, the Board's 2001 rule amending the patient copy rule was not subject to HIPAA's rules regarding copying patient records. When HIPAA took effect in 2003, the portion of the 2001 rule that applied to HIPAA-covered individuals was required to come into compliance with HIPAA. The Board's proposed amendment did not show that the copy fees charged to HIPAA-covered persons were cost-based and excluded ancillary costs. Because the General Assembly used the phrase "payment of the reasonable costs," Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 25-1-801(1)(b)(I) and 25-1-802(1)(b)(I) (2009) only authorized health care facilities and individual providers to charge patients for the reasonable costs of providing the copies. The Board's 2001 and 2008 patient copy rules did not support the Board's summary judgment motion because they did not indicate that the copy fees reflected costs.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying the organization's motion was affirmed; the order granting the Board's summary judgment motion was reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

 

407 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Bruce v. City of Colo. Springs


Court of Appeals No. 09CA1541


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SIX


252 P.3d 30; 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 822



June 10, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Bruce v. City of Colorado Springs, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 750 (Colo., Oct. 12, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
El Paso County District Court No. 07CV244. Honorable David A. Gilbert, Judge.
Bruce v. City of Colo. Springs, 200 P.3d 1140, 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 2176 (Colo. Ct. App., 2008)



DISPOSITION: ORDERS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a proponent of a proposed ballot initiative, challenged the orders issued by the El Paso County District Court, Colorado, finding that the single subject ordinance of appellee city was not unconstitutional and that the proponent's petition for an initiated ordinance violated the single subject rule, and denying his motion seeking disqualification of the trial judge.


OVERVIEW: The proponent attempted unsuccessfully to place an initiative on the city's municipal ballot. The proponent argued that the city's single subject ordinance was unconstitutional because it was adopted without first holding a public election to allow voters to decide the matter through a state constitutional amendment, and because it violated the right to petition. The appellate court ruled that Colorado Springs, Colo., City Code § 5.1.503, the city's ordinance requiring a single subject to be expressed in ballot initiatives, did not offend the Colorado Constitution. The city, as a home rule city, was authorized to enact ordinances establishing the manner in which municipal legislation was exercised, which included ordinances that required initiatives submitted for voter approval to contain only single subjects. Also, the appellate court agreed with the trial court that the proposed initiative contained more than one subject with two distinct and separate purposes. Furthermore, the motion to disqualify the trial judge was insufficient to warrant recusal. The allegations of bias and prejudice were based largely on the trial judge's prior rulings.


OUTCOME: The orders were affirmed.

 

408 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Trujillo


Court of Appeals No. 06CA0697


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


251 P.3d 477; 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 813



June 10, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Trujillo v. People, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 915 (Colo., Nov. 30, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Jefferson County District Court No. 04CR3020. Honorable Thomas C. Levi, Judge. Honorable Tom Woodford, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Jefferson County District Court (Colorado) found defendant guilty of aggravated incest under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6-302 (2009) and sexual assault on a child by one in a position of trust under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-405.3 (2009). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Before trial, the prosecution moved to admit separate hearsay statements that the victim, defendant's daughter, had made about the assault to her mother, a physician, and a social worker. After a hearing, the trial court found that the statements were admissible under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-25-129 (2009). They were presented to the jury, although the victim also testified at trial. Defendant contended that the trial court erred by admitting the child victim's hearsay statements under § 13-25-129. Defendant asserted that the statute should be interpreted as applying only to victims who were less than 15 years of age at the time of any unlawful sexual offense under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-411(1) (2009). The victim was 16 years old when defendant allegedly assaulted her. Because the phrase "when the victim was less than fifteen years of age at the time of the commission of the offense" in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-25-129(1) applied only to a victim of incest under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6-301 (2009), which defendant was not charged with, the appellate court concluded that the trial court did not err by admitting the victim's hearsay statements under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-25-129 (2009).


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

409 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Cerbo v. Protect Colo. Jobs, Inc.


Court of Appeals No. 09CA0587


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SEVEN


240 P.3d 495; 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 685



May 13, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified June 10, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Office of Administrative Courts. Case No. OS080017.



DISPOSITION: ORDER REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An administrative law judge (ALJ) with the Colorado Office of Administrative Courts entered an order determining that respondent organization was not an "issue committee" within the meaning of Colo. Const. art. XXVIII, § 2(10)(a), with respect to a right-to-work ballot initiative and that the organization had not violated Colo. Rev. Stat. § 1-45-108(1)(a)(I) and (3) (2009) of the Fair Campaign Practices Act. Appellant complainant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that the facts in the record demonstrated that the organization had a major purpose of supporting the initiative. The ALJ erred in her analysis in three ways: (1) she placed undue weight on the fact the organization had purposes other than supporting the initiative; (2) she gave too much weight to activities that the organization merely considered undertaking while giving too little weight to what it actually did; and (3) she failed to give weight to other facts relevant to the inquiry. Because the organization was created at the same time the ballot issue was conceived of, was operated and represented by individuals otherwise intimately involved in drafting and promoting the ballot issue individually and through other organizations, spent its entire first year promoting the ballot issue to the exclusion of almost all other activities, and spent three-fourths of all of the funds it had ever expended promoting that ballot issue, the conclusion was inescapable that the organization had a major purpose of supporting the ballot issue. The phrase "a major purpose" in Colo. Const. art. XXVIII, § 2(10)(a)(I), was not unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings on whether the organization was an "issue committee" under Colo. Const. art. XXVIII, § 2(10)(a), and if necessary, for the imposition of appropriate penalties if the ALJ were to determine that the organization was an issue committee and failed to comply with the Act's registration and reporting requirements.

Vickery v. Vickery


Court of Appeals No. 09CA0586


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SIX


271 P.3d 516; 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 356



March 18, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part Vickery v. Vickery, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 761 (Colo., Oct. 18, 2010)
Related proceeding at Vickery v. Evelyn V. Trumble Living Trust, 2011 Colo. App. LEXIS 1399 (Colo. Ct. App., Aug. 18, 2011)
Reversed by, Remanded by Vickery v. Evans, 266 P.3d 390, 2011 Colo. LEXIS 931 (Colo., Dec. 12, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 07CV7674. Honorable Robert L. McGahey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a suit alleging claims of defamation and malicious prosecution, plaintiff, the wife of a decedent, appealed a judgment of the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) against defendant, the decedent's sister, arguing that the district court erred in reducing the jury's award of exemplary damages and in denying her motion to increase exemplary damages under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-21-102(1)(a) and (3) (2009).


OVERVIEW: During the decedent's final illness, his wife and sister became embroiled in a bitter dispute. Following the decedent's death, his sister accused his police sergeant wife of murder, fraud, theft, and misuse of police authority. The wife filed suit alleging claims of malicious prosecution and defamation. The district court found in favor of the wife as a matter of law but submitted the issue of damages to the jury. In seeking additional punitive damages, the wife pointed the fact that her husband's sister continued her defamatory and malicious conduct during the pendency of the present litigation. On review of the judgment entered, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the motion to increase the exemplary damages award because Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-21-102(3) did not require the trial court to increase the exemplary damages beyond the statutory amount that could be properly awarded by the jury as compensatory damages. Further, the trial court did not err under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-21-102(1)(a) in reducing the jury's award of exemplary damages because it properly capped the exemplary damages award at the amount of the compensatory damages.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

People v. Key


Court of Appeals No. 07CA1257


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SIX


2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 361



March 18, 2010, Decided


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION IS NOT THE FINAL VERSION AND SUBJECT TO REVISION UPON FINAL PUBLICATION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied People v. Key, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 919 (Colo., Nov. 30, 2010)
Vacated by, Remanded by Colorado v. Key, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 4912 (U.S., June 27, 2011)
On remand at People v. Key, 2011 Colo. App. LEXIS 1416 (Colo. Ct. App., Aug. 25, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Pitkin County District Court Nos. 05CR50 & 06CR62. Honorable James B. Boyd, Judge. Honorable Robert A. Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Pitkin County District Court (Colorado) that convicted him of felony theft, misdemeanor theft, and unlawful use of a financial transaction device, arguing that the district court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stole a cell phone and a wallet while at a nightclub and made withdrawals from a victim's bank account using stolen debit cards. Bank surveillance video captured defendant making the unauthorized withdrawals, and the cell phone was found during a search of his car when he was arrested on an unrelated charge. On review, the court held that, under the U.S. Supreme Court's recent Gant ruling, the police violated defendant's Fourth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. IV, rights when they searched defendant's car incident to his arrest because defendant had already been secured and was beyond reaching distance of the car's passenger compartment when the search was conducted. However, although the court recognized that, under the retroactive application of Gant, the police violated defendant's Fourth Amendment rights, it declined to apply the remedy of suppressing the evidence because the statutory good faith exception under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-3-308 supported the denial of defendant's motion to suppress, as the court found it reasonable for the police to act according to Supreme Court precedent as it existed on the date they conducted the search.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

412 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Colo. Ethics Watch v. Senate Majority Fund, LLC


Court of Appeals Nos. 08CA2689 & 09CA0384


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


275 P.3d 674; 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 368



March 18, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part Colo. Ethics Watch v. Senate Majority Fund, LLC, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 914 (Colo., Nov. 30, 2010)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Colo. Ethics Watch v. Senate Majority Fund, LLC, 2012 Colo. LEXIS 103 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Office of Administrative Courts OS No. 2008-0028.



DISPOSITION: ORDERS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant special interest group sued respondent tax-exempt political organizations for alleged violations of Colorado's campaign finance laws. The administrative law judge (ALJ) granted respondents' motion to dismiss, finding that their advertisements did not constitute "express advocacy" for purposes of Colo. Const. art. XXVIII, § 2(8). Appellant filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: Respondents were tax-exempt political organizations. During the 2008 election cycle, respondents paid for and distributed advertisements discussing certain candidates for the state legislature. Appellant alleged that respondents had engaged in advertising for the purpose of expressly advocating the election of certain candidates. Appellant contended that this rendered both organizations "political committees" pursuant to Colo. Const. art. XXVIII, § 2(12)(a) and Colo. Rev. Stat. § 1-45-103(14) (2009). Appellant claimed that respondents were required to register as political committees with the secretary of state and comply with restrictions as to the amount of contributions that they could accept. The ALJ granted respondents' motion to dismiss, finding that the advertisements in question did not constitute "express advocacy" as the ALJ construed that phrase. The Court of Appeals of Colorado upheld the decision. Respondents' advertisements merely stated that local leaders endorsed a particular candidate. These advertisements did not meet the definition of express advocacy under Colo. Const. art. XXVIII, § 2(8), because they did not contain the "magic words."


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

413 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gardner


Court of Appeals No. 09CA0085


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


250 P.3d 1262; 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 270



March 4, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied People v. Gardner, 2011 Colo. LEXIS 170 (Colo., Feb. 22, 2011)
Related proceeding at Gardner v. Clements, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 20962 (D. Colo., Feb. 21, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court Nos. 05CR4037 & 05CR5321. Honorable Martin F. Egelhoff, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order of the City and County of Denver District Court, Colorado, denying his motion for postconviction relief under Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c) following the entry of guilty pleas.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to three counts of theft over $ 15,000, each a class three felony in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-4-401(1), (2)(d). In postconviction proceedings, appellant's double jeopardy claim was not waived by his entry of a guilty plea. Section 18-4-401(4) designated all instances of theft within a six-month period as a single theft offense; because two of the theft counts occurred within a single six-month period, his conviction violated his right to be free from double jeopardy. The Court of Appeals of Colorado held that he was entitled to have two of the convictions merged. The felony complaints tracking the language of section 18-4-401(1) were sufficient to invoke the jurisdiction of the county court, which had power to bind felony cases over to the district courts. Appellant's admission that the substantive crimes of theft occurred in Denver was sufficient to prove a factual basis for the court's jurisdiction. By entering a guilty plea, appellant waived his equal protection challenge to the theft statute. The district court had the power to sentence appellant to the custody of the department of corrections.


OUTCOME: The district court's order was reversed as to appellant's claim of multiplicitous charges in 05CR5321; the order was affirmed in all other respects. The case was remanded for the district court to merge appellant's two convictions in 05CR5321 and to resentence him to two six-year terms, running consecutively.

 

414 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Collins


Court of Appeals No. 06CA1235


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SIX


250 P.3d 668; 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 214



February 18, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Collins v. People, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 825 (Colo., Nov. 8, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 05CR2654. Honorable Shelley I. Gilman, Judge. Honorable Larry J. Naves, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) that convicted him of second-degree kidnapping, first-degree sexual assault, and attempted aggravated robbery, arguing that the district court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence under U.S. Const. amend. IV, and Colo. Const. art. II, § 7.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested in Missouri on an armed robbery charge. The police believed that they could link him to another robbery, and defendant consented to give a DNA sample. After noting that defendant had a Colorado arrest record, the police contacted Denver police and forwarded defendant's DNA profile to them. Based upon that DNA profile, defendant was charged with kidnapping, rape, and robbery stemming from an attack upon a woman four years earlier. Defendant moved to suppress, but the trial court denied his motion. On review, the court held that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion because his consent was voluntary even though Missouri law enforcement officials did not expressly advise him that his DNA would be used for purposes other than determining whether his DNA matched DNA associated with the Missouri robbery charge; defendant consented to provide a DNA sample and failed to limit his consent in any way. Under the totality of the circumstances, defendant's consent was not rendered involuntary merely because the Missouri authorities did not expressly inform him that his DNA sample might be used to implicate him in other crimes.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

In re Marriage of Davis


Court of Appeals No. 09CA1002


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


252 P.3d 530; 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 1982



February 17, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Arapahoe County District Court No. 89DR2840. Honorable Robert H. Russell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The trial court had to recalculate the child support obligations that accrued before January 1, 2008, without applying the amended version of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 14-10-115(6)(b)(I). The trial court did not err by excluding the employer's contributions to the husband's plans from his income for child support purposes. The child's employment income was properly included in the child support calculation. The trial court did not err by not finding the husband in contempt for violating a prior court order, Colo. R. Civ. P. 107(a)(1).


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded with directions.

 

416 of 734 DOCUMENTS


In re Parental Responsibilities of Reese


Court of Appeals No. 08CA2428


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


227 P.3d 900; 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 142



February 4, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Adams County District Court No. 08DR10. Honorable F. Michael Goodbee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER VACATED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Adams County District Court, Colorado, awarded sole decision-making authority and majority parenting time to petitioner couple. Respondent mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that the trial court did not give special weight to her determination of the child's best interests. The appellate court found that when a non-parent sought allocation of parental responsibilities contrary to the wishes of a parent, the court may not allocate parental responsibilities to the non-parent unless it complied with the requirement to accord "special weight" to the parent's determination of the best interests of the chid. The court had to consider all relevant factors including those listed in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 14-10-124(1.5)(a) and (b) (2009). A parent's liberty interest in the care, custody, and control of his or her child was not infringed when the parent's determination regarding the best interests of the child was overcome by clear and convincing proof of relevant factors and the court's determination of the best interests of the child. The trial court's finding that the couple were psychological parents was not sufficient to accord special weight to the mother's parental rights. The record did not demonstrate that the court accorded any "special weight" to the mother's liberty interest in the care, custody, and control of the child.


OUTCOME: The order was vacated and remanded to the trial court for a determination of whether the couple met their burden of proof that allocation of parental responsibilities to them was in the best interests of the child.

 

417 of 734 DOCUMENTS


O'Quinn v. Baca


Court of Appeals No. 09CA0388


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


250 P.3d 629; 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 1



January 7, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by O'Quinn v. Baca, 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 489 (Colo. Ct. App., Apr. 1, 2010)
Writ of certiorari denied O'Quinn v. Baca, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 763 (Colo., Oct. 18, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 07CV11938. Honorable R. Michael Mullins, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a personal injury action, plaintiff injured pedestrian appealed the judgment of the City and County of Denver District Court, Colorado, awarding costs to defendant driver.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was hit by defendant's car. He sued defendant for negligence. She timely offered to settle the case for $ 75,000. Plaintiff rejected the offer. The matter proceeded to trial, where the jury returned a verdict awarding him $ 54,000 in damages. Because that figure did not exceed defendant's $ 75,000 settlement offer, the trial court ordered plaintiff to pay defendant's costs of $ 25,721 pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 13-17-202, 13-16-105 (2009). On appeal, plaintiff contended that the offer of settlement statute was unconstitutional. Plaintiff's brief did not comply with Colo. App. R. 28(k), by directing the court to a place in the record where the constitutional issue was raised and ruled upon. Having thoroughly examined the 834-page record, the Court of Appeals of Colorado found no indication that plaintiff presented to the trial court any constitutional challenge to the validity of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-17-202. Therefore, the issue was not properly preserved for review.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Flockhart


Court of Appeals No. 07CA0312


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


310 P.3d 66; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1967



December 24, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Flockhart, 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 298 (Colo. Ct. App., Mar. 4, 2010)
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part People v. Flockhart, 2011 Colo. LEXIS 149 (Colo., Feb. 22, 2011)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by People v. Flockhart, 304 P.3d 227, 2013 Colo. LEXIS 471 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Chaffee County District Court No. 06CR40. Honorable Charles M. Barton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT VACATED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Chaffee County District Court, Colorado, convicting him of possession and distribution of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with distribution of marijuana and possession of eight ounces or more of marijuana. The trial court did not err in failing to suppress the evidence found in a search of the building adjacent to defendant's residence, because he lacked standing to challenge the search. The information tracked the statutory language and provided surrounding factual details sufficient to vest jurisdiction over the possession of marijuana offense. The trial judge was not required to recuse himself, because he had acted as a prosecuting attorney in a case against defendant seven years earlier. The trial judge had no knowledge of evidentiary facts concerning the current proceeding. The trial court committed constitutional error by giving the jury a predeliberation instruction several times during the three-day trial; the People did not point to any evidence to overcome the predeliberation presumption. The Court of Appeals of Colorado held that the error was not harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was vacated, and the case was remanded to the trial court for a hearing on the predeliberation issue and for further proceedings.

People v. Ford

COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


232 P.3d 260; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1915



December 10, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied, En banc Ford v. People, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 475 (Colo., June 21, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
El Paso County District Court No. 07CR5767. Honorable David S. Prince, Judge.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the El Paso County District Court (Colorado), which denied his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to one count of identity theft, in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-5-902(1)(a) and (f) (2009). Defendant later filed a motion for postconviction relief, claiming that the identity theft statute underlying his conviction violated his equal protection rights. The trial court upheld the constitutionality of the statute. On appeal, the court found that defendant's claim could not be resolved by looking to the structure of the information and guilty plea at the time of the providency hearing. Because defendant's challenge required the court to consult the facts underlying the plea, it did not fall within the exceptions to the general rule that guilty pleas barred the right to raise constitutional questions. Because defendant did not raise a postconviction issue that qualified as an exception to the general rule that a guilty plea barred constitutional challenges, his appeal had to be dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

 

421 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Baldwin v. Huber


Court of Appeals No. 08CA2492


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


223 P.3d 150; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1907



November 25, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Adams County District Court No. 08CV303. Honorable C. Scott Crabtree, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensee challenged the judgment of the Adams County District Court, Colorado, affirming the revocation of her driver's license by appellee Texas Department of Revenue, for driving with an excessive breath alcohol content.


OVERVIEW: In the criminal summons, the arresting officer identified the initial traffic violation as weaving. The licensee testified that the arresting officer arrived at the scene several minutes after other police officers had stopped her, and she specifically denied any weaving and testified that she had driven for only two blocks. The appellate court ruled that the evidence at the revocation hearing was sufficient to support the hearing officer's conclusions that there was reasonable suspicion to justify the initial traffic stop and probable cause to justify defendant's arrest. Since the arresting officer did not testify, his assertions in the documentary evidence were hearsay, and there was no indication in the documentary evidence whether his assertions that the licensee was weaving were based on his own observations of the licensee's driving as the stopping officer or whether they were based instead on information from fellow police officers making the initial stop. Nevertheless, the hearing officer credited this evidence and it was sufficiently reliable and trustworthy to support the factual finding that the licensee was weaving.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

422 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Curren


Court of Appeals No. 09CA0872


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


228 P.3d 253; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1908



November 25, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied People v. Curren, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 311 (Colo., Apr. 12, 2010)
Appeal after remand at, Decision reached on appeal by People v. Curren, 2014 Colo. App. LEXIS 763 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Adams County District Court No. 97CR3075. Honorable Thomas R. Ensor, Judge.
People v. Curren, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 863 (Colo. Ct. App., June 2, 2005)



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from an order of the Adams County District Court, Colorado, granting defendant's Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c) motion which vacated his conviction on two counts of felony first degree murder, and ordered a new trial based on an actual conflict of interest of trial counsel.


OVERVIEW: An investigation surrounding two corpses led to defendant. Defendant was arrested in Mexico. During the course of representation, defendant accused his trial counsel of having advised him to abscond to Mexico. On appeal from the order granting defendant's Rule 35(c) motion, the prosecution argued (1) there was no actual conflict of interest that adversely affected trial counsel's performance; (2) trial counsel investigated the allegation giving rise to the conflict of interest, determined it to be groundless, and proceeded in good faith; (3) there was only a potential conflict of interest; and (4) defendant failed to show that it resulted in prejudice to him as required by Strickland. The appellate court disagreed with the prosecution's contention that there was no actual conflict of interest because the record showed that when trial counsel became aware of defendant's allegation, he was very upset and that both trial counsel and his partner recognized the significant impact of the allegation. Moreover, trial counsel's actual conflict of interest adversely affected his representation of defendant. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting a new trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Clendenin


Court of Appeals No. 08CA0624


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SIX


232 P.3d 210; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1864



October 29, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied, En banc Clendenin v. People, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 394 (Colo., June 1, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Boulder County District Court No. 06CR1758. Honorable D.D. Mallard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On jury verdicts before the Boulder County District Court, defendant was convicted of cultivation of marijuana; possession with intent to distribute marijuana; possession of marijuana concentrate; possession of marijuana, eight ounces or more; and possession of drug paraphernalia. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police received a tip that defendant's residence had "come and go" traffic. When a detective executed a search warrant, he noticed a strong scent of marijuana. The detective found 44 marijuana plants, cash in defendant's bedroom, and 67 medium-sized zip lock jeweler's bags. Defendant told the detective that she grew four different kinds of marijuana plants because she suffered from headaches. At issue on appeal was whether defendant qualified as a primary care-giver under Colo. Const. art. XVIII, § 14. The appellate court concluded that defendant was required to do more to manage the well-being of a patient who had a debilitating medical condition than merely supply marijuana. The act of supplying marijuana for medical use, by itself, was insufficient to constitute significant management responsibility for a patient's well-being, and consequently was insufficient to constitutionally qualify a person doing so as a primary care-giver. Also, the appellate court rejected defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-18-406(8)(b)(I) (2009) because the phrase "intent to distribute" was a term that a person of ordinary intelligence could understand.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Vagneur v. City of Aspen


Court of Appeals No. 08CA2552


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


232 P.3d 222; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1866



October 29, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari granted, in part, En banc Vagneur v. City of Aspen, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 397 (Colo., June 1, 2010)
Affirmed by Vagneur v. City of Aspen, 2013 Colo. LEXIS 116 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Pitkin County District Court No. 07CV175. Honorable Gail H. Nichols, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioners submitted petitions setting forth alternative proposals for construction of a highway. Appellee protesters challenged the proposals, and an administrative hearing officer determined the initiated ordinances consisted of administrative matters and, therefore, could not be placed on the ballot for appellee City. The Pitkin County District Court, Colorado, affirmed. The petitioners appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the petitioners contended the district court erred when it affirmed the hearing officer's conclusion that their proposed initiatives related to administrative matters and could not be placed on the ballot under the people's initiative power. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the initiatives each would have authorized (but not required) the Colorado Department of Transportation (CDOT), not the City, to construct the entrance to the City using a design different from that developed for the same land over many years by the City's engineers and administrative staff in conjunction with their counterparts from CDOT and the Federal Highway Administration (FHA). Thus, the proposed ordinances were administrative and not legislative in nature.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

425 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Aguilar-Ramos


Court of Appeals No. 08CA1392


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


224 P.3d 402; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1785



October 15, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Aguilar-Ramos v. People, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 102 (Colo., Feb. 8, 2010)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Aguilar-Ramos v. Medina, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 47023 (D. Colo., Apr. 8, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Weld County District Court No. 02CR1418. Honorable Gilbert A. Gutierrez, Judge.
People v. Aguilar-Ramos, 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 1975 (Colo. Ct. App., Oct. 4, 2007)



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner's second degree kidnapping as a class two felony and 24-year sentence was affirmed on direct appeal. The petitioner sought postconviction relief, alleging that his conviction of a class two felony based on a crime of which he was acquitted violated his constitutional rights, and his counsel was ineffective for not raising the issue. The Weld County District Court, Colorado, denied the petitioner relief, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the petitioner contended the enhancement of his kidnapping conviction violated double jeopardy; the jury instruction for the kidnapping charge was constitutionally deficient; and his constitutional right to have a jury determine the facts used to aggravate his sentence was violated. The appellate court disagreed, holding that the plain language of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-302(3)(a) (2009) specifically required only that the person kidnapped be a victim of sexual assault, not that the kidnapper have perpetrated that crime. Contrary to defendant's argument, he was not being punished for the crime of which he was acquitted; rather, he was being punished for the kidnapping, and such punishment was enhanced because the victim of the kidnapping suffered some additional harm during the kidnapping. As the instruction tracked the language of the statute, the jury was properly instructed. Because the rule announced in Blakely and Apprendi only applied when an offender received a sentence outside the presumptive range, and defendant's 24-year sentence was within the presumptive range for the class two felony of which the jury convicted him, Blakely and Apprendi were not implicated.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed, but the case was remanded to the trial court to remove a reference from the mittimus.

People v. Samuels


Court of Appeals No. 06CA1560


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SEVEN


228 P.3d 229; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1789



October 15, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Samuels v. People, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 281 (Colo., Apr. 5, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Arapahoe County District Court No. 05CR926. Honorable Michael Spear, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Arapahoe County District Court, Colorado, which convicted him of one count of first degree murder (extreme indifference), two counts of attempted first degree murder (extreme indifference), one count of conspiracy to commit first degree murder, one count of possession of a weapon by a previous offender, and two crime of violence counts.


OVERVIEW: The instant court concluded that a search, of some scope, of defendant's bedroom by his probation officer did not violate the Fourth Amendment. The probation officer's reasonable suspicion that defendant had violated conditions of his probation was sufficient to justify the search. Defendant's attorney's previous representation of a prosecution witness did not create a conflict of interest with defendant. Defendant's attorney did not obtain any confidential information from the witness that was relevant to the defense. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's challenge for cause of a prospective juror. The trial court did not deprive defendant of his right to a fair and impartial jury by limiting his counsel's voir dire to 60 minutes. The trial court also did not abuse its discretion in allowing the prosecution to refer to defendant by his nickname, as the nickname was relevant to the issue of identification. The trial court also did not abuse its discretion in admitting testimony that defendant possessed a gun or in allowing a witness to testify that defendant threatened to kill his codefendant if the codefendant talked to the police about the murder.

Mahaney v. City of Englewood


Court of Appeals No. 08CA1505


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


226 P.3d 1214; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1737



October 1, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended January 21, 2010.
Modified and rehearing denied by Mahaney v. City of Englewood, 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 75 (Colo. Ct. App., Jan. 21, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Arapahoe County District Court No. 07CV1373. Honorable Cheryl L. Post, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff shop owner brought an action for declaratory and injunctive relief against defendant city, alleging that the city's municipal code violated U.S. Const. amend. I, and Colo. Const. art. II, § 10. The Arapahoe County District Court, Colorado, granted summary judgment for the city. The shop owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: In an effort to prevent graffiti, the shop owner hired artists to paint a mural on the building's north and south exterior walls. The city alleged that the murals violated Englewood, Colo., Municipal Code § 16-6-13. The appellate court focused its analysis on the constitutionality of the city's special review procedure, under a strict scrutiny standard of review. The appellate court concluded the special review procedure did not provide adequate procedural safeguards. The murals were signs as that term was defined by the sign code, Englewood, Colo., Municipal Code § 16-11-2, and thus constituted speech protected under U.S. Const. amend. I. The appellate court noted that no part of the sign code or the special review policy provided a specific period within which the city manager or designee was required to determine whether to approve a permit after receiving the sign committee's recommendation. The essential procedural safeguard was a constitutionally impermissible prior restraint on protected free speech. Attorney's fees were not available under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 because the shop owner did not bring a cause of action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OUTCOME: The trial court's summary judgment for the city was reversed, and the case was remanded with instructions that the trial court enter summary judgment for the shop owner.

People v. O'Neal


Court of Appeals No. 07CA1895


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


228 P.3d 211; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1740



October 1, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied O'Neal v. People, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 309 (Colo., Apr. 12, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
El Paso County District Court No. 06CR4625. Honorable Kirk S. Samelson, Judge. Honorable David D. Parrish, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, before the El Paso County District Court, Colorado, following jury verdict finding him guilty of possession of a weapon by a previous offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police encountered defendant and two others sitting in a car in the parking lot of a store. The police noticed a pistol sitting on the floor of the inside of the car. Defendant had previously been adjudicated a juvenile delinquent. At trial, it was uncontested that the pistol was inoperable. The trial court rejected defendant's proffered instructions that centered on intent. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial court erroneously interpreted the law when it ruled his intent was irrelevant to the determination of whether the inoperable pistol was a firearm. It was not necessary for the prosecution to prove anyone in particular intended the pistol be capable of discharging bullets or the like. Under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1-901(3)(h) the pistol was "per se" a firearm. The appellate court also rejected defendant's contention that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1-901(3)(h) was unconstitutionally vague or violative of due process. Finally, because the statute did not require a showing of anyone's intent when the claimed firearm was a pistol, the appellate court reject defendant's sufficiency of the evidence challenge.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

People v. Tillery

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Arapahoe County District Court No. 05CR667. Honorable Timothy L. Fasing, Judge. Honorable Angela R. Arkin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, SENTENCE VACATED, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, before the Arapahoe County District Court, Colorado, of sexual assault on a child (SAOC) as part of a pattern; sexual assault on a child-position of trust (POT); SAOC with a second victim; and contributing to the delinquency of a minor. Defendant appealed the convictions and sentences.


OVERVIEW: Evidence was introduced that defendant had sexually assaulted his 12-year-old stepdaughter over a seven month period while she was living with him. The victim also testified that defendant had sexually assaulted her while they were living elsewhere. The appellate court concluded that the earlier incident was properly admitted because the incident occurred within 10 years prior to the predicate offenses charged under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-405(1). Defendant next contended that testimony of a forensic interviewer constituted expert testimony that did not comply with Colo. R. Evid. 702. Nevertheless, the witness's statements did not express an opinion on the victim's truthfulness or sincerity. Defendant argued that he lacked notice of another incident that allegedly took place in an apartment; however, the appellate court did not discern a clear abuse of discretion. The reference to the incident was brief and promptly suppressed by the trial court. With respect to defendant's sentence, defendant's sentences exceeded what was authorized by law. Further, the trial court could not apply Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1.3-401(10) to increase the presumptive range in calculating the sentence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The sentence was vacated. The case was remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

People v. Villa


Court of Appeals No. 06CA1857


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


240 P.3d 343; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1733



October 1, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Villa v. People, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 653 (Colo., Aug. 30, 2010)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by, As moot Villa v. Dep't Corr. Co. D.O.C., 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 152144 (D. Colo., Oct. 23, 2012)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by Villa v. Colorado, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 29098 (D. Colo., Mar. 10, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 05CR400. Honorable Gaspar F. Perricone, Judge. Honorable Christina M. Habas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, SENTENCE VACATED, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted before City and County of Denver District Court, Colorado, entered on a jury verdict finding him guilty of sexual assault on a child. Defendant appealed the conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: The victim told her great-grandmother and others that defendant had touched her vaginal and anal areas. A witness testified that defendant had also allegedly anally raped the witness. The prosecution filed a pretrial notice of its intent to introduce other act evidence, under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-10-301 and Colo. R. Evid. 404(b). The appellate court rejected the contention that the witness's allegations were not logically relevant to the issue of the intent. The evidence of the prior acts satisfied a Spoto analysis. The trial court did not err in admitting evidence of defendant's prior sexual assaults on the witness. The trial court also did not err in excluding evidence under Colorado's rape shield statute, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-407 (2009). The appellate court found defendant's due process right of confrontation arguments were unavailing. Further, the rape shield statute also did not deny the equal protection of the law because § 18-3-407 was a rational attempt by the legislature to protect a complainant. As to the sentence, the appellate court agreed with defendant's contention that the 15-year lower limit of his indeterminate sentence exceeded the maximum authorized by law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Defendant's sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

Sinclair Transp. Co. v. Sandberg


Court of Appeals No. 08CA1249


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SIX


228 P.3d 198; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1671; 175 Oil & Gas Rep. 887



September 17, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Sinclair Transp. Co. v. Sandberg, 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1809 (Colo. Ct. App., Oct. 22, 2009)
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part Larson v. Sinclair Transp. Co., 2010 Colo. LEXIS 308 (Colo., Apr. 12, 2010)
Writ of certiorari granted Larson v. Sinclair Transp. Co., 2010 Colo. LEXIS 934 (Colo., Dec. 6, 2010)
Reversed by, Remanded by Larson v. Sinclair Transp. Co., 2012 Colo. LEXIS 349 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Weld County District Court Nos. 07CV290 & 07CV292. Honorable Daniel S. Maus, Judge, Honorable Paul McLimans, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AND JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporation initiated condemnation proceedings. At the immediate possession hearing, the Weld County District Court, Colorado, found that the corporation proved by a preponderance of the evidence that it was entitled to immediate possession. Respondent landowners appealed the trial court's order granting immediate possession of the landowners' properties and its judgment determining the properties' values.


OVERVIEW: The corporation requested landowners to amend an easement over their properties to allow the corporation to install within the easement a pipeline adjacent to a previously installed pipeline. After negotiations, the corporation and landowners failed to reach an agreement. The landowners contended that the trial court erred by finding that the corporation had legal authority to condemn the properties because the corporation did not qualify as an entity granted the power of eminent domain under either Colo. Rev. Stat. § 38-4-102 (2009) or Colo. Rev. Stat. § 38-5-105 (2009). The corporation was a foreign corporation that operated and maintained the pipeline on landowners' properties; it conveyed petroleum products through its pipelines; and it would be responsible for the construction, cost, operation, and maintenance of the pipeline. The corporation was a pipeline company for the purposes of § 38-5-105. The appellate court did not construe Colo. Rev. Stat. § 7-43-102 to define a pipeline company. Further, the trial court properly found that the pipeline would serve a public purpose. Finally, the landowners' properties were not unconstitutionally taken without just compensation.


OUTCOME: The order and the judgment were affirmed.

Eller v. Indus. Claim Appeals Office of Colo.


Court of Appeals No. 08CA2274


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


224 P.3d 397; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1570



September 3, 2009, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 4-694-053.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado upheld the denial and dismissal of appellant employee's workers' compensation claim. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee argued that, because appellee employer did not initiate the division-sponsored independent medical examination (DIME) process to challenge the authorized treating physician's (ATP) findings as to maximum medical improvement (MMI) and permanent impairment, the ATP's opinion that the employee sustained a work injury was binding and the administrative law judge (ALJ) was divested of jurisdiction to consider the issues of causation and compensability. The appellate court found that the employer did not challenge either the MMI determination or the impairment rating. Contrary to the employee's position, the applicable statutory scheme granted no authority to the ATP to determine causation as it pertained to compensability. Because compensability remained a factual question for determination by the ALJ without application of an enhanced burden of proof, the employee's inability to procure a DIME posed no disadvantage to her. Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-42-107.2(2)(b) (2008) was not vague and the employee did not show a due process violation. Any errors in the ALJ's evidentiary rulings were harmless.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Munoz


Court of Appeals No. 07CA0697


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Munoz, 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1798 (Colo. Ct. App., Oct. 15, 2009)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
El Paso County District Court No. 06CR648. Honorable Jann P. DuBois, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the El Paso County District Court (Colorado) that convicted him of first-degree murder after deliberation and felony murder under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-102(1)(a) and (b) (2008), two counts of first-degree burglary under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-4-202(1) (2008), three counts of menacing under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-206(1)(a), and two crimes of violence counts under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1.3-406(2)(a)(I)(B) (2008).


OVERVIEW: Defendant went to the victim's home to speak with a mutual friend who was staying there. The victim refused to allow defendant to speak with the friend, and a fight ensued. As defendant departed, he threatened to return and made a threat to the friend that she interpreted to mean that defendant planned to destroy belongings that she stored in a storage unit rented to defendant's wife. Evid. 403 and 404 because the evidence showed defendant's motive and plan to carry out the threats made after fighting with the victim on the previous day. Further, the reasonable doubt jury instruction was not improper for containing the word "should," as the instruction clearly informed the jury of its obligation to acquit defendant if the prosecution did not prove every element of each offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Vitetta v. Corrigan


Court of Appeals No. 07CA0687


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SEVEN


240 P.3d 322; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1477



August 20, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion Modified and Petition for Rehearing Denied August 20, 2009
Modified and rehearing denied by Vitetta v. Corrigan, 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1803 (Colo. Ct. App., Oct. 15, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
El Paso County District Court No. 04CV2023. Honorable Larry E. Schwartz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The El Paso County District Court, Colorado, granted judgment in favor of appellee parents, who obtained a multi-million dollar negligence verdict against appellants, doctor and medical group, for post-natal injuries to their minor daughter. The doctor and medical group appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that the parents could rely on the amended statute, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-64-205(1)(f) (2008). The amended statute was intended to apply as it directed that the new provisions applied to civil actions pending on or after the effective date of August 3, 2007. The amended statute was remedial in that it extended to incapacitated plaintiffs the ability to obtain a form of damages. They did not eliminate any substantive right formerly vested in appellants. Appellants' special argument did not raise a reasonableness challenge nor would any such challenge have merit. The amended statute was not unconstitutional special legislation, Colo. Const. art. V, § 25, because, by covering all minor and incapacitated persons who received large medical malpractice verdicts, it had general future applicability. The trial court's consideration of lack of prior earnings as one factor in evaluating good cause/unfairness did not deny equal protection to the child. The trial court properly allowed appellee insurer to recover its prior payments on behalf of the parents from appellants. The insurer's subrogation rights were not limited.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed as to the claim for a lump-sum payment, and the case was remanded for entry of a lump-sum judgment in favor of the parents; the judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

People ex rel. J.R.


Court of Appeals No. 08CA1709


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


216 P.3d 1220; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1383



August 6, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 2, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Adams County District Court No. 07JD673. Honorable Harlan R. Bockman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, SENTENCE VACATED, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a juvenile, challenged the judgment of delinquency of the Adams County District Court, Colorado, entered on the trial court's finding that he committed acts which, if committed by an adult, would have constituted the offense of sexual assault. under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-402(1)(b), (1)(h). The juvenile also appealed the court's refusal to apply presentence confinement credit against his sentence.


OVERVIEW: It was undisputed that the victim (a female student who attended the same school as the juvenile) became extremely intoxicated while at a party with the juvenile. The trial court found that the juvenile accompanied the victim to a private room where he had sexual intercourse with her even though he knew that she was too intoxicated to appraise the nature of her conduct, or to consent. In addition, the court relied on the testimony of a nurse who examined the victim soon after the assault and observed vaginal tearing and bruising consistent with recent intercourse. Based on these and other findings, the court concluded that the prosecution had proved, beyond a reasonable doubt, that the juvenile violated Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-402(1)(b), (1)(h). Next, the trial court did not conduct a sentencing hearing until eighty-eight days after the expiration of the forty-five-day mandatory deadline. The appellate court concluded that, because the juvenile had a statutory right to be sentenced within forty-five days of adjudication pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 19-2-804(3), 19-2-906(3)(a), he was entitled to eighty-eight days of presentence confinement credit.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment of conviction, vacated the sentence, and remanded for resentencing.

 

436 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lara


Court of Appeals No. 05CA2281


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


224 P.3d 388; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1379



August 6, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Lara, 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1701 (Colo. Ct. App., Sept. 24, 2009)
Writ of certiorari denied People v. Lara, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 82 (Colo., Feb. 8, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Weld County District Court No. 04CR1594. Honorable Roger A. Klein, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Weld County District Court (Colorado) that convicted him of first-degree murder under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-102(1)(d) (2008) for the killing of a rival gang member in a drive-by shooting, arguing that the district court erred in instructing the jury that the prosecution did not have the burden of disproving that he acted in self-defense or in defense of another.


OVERVIEW: Defendant met the murder charge against him by claiming that he acted to protect himself and his companions. At trial, the district court rejected defendant's proposed instructions and gave an instruction that tracked the language of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1-704(4) (2008). The jury convicted defendant of first-degree extreme indifference murder. On review, the court concluded that the trial court committed reversible error in instructing the jury that the prosecution did not have the burden of disproving self-defense or the defense of others. The element of malice was negated by conduct that constituted self-defense or the defense of others under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1-704 if defendant reasonably believed that he or another was about to suffer unlawful physical force and responded with the appropriate force; if defendant was acting in self-defense or defense of another, then he was not acting under circumstances that evidenced an attitude of universal malice manifesting extreme indifferent to human life. Thus, to prove the elements of extreme indifference murder, the prosecution was required to disprove that defendant acted in reasonable defense of a person.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

People v. Mantos


Court of Appeals No. 07CA2107


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


250 P.3d 586; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1382



August 6, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Mantos, 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1875 (Colo. Ct. App., Oct. 29, 2009)
Writ of certiorari denied People v. Mantos, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 682 (Colo., Sept. 13, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
El Paso County District Court No. 06CR1416. Honorable David A. Gilbert, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT VACATED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the El Paso County District Court (Colorado) that convicted him of sexual exploitation of a child under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6-403(3)(b) (2008), arguing that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that downloading and saving sexually exploitative material in a share-capable computer file did not constitute the felony offense of sexual exploitation of a child as defined in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6-403(3)(b) (2008). The trial court erred in allowing the case to go to the jury on the theory that defendant "arranged for" the pornographic images to be distributed and erroneously construed the term "arranged for" as encompassing either arranging for the distribution of material or arranging to obtain material; because the Colorado General Assembly did not proscribe arranging for obtaining or distributing pornographic material in the plain language of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6-403(3)(b), such conduct was not proscribed by the prohibition against arranging for sexually exploitative material. Because the State failed to establish that defendant published, promoted, sold, financed, offered, exhibited, advertised, dealt in, or distributed child pornography, the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction for the sexual exploitation of a child.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was vacated, and the case was remanded to the district court for entry of a judgment of acquittal.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Adams County District Court, Colorado, convicting him for first degree criminal trespass and harassment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with burglary, criminal trespass, assault, and harassment. He claimed that he was under the influence of prescription medications when the offenses occurred. People v. Lucas


Court of Appeals No. 05CA1621


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


232 P.3d 155; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1185



June 25, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified and rehearing denied by People v. Lucas, 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1427 (Colo. Ct. App., Aug. 6, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Douglas County District Court No. 03CR194. Honorable Paul A. King, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Douglas County District Court (Colorado), which convicted him of first-degree burglary in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-4-202(1) (2008), third-degree assault, menacing, second-degree criminal tampering in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-4-506 (2008), and first-degree criminal trespass.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for first-degree burglary, third-degree assault, menacing, second-degree criminal tampering, and first-degree criminal trespass, but the appellate court affirmed. The Miranda warnings delivered to defendant at the start of his second station-house interview were effective in accomplishing their object. The second interview was not a continuation of the first and defendant's choice not to assert his right to remain silent was not a product of ineffective Miranda warnings. Additionally, the jury instructions did not imply that the prosecution had been relieved of any burden to prove defendant's mental state. There was no double jeopardy violation under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1-408(1)(a) (2008). Neither criminal tampering nor menacing was a lesser-included offense and neither therefore merged with the burglary conviction. Element number five did not require the prosecution to prove all of the elements of either criminal tampering or menacing in order to prove that defendant committed burglary. Rather, the prosecution needed only to prove that defendant intended to commit tampering or menacing when he entered the victim's home.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Vondra v. Colo. Dep't of Corr.


Court of Appeals No. 08CA0912


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


226 P.3d 1165; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1039



June 11, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Vondra v. Colo. Dep't of Corr., 2010 Colo. LEXIS 206 (Colo., Mar. 15, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
El Paso County District Court No. 07CV183. Honorable Kirk S. Samelson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an inmate in the custody of appellee, the Colorado Department of Corrections (DOC), appealed an order of the El Paso County District Court (Colorado) that dismissed his complaint challenging the DOC's classification of him as a sex offender under former Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-22-103(2)(d), arguing that the DOC abused its discretion when it classified him as a sex offender because he had not been convicted of a sex offense.


OVERVIEW: A DOC hearing panel classified the inmate as a sex offender, basing its determination on the inmate's alleged sexual assault of his ex-girlfriend. The inmate filed a complaint under Colo. R. Civ. P. 106(a)(4) seeking judicial review of the DOC's classification. On review of the district court's order of dismissal, the court held that the DOC properly classified the inmate as a sex offender because there was evidence in the record establishing that he sexually assaulted his ex-girlfriend. The victim's statements and police reports enabled the hearing panel to conclude that the inmate behaved in a sexually violent and abusive manner by subjecting an adult female victim to unwanted sexual contact through threats, intimidation, and physical force; therefore, the competent evidence in the record supported the classification of the inmate as a sex offender. The fact that the prosecution did not believe that it could prove a sexual assault charge beyond a reasonable doubt did not preclude the hearing panel from determining that the same evidence established, by a preponderance of the evidence, each of the prerequisites for classification as a sex offender within the DOC.


OUTCOME: The district court's order of dismissal was affirmed.
