Blood v. Qwest Servs. Corp.


Court of Appeals No. 08CA0134


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


224 P.3d 301; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 716



April 30, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended May 29, 2009.
Modified and rehearing denied by Blood v. Qwest Servs. Corp., 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 937 (Colo. Ct. App., May 28, 2009)
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part Qwest Servs. Corp. v. Blood, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 155 (Colo., Feb. 22, 2010)
Affirmed by Qwest Servs. Corp. v. Blood, 2011 Colo. LEXIS 428 (Colo., May 23, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 05CV6972. Honorable Sheila A. Rappaport, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a personal injury action involving a joint use utility pole, defendant telephone company appealed the judgment of the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) that entered judgment on a jury verdict in favor of plaintiffs, a lineman and his wife, and third-party defendant electric company, and denied the telephone company's post-trial motions.


OVERVIEW: The telephone company argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by increasing the exemplary damages award without granting it a hearing. The court of appeals agreed. Without a hearing concerning conduct during the pendency of the case, the trial court could not have determined whether "willful and wanton manner" under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-21-102 had been proven beyond a reasonable doubt. The telephone company did not have an opportunity to develop a complete record during trial on the reasons for its failure to implement a periodic pole inspection program. The lack of a hearing severely limited review of the order increasing exemplary damages. It was not known what additional evidence might have been offered concerning factors relevant to the due process implications of the ratio of any increased exemplary damages to compensatory damages, which were high. The telephone company had a substantial interest in any increase to exemplary damages because a post-trial hearing was its only opportunity to further develop a record for de novo review of an increased award. Therefore, the trial court abused its discretion in not granting the telephone company a hearing.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order increasing exemplary damages was vacated and the case was remanded for an evidentiary hearing on the lineman's motion to increase exemplary damages. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

Turney v. Civil Serv. Comm'n


Court of Appeals No. 08CA0215


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


222 P.3d 343; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 574



April 16, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Turney v. Civ. Serv. Comm'n, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 21 (Colo., Jan. 11, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 07CV4025. Honorable Sheila A. Rappaport, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer was suspended for 10 months for tactical errors preceding his fatal shooting of a developmentally disabled 15-year-old boy who had been wielding a knife. Appellee Civil Service Commission, reversing an administrative hearing officer, upheld the suspension. The officer sought judicial review, and City and County of Denver District Court, Colorado, affirmed the Commission. The officer appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the officer contended the Commission exceeded its jurisdiction or abused its discretion in upholding his suspension and argued that the "highest standard of efficiency and safety" provision in the police department's operations manual was unconstitutionally vague. The appellate court disagreed, finding that a provision requiring officers to use the "highest standard of efficiency and safety" survived a vagueness challenge as this standard could have been applied to evaluate the reasonableness of officers' actions in light of their training; the standard was an objective one providing fair notice, and judicial review was available to ensure it was applied fairly. Contrary to the officer's contention, review was authorized under Denver, Colo., Municipal Code § 9.4.15(F) as the hearing officer's decision reasonably could have been determined to have rested on an erroneous interpretation of departmental or civil service rules and policy considerations that may have had effect beyond the case at hand. The department was not legally precluded from using its operations manual to review the propriety of its officers' tactical decisions preceding an actual use of force.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

OVERVIEW: Claimant sustained an admitted injury to her bilateral upper extremities and suffered from bilateral carpal tunnel syndrome. Jefferson County District Court No. 01CR458. Honorable Jack W. Berryhill, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART; SENTENCE VACATED IN PART; ORDER AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART; AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Jefferson County District Court (Colorado) convicting him of one count of securities fraud in the course of business, in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 11-51-501(1)(c) (2008), and one count of computer crime, in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-5.5-102(1). The People cross-appealed certain aspects of a restitution order.


OVERVIEW: Defendant worked as a salesperson, seeking investors for children's television programming. He sold units, which the jury found to be securities. There was evidence that defendant knew that cease and desist orders prohibited the sale of units in various other states and that defendant was culpable for misrepresentations in the brochure. The trial court denied defendant's motions for judgment of acquittal and for a new trial. Stat. § 18-1.3-205 (2008), and by ruling that co-defendants were not jointly and severally liable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for securities fraud, reversed his conviction for computer fraud, vacated defendant's sentence for computer fraud, and otherwise affirmed. The restitution order was affirmed, as modified to not require the Attorney General to distribute the restitution monies among the victims.

Simpson v. Indus. Claim Appeals Office of Colo.


Court of Appeals No. 07CA1581


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


219 P.3d 354; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 576



April 16, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 2, 2009.
Modified and rehearing denied by Simpson v. Indus. Claim Appeals Office, 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 1229 (Colo. Ct. App., June 25, 2009)
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part Benchmark/Elite, Inc. v. Simpson, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 1046 (Colo., Nov. 9, 2009)
Reversed by, in part, Vacated by, in part, Remanded by Benchmark/Elite, Inc. v. Simpson, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 387 (Colo., June 1, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 4-467-097.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED IN PART, SET ASIDE IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In this workers' compensation proceeding, petitioner claimant sought review of the final order of respondent Industrial Claim Appeals Office (Panel), affirming the order of the administrative law judge (ALJ), finding that respondent employer and respondent insurer had overpaid benefits to the claimant and were entitled to credit for the overpayment.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was injured in an admitted, work-related accident. The employer and its insurer paid temporary total disability (TTD) benefits and, later, benefits for permanent partial disability (PPD). The employer also admitted liability for permanent total disability (PTD) benefits. The employer discovered that it had overpaid the claimant. The claimant asserted that recovery of an overpayment arising from an employer's error was barred by caselaw. Nevertheless, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-43-303(1) & (2)(a) permitted reopening of an award because of overpayment. Further, the meaning of the statutory definition of "overpayment" in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-40-201(15.5) was clear and unambiguous. The claimant argued that the ALJ failed to account for the employer's deduction of the lump sum award from the total overpayment calculated; however, the ALJ had discretion to fashion a remedy. The ALJ's calculations made clear that the amount of overpayment was determined by adding the excess benefits actually paid to claimant. The claimant was entitled to have his benefits for PTD capped at 91 percent of the state average weekly wage that was in effect at the time of his disablement.


OUTCOME: The order was set aside as to the amount of PTD benefits claimant was entitled to receive, and the case was remanded to the ALJ for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

Dolores Huerta Preparatory High v. Colo. State Bd. of Educ.


Court of Appeals No. 08CA0664


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


215 P.3d 1229; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 578



April 2, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 2, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 07CV3538. Honorable Catherine A. Lemon, Judge.
Dolores Huerta Preparatory High v. Colo. State Bd. of Educ., 2008 Colo. LEXIS 677 (Colo., June 23, 2008)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a dispute over the terms of a charter school contract, plaintiffs, a charter school and parents, appealed the judgment of the City and County of Denver District Court, Colorado, dismissing their complaint for declaratory relief, certiorari, and mandamus, against defendants, the Colorado State Board of Education and a school district.


OVERVIEW: The school district and the charter school entered into a charter school contract that contemplated funding for a long-term facility based on sharing proceeds of future mill levies or bond issues. To obtain specific long-term facility funding, the charter school initiated non-binding third-party arbitration under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 22-30.5-107.5 (2008). An arbitrator agreed with the charter school that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 22-30.5-105(2)(c)(II) (2008) required a charter school contract to include funding, and ordered the school district to provide funding. The appellate court concluded that the charter school was subject to the political subdivision doctrine; therefore, the charter school lacked standing. Moreover, § 22-30.5-107.5 precluded judicial review of the decision because the charter school's dissatisfaction with the contract arose out of implementation of the statutorily required portions and was reserved for resolution by the State Board. Further, the parents rights were not violated under the Colorado Constitution because the parents did not cite to any case interpreting the phrase "thorough and uniform" to require that a school district equitably allocate expenditures.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Kuhndog, Inc. v. Indus. Claim Appeals Office


Court of Appeals No. 08CA1926


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


207 P.3d 949; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 398



March 19, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 3, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 20-0719436.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a workers' compensation proceeding, petitioner employer sought review of a final order issued by the respondent Industrial Claim Appeals Office (Panel) upholding the fine imposed for the employer's failure to carry workers' compensation insurance.


OVERVIEW: The employer received a notice to show compliance stating that division records indicated the employer's business did not have workers' compensation insurance. The notice required employer to complete a compliance questionnaire within 20 days and to provide an explanation and proof that it either had insurance or was exempt from the Workers' Compensation Act. The employer failed to respond and the director issued an order finding it in default and imposing a fine. On appeal, the employer appears to argue that service of the notice to show compliance by mail was insufficient. Nevertheless, the record indicated and the employer did not contest that it received actual notice. The service was not constitutionally deficient. The employer next contended that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-43-409 violated due process because it did not mandate that an evidentiary hearing occur prior to the issuance of a default order. The appellate court concluded that it was reasonable to condition the occurrence of an administrative hearing on an employer's timely request to participate in a prehearing conference. Here, the employer failed to request a prehearing conference in a timely manner.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

People v. Chavarria-Sanchez


Court of Appeals No. 08CA0241


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


207 P.3d 902; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 334



March 5, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 3, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Adams County District Court No. 06CR3854. Honorable C. Vincent Phelps, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee State brought a forfeiture proceeding before the Adams County District Court, Colorado. Appellant surety appealed the district court's judgment forfeiting a $ 20,000 bond posted for a defendant.


OVERVIEW: The surety posted an appearance bond promising to pay $20,000 to the State if defendant, who was charged with felonies, failed to appear. When defendant failed to appear, the district court ordered the bond forfeited. The surety moved to limit bond liability to the amount of fees collected from defendant. Defendant was a Mexican national who had been in this country illegally, and who had been deported to Mexico prior to the arraignment at which he failed to appear. The surety argued the bond forfeiture judgment violated Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-3-503(1)(c). The legislative history of this statute confirmed the appellate court's reading of subsection (1)(c) as intended to limit professional bonding agents' liability to the actual fees collected. The appellate court also concluded that the new provisions of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-3-503 did not apply to this case. Applying subsection (1)(c) would change the consequences for two contracting parties -- the surety and the State -- after defendant had failed to appear for a required court proceeding. In sum, the surety was not entitled to relief because § 16-3-503(1)(c) did not apply retroactively.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

449 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. Brannon


Court of Appeals No. 08CA0581


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SIX


207 P.3d 923; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 328



March 5, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 3, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Larimer County District Court No. 06CV584. Honorable Stephen J. Schapanski, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured party challenged a decision from the Larimer County District Court, Colorado, which found that appellee driver was negligent, but awarded the injured party no damages.


OVERVIEW: Six days after the effective date of the repeal of the Colorado Auto Accident Reparations Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 10-4-701 to -725, the parties were involved in a collision. The injured party was a named insured on a policy that had been renewed prior to the repeal of the Act. The policy provided a basic level of personal injury protection (PIP) benefits that included wage-loss reimbursements and payment of medical expenses. In a subsequent negligent trial, no damages were awarded. This appeal followed. In partially reversing, the appellate court held that the district court did not err by prohibiting the injured party from presenting evidence of past medical expenses or in denying her request for a continuance to seek additional medical treatment and recovery of damages therefor. However, the district court erred by applying the repealed Act and instructing the jury to subtract from the injured party's lost earnings wage reimbursements that she received from her own PIP insurance. The repeal of former Colo. Rev. Stat. § 10-4-713(1) was presumed to be prospective in nature, and the driver had no vested right to assert § 10-4-713(1). Finally, a collateral source exception applied.


OUTCOME: The portion of the judgment relating to lost earnings was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial on that claim. The rest of the judgment was affirmed.

 

450 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Boulder Valley Sch. Dist. Re-2 v. Colo. State Bd. of Educ.


Court of Appeals No. 07CA1599


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


217 P.3d 918; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 223



February 19, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 30, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 05CV196. Honorable Joseph E. Meyer, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a school district, its board, and two individuals, sued defendant State, challenging the constitutionality of Part 5 of the Colorado Charter Schools Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 22-30.5-501 to 22-30.5-516 (2008). The District Court of the City and County of Denver, Colorado, granted the State's motion for summary judgment. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court found Part 5 to be constitutional. Although plaintiffs argued that Part 5 is unconstitutional because Colo. Const. art. IX, §§ 1, 2, and 15, collectively prohibit the legislature from establishing schools that are not part of the local school district system, the court disagreed with this argument. The general arrangements of Part 5 maintain a balance between the competing interests of local school districts and the State. Colo. Const. art. IX, § 2, does not prohibit the State from establishing institute charter schools that are not controlled by school districts. The creation of institute charter schools, which are funded exclusively from state-controlled funds, does not exceed the State Board of Education's general supervisory powers under Colo. Const. art. IX, §§ 1 and 2, or infringe on a school district's right of local control under Colo. Const. art. IX, § 15. Regarding plaintiffs' claim that Part 5 violates the right to local self-government under Colo. Const. art. V, § 35, the court disagreed with plaintiffs' argument that the functioning of the public schools primarily affects only those within the geographic boundaries of a school district.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Woodrow v. Wildlife Comm'n, Dep't of Natural Res.


Court of Appeals No. 08CA0753


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


206 P.3d 835; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 220



February 19, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 3, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 06CV2963. Honorable Martin F. Egelhoff, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, licensees, challenged the order of the City and County of Denver District Court, Colorado, affirming the decision of defendant Colorado Wildlife Commission, suspending their hunting and fishing license privileges for one year.


OVERVIEW: During hunting season, the licensees drove across private property adjacent to public lands open for hunting, while in possession of hunting firearms and licenses, and dressed in hunter safety orange. The licensees were charged with hunting on private property without permission in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 33-6-116 (2008). Ultimately, each licensee pled guilty to a reduced charge of criminal trespass and the original charges were dismissed. The licensees argued that since their license suspensions were based on the same facts as the criminal charges against them, the suspensions were barred by Double Jeopardy. The appellate court ruled that the license suspensions did not constitute multiple punishments in violation of the Double Jeopardy Clause. The primary goal for the civil sanction was not the imposition of punishment, but the remedial purpose of protecting the public's interest in the State's wildlife. Also, a person of ordinary intelligence would know that if his criminal conviction had a close and logical connection to his hunting or fishing activity, such conduct fell within the ambit of potential license suspension under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 33-6-106.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

People v. Stevenson


Court of Appeals No. 06CA1612


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


228 P.3d 161; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 213



February 19, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Stevenson, 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 2012 (Colo. Ct. App., Mar. 19, 2009)
Writ of certiorari denied Stevenson v. People, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 273 (Colo., Apr. 5, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Mesa County District Court No. 04CR5. Honorable Thomas M. Deister, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Mesa County District Court, Colorado, convicting and sentencing him to twenty-four years for first degree burglary and aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and codefendant broke into the victim's apartment. The People granted defendant use-and-derivative-use immunity to compel his testimony at a codefendant's trial. By granting defendant use immunity before his own prosecution, the People bore the burden of proving that the trial evidence derived from sources wholly independent of the immunized testimony. In this case, the trial court's ruling was made without a transcript of defendant's immunized testimony. Without knowing the particulars of the immunized testimony, the Court of Appeals of Colorado held that the trial court could not have made the required finding that the People's evidence derived entirely from sources other than the immunized testimony. Because defendant consented to a trial outside the normal six-month time limits, his speedy trial claim failed. Where the prosecution conceded two discovery violations, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by dismissing two counts instead of granting a mistrial as a sanction. The prosecutor's rebuttal closing argument attacking the credibility of defendant's post-arrest denials was not plain error.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the trial court for hearings and findings on defendant's immunity claim.

Snook v. Joyce Homes, Inc.


Court of Appeals No. 07CA2352


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


215 P.3d 1210; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 85



February 5, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 2, 2009.
Writ of certiorari denied Snook v. Joyce Homes, Inc., 2009 Colo. LEXIS 812 (Colo., Sept. 14, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Douglas County District Court No. 05CV1554. Honorable Nancy A. Hopf, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff worker brought a negligence action against defendant home builder. The Douglas County District Court, Colorado, held that the home builder was the worker's statutory employer. The district court also concluded that the worker's claims were limited to $ 15,000, and dismissed his claims with prejudice. The worker appealed.


OVERVIEW: The worker was a sole proprietor and an independent contractor who did trim work on a home under a contract between the worker and a subcontractor, which had agreed to do the work for the home builder. The worker alleged that the scaffolding had been negligently constructed, causing it to fall. At issue was whether damages were capped at $ 15,000 by operation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-41-401(3). On appeal, the worker challenged the constitutionality of the statute. The appellate court did not agree that the statute was special interest legislation. Further, the statute did not violate the equal protection guarantee because the classification was reasonable and rationally related to a legitimate government purpose. The appellate court also rejected the worker's argument that amount of the statutory cap was unreasonably low, arbitrary, and not rationally related to the purpose of encouraging participation in the worker's compensation system. The appellate court concluded that the trial court properly determined under the undisputed evidence in the record that the home builder was the worker's statutory employer within the meaning of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-41-401(1)(a).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Oram


Court of Appeals No. 07CA0023


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


217 P.3d 883; 2009 Colo. App. LEXIS 82



February 5, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part Oram v. People, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 946 (Colo., Oct. 13, 2009)
Affirmed by Oram v. People, 2011 Colo. LEXIS 414 (Colo., May 16, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 04CR4538. Honorable Morris B. Hoffman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) convicting him of second-degree burglary under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-4-203(1) (2008) and felony menacing under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-206(a)(1) (2008).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a bounty hunter, was convicted for entering the victims' home in an attempt to locate a man who was out on bond but had failed to appear in court. On appeal, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's burglary conviction. The evidence showed that defendant unlawfully entered the victims' home because, even though the common law bonding agent's privilege permitted a bond recovery agent to enter a principal's house to seize the principal, it was not necessary for defendant to enter because whether the man lived at the home was a disputed question, as defendant did not see the man at the home during the one hour of surveillance and he did not make any other efforts to locate him. A reasonable juror could conclude that defendant knew that his entry was unnecessary to seize the man because he did so after little investigation, when the man was not there, and using a ruse. There was also sufficient evidence that defendant committed the crime of menacing while in the home because two victims testified that they believed defendant pointed a gun at one victim after entering the home.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

Bruce v. City of Colo. Springs


Court of Appeals No. 08CA0239


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SEVEN


200 P.3d 1140; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 2176



December 24, 2008, Decided 
February, 27, 2009, Released for Publication


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Bruce v. City of Colo. Springs, 2010 Colo. App. LEXIS 822 (Colo. Ct. App., June 10, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
El Paso County District Court No. 07CV244. Honorable David A. Gilbert, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a proponent of a proposed ballot initiative, appealed from an order of the El Paso County District Court (Colorado) that denied his request for relief against defendants, a city, its initiative title-setting board, and the members thereof in their official capacities. The proponent argued that the city misapplied state law in restricting the ballot initiative to a single subject.


OVERVIEW: The title board concluded it was unable to determine, or convey in a title, the true meaning and intent of the proponent's petition, because the initiative contained multiple subjects in violation of the single subject requirement set forth in Colorado Springs CO. Code § 5.1.503. The proponent wanted the court to set the ballot title to contain the entire text of the initiative verbatim. In reviewing the Colo. R. Civ. P. 57 declaratory judgment claim as a matter of law, the court of appeals concluded that the case must be remanded to the trial court for a determination on the constitutionality of the city's single subject ordinance. The city's single subject ordinance was substantially similar to the constitutional and statutory single subject rule. The ordinance, and not State constitutional provisions, applied to the initiative, and the proponent had not waived his challenge. Therefore, any determination whether the title board abused its discretion in finding that the proposed initiative violates the single subject requirement was premature, and the court declined to address that issue. Accordingly, the case was remanded for resolution of the constitutional issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded for a determination whether the city's ordinance was constitutional. The lower court erred in applying the constitutional and statutory single subject requirements to the proposed ordinance.

Independence Inst. v. Coffman


Court of Appeals No. 07CA1151


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


209 P.3d 1130; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 2086



November 26, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Independence Inst. v. Buescher, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 8215 (U.S., Nov. 16, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 05CV7604. Honorable Herbert L. Stern, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nonprofit organization sued appellee Colorado Secretary of State, alleging constitutional challenges to article XXVIII of the Colorado Constitution and the disclosure provisions of the Colorado Fair Campaign Practices Act (FCPA). The District Court for the City and County of Denver, Colorado, granted summary judgment in favor of the Secretary on all of the organization's claims. The organization appealed.


OVERVIEW: The organization argued that Colo. Const. art. XXVIII, § 2(10)(a), which defines "issue committee," was unconstitutionally vague and facially overbroad. The court concluded that art. XXVIII, § 2(10)(a), was neither facially vague nor overbroad. Art. XXVIII, § 2(10)(a), did not sweep a substantial amount of protected speech within its application. The organization did not prove that the definition of "issue committee" was invalid in all respects and could not be constitutionally applied in any circumstances. The court rejected the organization's argument that the definition of "a major purpose" in art. XXVIII, § 2(10)(a), was facially overbroad. Art. XXVIII, § 2(10)(a), did not burden a substantial amount of constitutionally protected speech. The court also concluded that the FCPA's disclosure requirements did not violate the right to engage in anonymous speech and association and that requiring the disclosure of the identity of contributors to ballot measures was constitutional. The organization did not allege that compelled disclosure would subject its contributors to threats, harassment, or reprisals from other government officials or private parties.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

McLane Western, Inc. v. Dep't of Revenue


Court of Appeals No. 07CA2497


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SEVEN


199 P.3d 752; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 2080



November 26, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 30, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 06CV12232. Honorable Larry J. Naves, Judge.
McLane W., Inc. v. Dep't of Revenue, 126 P.3d 211, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 672 (Colo. Ct. App., 2005)



DISPOSITION: ORDER REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company sued defendants, state department of revenue and a director (department), alleging that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 39-28.5-102 (2008) violated the Due Process and the Equal Protection Clauses of the United States and state constitutions. The City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) granted the department's motion to dismiss. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The company bought, resold and shipped grocery products throughout the state and in other western states. As part of its operations, the company bought other tobacco products (OTP) directly from a tobacco manufacturer. The manufacturer, made, marketed and sold smokeless tobacco products to unaffiliated distributors. The company sought refunds for what it asserted were excess OTP excise taxes. The company had filed a prior action in which it alleged that the statute violated the Commerce Clause and sought a refund for tax years 1990 through 2001. In the current action, the company sought a refund for tax years 2002 through 2004 alleging violations of due process and equal protection. The appellate court found that the trial court conflated the requirements of issue preclusion with those of claim preclusion. The present suit involved only OTP excise taxes paid during various periods between 2002 and 2004. Although the current case and the prior action concerned the discriminatory nature of the OTP tax statutes in violation of the Equal Protection Clause, the equal protection claim in the current case and the equal protection claim adjudicated in the prior action were distinct.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was reversed and the case was remanded with directions to reinstate the complaint.

People v. Griego


Court of Appeals No. 06CA2609


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


207 P.3d 870; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1829



October 30, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Griego v. People, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 441 (Colo., May 11, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Douglas County District Court No. 03CR2. Honorable Paul A. King, Judge.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to aggravated felony theft. In accordance with the terms of the plea agreement, the Douglas County District Court (Colorado) sentenced her to community corrections for nine years. However, defendant was later terminated for cause from the program, and, after holding a hearing, the trial court changed her placement and resentenced her to nine years in the Colorado Department of Corrections (DOC). She appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the plea agreement, the People agreed not to object to a direct sentence to community corrections, and the parties agreed to a six-year cap on any prison sentence imposed. Defendant argued that the nine-year prison sentence violated her right to due process because it was inconsistent with her understanding of the agreement. Because it was undisputed and defendant admitted that she was on probation for another felony at the time of the offense and the trial court held a hearing under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1.3-301(1)(h) (2008), the nine-year DOC sentence was appropriate and within the range of sentences that could originally have been imposed for defendant's aggravated felony theft offense under Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 18-1.3-401(1)(a)(V)(A), (6), (8)(a)(III), and 18-4-401(2)(c) (2008). Furthermore, because defendant's agreement contained no explicit language covering the contingency of her termination from community corrections and, following her termination, a different factual predicate existed upon which the trial court could base its sentencing determination, the trial court was no longer bound by the terms of the agreement, including the six-year sentencing cap.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's sentence.

People v. Cooper


Court of Appeals No. 07CA0505


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SIX


205 P.3d 475; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1835



October 30, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 1, 2009.
Writ of certiorari denied Cooper v. People, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 383 (Colo., Apr. 20, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Larimer County District Court No. 06CR211. Honorable Terence A. Gilmore, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, SENTENCE AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Larimer County District Court (Colorado), which convicted him of felony theft and second-degree aggravated motor vehicle theft. The court sentenced him as a habitual offender to 18 years in prison for the theft conviction and four and one-half years in prison for the motor vehicle theft conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of felony theft and second-degree aggravated motor vehicle theft. The trial court determined that he was a habitual offender with two prior felony convictions in the 10 years leading up to the current crimes. The trial court sentenced him to 18 years in prison for his theft conviction, a class four felony, and four and one-half years in prison for the motor vehicle theft conviction, a class six felony. On appeal, the court found that the trial court did not have the authority to sentence defendant as a habitual offender for the class six felony of aggravated motor vehicle theft. Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1.3-401(1)(a)(V)(A) (2008) provided that the maximum sentence for a class six felony was 18 months. Because second-degree aggravated motor vehicle theft was a class six felony, it did not fall within the purview of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1.3-801(1.5). However, even assuming that the offense of felony theft and the two predicate offenses were not individually grave or serious, in combination, they were sufficiently grave and serious to support a conclusion that defendant's 18-year sentence was not extreme and grossly disproportionate to his crimes.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed. The habitual criminal sentence for the felony theft conviction was affirmed. The habitual criminal sentence for the aggravated motor vehicle theft conviction was reversed, and the case was remanded to the trial court for resentencing on that conviction.

Glenwright v. St. James Place Condo. Ass'n


Court of Appeals No. 07CA0727


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


197 P.3d 264; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1433



October 16, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Eagle County District Court No. 05CV681. Honorable R. Thomas Moorhead, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff condominium owner appealed summary judgment granted by the Eagle County District Court (Colorado) in favor of defendant condominium association in the condominium owner's suit seeking declaratory and injunctive relief under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 38-33.3-317 (1991).


OVERVIEW: Believing that the condominium association was overcharging condominium owners for services, the condominium owner requested records documenting housekeeping services and subsequently filed suit to compel production. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the association, holding that, because the association did not produce or maintain the records at issue and because they were created and maintained by the management company that provided services, the owner was entitled to no relief. On review, the court held that, because the management company was the association's agent, the records were subject to production if they constituted a part of the association's "financial and other records" under former Colo. Rev. Stat. § 38-33.3-317. Summary judgment was improper because the record was insufficient to permit a determination of whether the records at issue contained information pertinent to the association's exercise of its responsibilities under the statute. While the trial court afforded greater weight to the evidence produced by the association in making its conclusion, weighing evidence was improper when passing upon a summary judgment motion.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

463 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Manier


Court of Appeals No. 05CA2704


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


197 P.3d 254; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1392



October 2, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Jefferson County District Court No. 04CR3406. Honorable Jack W. Berryhill, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Jefferson County District Court (Colorado) of first degree aggravated motor vehicle theft under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-4-409(2) (2008), possession of one gram or less of a schedule II controlled substance, possession of drug paraphernalia, false reporting, and theft by receiving. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised many issues. The court reversed the first degree aggravated motor vehicle theft conviction and remanded with directions, but otherwise affirmed. The trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence. While the knowingly mens rea in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-4-409(2) (2008) did not necessarily apply to each of the eight aggravators, it did not follow that there was no mens rea requirement associated with the aggravator at issue in this case, § 18-4-409(2)(h). Attaching or displaying unauthorized license plates was not unlawful unless it was done knowingly, for purposes of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 42-3-121(1)(b) (2008). The trial court's response in telling the jury that defendant did not have to know the plates did not belong to the truck was incorrect, and its subsequent reminder that all the elements of the relevant jury instruction had to be proved beyond a reasonable doubt was inadequate. The evidence was sufficient to establish defendant's liability for second degree aggravated motor vehicle theft. Whether to retry defendant on the original charge or ask for resentencing on the lesser charge was left to the discretion of the prosecution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of conviction of first degree aggravated motor vehicle theft and remanded. The prosecution could elect to retry defendant on that charge or ask the trial court to enter a judgment of conviction of second degree aggravated motor vehicle theft and resentence defendant for that offense. The judgment of conviction was otherwise affirmed.

 

464 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bergerud


Court of Appeals No. 06CA0013


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


203 P.3d 579; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1397



September 18, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: April 2, 2009, Release for Publication.
Rehearing denied by People v. Bergerud, 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1749 (Colo. Ct. App., Oct. 16, 2008)
Writ of certiorari granted People v. Bergerud, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 303 (Colo., Mar. 23, 2009)
Reversed by, Remanded by People v. Bergerud, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 4 (Colo., Jan. 11, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Weld County District Court No. 02CR457. Honorable J. Robert Lowenbach, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Weld County District Court (Colorado) convicting him of first-degree murder, second-degree murder, and assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for killing his ex-girlfriend and her male companion and for shooting at police officers. During his second trial, counsel argued during opening statements that defendant lacked the premeditation and intent necessary for first-degree murder. Defendant subsequently sought the appointment of different counsel, contending that he wanted to argue at trial that he was innocent based on self-defense. The trial court refused, requiring defendant to choose between having counsel or claiming self-defense. Defendant chose to represent himself and was convicted. On appeal, the court held that defendant's constitutional right to counsel under the Sixth Amendment and Colo. Const. art. II, § 16 was violated by the trial court's requiring him to choose between having counsel or claiming self-defense, and therefore his waiver of counsel was not voluntary. Defendant's clear objective was outright acquittal, and however unlikely that prospect, his counsel could not deny him that right and refuse to raise the defense.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

465 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. McCulloch


Court of Appeals No. 07CA0773


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


198 P.3d 1264; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1387



September 4, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 30, 2009.
Writ of certiorari denied McCulloch v. People, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 88 (Colo., Jan. 12, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Boulder County District Court No. 05CR1367. Honorable Lael E. Montgomery, Judge. Honorable David Anthony Archuleta, Acting District Judge.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Boulder County District Court (Colorado) to two felony counts of contributing to the delinquency of a minor. The parties stipulated to a four-year prison sentence on one count consecutive to four to ten years imprisonment on the other count. A county court judge, sitting by assignment, sentenced defendant to 14 years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a 48-year-old man, had five prior felony convictions for attempted sexual assault of a child, pandering, attempted theft, attempted first degree criminal trespass, and contributing to the delinquency of a minor. Because defendant was on parole for another felony, the presumptive term of imprisonment increased to four to twelve years per count under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1.3-401(8)(a)(II) (2007). On appeal, he challenged the authority of the county court judge to impose the sentence and the proportionality of his sentence under U.S. Const. amend. VIII. The chief judge of the Boulder district court had assigned the county court judge to sit as a district judge for one week. The court held that the Chief Justice's authority to assign judges under Colo. Const. art. VI, § 5(3) and Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-6-218 (2007) could be delegated to the district judge. Further, defendant's sentences gave rise to no inference of gross disproportionality. Defendant tried to minimize his offense as simply providing beer and cigarettes to a 17-year-old boy; however, the trial court found that he was trying to lure the minor into a sexual encounter, a grave and serious offense.


OUTCOME: The district court's denial of defendant's challenges to his sentence was affirmed.

 

466 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Firth


Court of Appeals No. 06CA2346


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SIX


205 P.3d 445; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1398



September 4, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 3, 2009.
Writ of certiorari denied Firth v. People, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 341 (Colo., Apr. 13, 2009)
Post-conviction proceeding at Firth v. Shoemaker, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 20854 (D. Colo., Mar. 8, 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by, Certificate of appealability denied Firth v. Smelser, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 76176 (D. Colo., June 24, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Archuleta County District Court No. 02CR68. Honorable Jeffrey R. Wilson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Archuleta County District Court (Colorado), which denied his Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c) motion for postconviction relief following the revocation of his probation and which sentenced him to an indeterminate term of six years to life pursuant to the Colorado Sex Offender Lifetime Supervision Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 18-1.3-1001 to -1012 (2007).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's probation was revoked based on his failure to complete treatment and his possession of a knife. Although the district court agreed that the evidence as to the knife was insufficient to support the revocation, it rejected his remaining arguments in his motion. The court held that the condition of defendant's probation requiring him to attend and actively participate in sex offender evaluation and treatment program approved by his probation officer and to complete the treatment program and treatment contract to the satisfaction of his probation officer was not unconstitutionally vague either on its face or as applied to defendant. Furthermore, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in determining that defendant's probation officer and treatment provider followed the requirements of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1.3-1010 (2007) and in revoking defendant's probation. Finally, because there was ample support for the findings regarding defendant's violations independent of the alleged deficient performance of defense counsel, there was no error in the trial court's finding that defendant failed to establish the requisite prejudice to support his ineffective assistance claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's order.

Saint John's Church in the Wilderness v. Scott


Court of Appeals No. 06CA2421


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


194 P.3d 475; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1422



August 21, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 1, 2008.
Writ of certiorari denied Scott v. St. John's Church in the Wilderness, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 832 (Colo., Sept. 14, 2009)
Appeal after remand at Saint Church in the Wilderness v. Scott, 2012 Colo. App. LEXIS 639 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 05CV2290. Honorable John N. McMullen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED, ORDER AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the City and County of Denver, Colorado, entered a final judgment in favor of plaintiffs, a church and two of its parishioners, against one of two defendants on plaintiffs' private nuisance claim and against both defendants on plaintiffs' conspiracy to commit private nuisance claims. The trial court also issued a permanent injunction against both defendants. Defendants appealed the judgments and the injunction.


OVERVIEW: Defendants had led anti-abortion demonstrations at the church. The instant court concluded that there was evidence in the record to support the trial court's findings and conclusions that one of the defendants created a private nuisance and that both defendants engaged in a civil conspiracy to create a private nuisance. The injunction was content-neutral. Entering the church's property and obstructing access to the church were not inherently expressive acts; therefore, the injunction's prohibitions of such conduct were not restrictions on speech. The time limitations on defendants' speech burdened no more speech than necessary to serve the interests protected by the injunction. The time restrictions applied only during worship and preparation for worship at the church. However, it could not be determined from the record whether the place and manner restrictions burdened more speech than was necessary. The place restrictions were not defined by a perimeter drawn a given distance from the protected facility, but were defined by a map attached to the injunction order. The trial court did not make specific findings justifying the scope and extent of the manner restrictions.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed. The injunction order was vacated as to the restriction on defendants' entry onto the church's property. The case was remanded for specific findings and, if necessary, amendment of the injunction as to the place and manner restrictions on picketing and noise in each buffer zone. The injunction was affirmed in all other respects.

 

468 of 734 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Schelp


Court of Appeals No. 06CA0424


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


194 P.3d 450; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1270



August 7, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 1, 2008.
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part In re Marriage of Schelp, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 250 (Colo., Mar. 16, 2009)
Reversed by, Remanded by 08sc748, in re Marriage Of: Petitioner: Rainer Schelp, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 230 (Colo., Mar. 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Arapahoe County District Court No. 03DR973. Honorable Karen S. Metzger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED IN PART AND DISMISSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former husband sought review of post-decree orders of the Arapahoe County District Court (Colorado) finding that the husband had not fully disclosed the value of a retirement pension, awarding the entire marital portion of the pension to appellee former wife, and ordering the husband to pay one-half of the master's fees to investigate the wife's allegations of non-disclosure.


OVERVIEW: In a marriage dissolution, permanent orders were entered after a hearing before a retired judge, who was selected by the parties pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-3-111 (2007). The parties agreed to share the husband's pensions equally. The wife filed a motion to adopt a qualified domestic relations order. In a non-jury action, the trial court appointed a special master to investigate the facts. The husband's appeal of the trial court's order to appoint the master and the trial court's order requiring each party to pay one-half of the master's fees to investigate the wife's allegations were premature. The orders were not final for purposes of appeal because the rights of the parties were not completely determined. The husband had failed to object to the initial appointment of the master, and therefore he did not preserve the issue for appeal. Finding that the special master's factual findings were not clearly erroneous, the court accepted the master's findings of non-disclosure and that the husband's omission of the value of his portion of the pension materially affected the division of assets, pursuant to Colo. R. Civ. P. 53(e)(2).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the part of the trial court's judgment adopting the special master's factual findings and in determining that the husband's omission of the value of his marital portion of his pension materially affected the division of assets. The court dismissed the part of the husband's appeal relating to the orders continuing the appointment of the master requiring the parties initially to share the payment of his fees.

In re Marriage of Roberts


Court of Appeals No. 07CA0903


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


194 P.3d 443; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1271



August 7, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 1, 2008.
Writ of certiorari granted In re Marriage of Roberts, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 266 (Colo., Mar. 16, 2009)
Reversed by, Remanded by 08sc748, in re Marriage Of: Petitioner: Rainer Schelp, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 230 (Colo., Mar. 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Boulder County District Court No. 04DR1249. Honorable Morris W. Sandstead, Jr., Judge.
Lipson v. Roberts, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 1161 (Colo., Dec. 17, 2007)



DISPOSITION: ORDER REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife challenged an order of the Boulder County District Court (Colorado) dismissing her motion to set aside a separation agreement, pursuant to Colo. R. Civ. P. 16.2(e)(10), which was reached with appellee husband, on the ground that the husband had failed to make a full disclosure of his assets.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered a decree of legal separation in March 2005 that incorporated the parties' separation agreement. The separation agreement provided that the husband retained his separate property including the entire interest in a limited liability company that owned certain stock. In January 2007, the wife filed a motion to set aside the separation agreement on the ground that the husband had failed to make a full disclosure of his assets in violation of former Colo. R. Civ. P. 26.2(a)(1)(A), (e), (g)(1), which was repealed and replaced by Colo. R. Civ. P. 16.2. The stock owned by the limited liability company substantially increased in value during the marriage. The court held that the trial court had jurisdiction to rule on the wife's motion. Colo. R. Civ. P. 16.2(e)(10) applied to post-decree motions filed on or after January 1, 2005, that sought to reopen a property division or to set aside a separation agreement based on alleged misstatements, omissions, or nondisclosure of assets or liabilities that materially affected the division of property. The rule change was not unconstitutionally retrospective simply because it expanded the remedy afforded to the wife.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

 

470 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. K.W.S.


Court of Appeals No. 07CA0667


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


192 P.3d 579; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1161



July 24, 2008, Decided 
October 1, 2008, Released for Publication


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari granted K.W.S. v. People, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 90 (Colo., Jan. 12, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Larimer County District Court No. 06JD600. Honorable Jolene C. Blair, Judge.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged the order of the Larimer County District Court, Colorado, denying his Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(b) motion challenging a condition of an unrevoked deferred judgment and sentence agreement.


OVERVIEW: The People filed a delinquency petition alleging that appellant, then twelve years old, sexually assaulted a six-year-old boy. The parties executed a one-year deferred adjudication agreement. Appellant later filed a motion for reconsideration of sentence, purportedly under Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(b), in which he argued that based on the facts of the case, the requirement for genetic marker testing was unreasonable. The People argued that the appellate court was without jurisdiction because a deferred judgment and sentence agreement was not subject to direct appellate review unless and until such time as it was revoked. The appellate court agreed with the People. Colo. R. Crim. P. 35 established postconviction remedies, and no conviction entered when a deferred judgment and sentence agreement remained unrevoked. It was undisputed that appellant's stipulation to the deferred judgment and sentence agreement was the event that triggered the applicability of the statutory mandate. Because appellant stipulated to genetic marker testing, the appellate court was without jurisdiction to review an order which did nothing more than hold appellant to the stipulation.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

471 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Laurent


Court of Appeals No. 06CA0885


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


194 P.3d 1053; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1162



July 24, 2008, Decided 
October 1, 2008, Released for Publication


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Laurent v. People, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 338 (Colo., Apr. 13, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Adams County District Court No. 05CR432. Honorable Katherine R. Delgado, Judge. Prior Opinion Announced April 17, 2008, WITHDRAWN. Petition for Rehearing GRANTED.
People v. Laurent, 186 P.3d 118, 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 620 (Colo. Ct. App., 2008)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Adams County District Court (Colorado) that convicted him of manufacturing methamphetamine in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-18-405(1) and (2)(a)(I)(A) (2007) and child abuse for manufacturing methamphetamine in the presence of a child in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6-401(1)(c) (2003).


OVERVIEW: On review, the court rejected defendant's arguments that he had a reasonable expectation of privacy in trash placed curbside for collection, that the trial court erred in admitting expert testimony under Colo. R. Evid. 702 because the forensic chemistry expert did not follow a "written analytical method," and that the statute making it a crime to manufacture methamphetamine in the presence of a child, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6-401, was unconstitutional. However, the court agreed that defendant's conviction for manufacturing methamphetamine should merge into his conviction for manufacturing that substance in the presence of a child. A comparison of the two statutes showed that child abuse based on manufacturing a controlled substance included all of the elements of manufacturing a controlled substance. Because proof of child abuse based on manufacturing a controlled substance necessarily proved the elements of manufacturing a controlled substance, manufacturing a controlled substance was a lesser included offense of child abuse based on manufacturing a controlled substance.


OUTCOME: That part of the judgment of conviction finding defendant guilty of child abuse based on manufacturing a controlled substance was affirmed. Defendant's conviction and sentence for manufacturing a controlled substance were vacated, and the case was remanded to the trial court for correction of the mittimus.

 

472 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Zelenoy v. Colo. Dep't of Revenue


Court of Appeals No. 06CA2635


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SIX


192 P.3d 538; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1163



July 24, 2008, Decided 
October 1, 2008, Released for Publication


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Jefferson County District Court No.: 06CV1422. Honorable Christopher J. Munch, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant challenged the order of the Jefferson County District Court, Colorado, affirming the suspension of her driver's license by appellee Colorado Department of Revenue, Motor Vehicle Division (Department), for the claimant's failure to provide proof of financial responsibility for the future, as required under Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 42-7-103(14) and 42-7-406(1.5) (2007).


OVERVIEW: The claimant's son was involved in two separate alcohol-related car accidents. In both accidents, he was driving the claimant's car. After the second accident, the Department sent a notice of suspension to the claimant, requiring proof of financial responsibility in the form of an SR-22. The hearing officer ultimately suspended the claimant's license, and she appealed. The appellate court ruled that the hearing officer did not err in requiring the claimant to submit an SR-22 in her name as such proof. The policy the claimant submitted, an SR-22 in her son's name, applied to the driver only, thus, she did not provide an assurance that someone would be responsible for damages regardless of who was driving. Also, the standard liability insurance policies the claimant submitted to the Department could be cancelled at any time without the Department being notified, and those policies did not provide an assurance that someone would be responsible for damages for future accidents, an assurance that would have been provided by an SR-22. Furthermore, Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 42-7-103(14) and 42-7-406(1.5) were not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

473 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Kruse v. Town of Castle Rock


Court of Appeals No. 07CA1111


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


192 P.3d 591; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1168



July 24, 2008, Decided 
October 1, 2008, Released for Publication


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Douglas County District Court No. 06CV264. Honorable Nancy A. Hopf, Judge. Honorable Thomas J. Curry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed the judgment of the Douglas County District Court, Colorado, affirming the decision of defendant, the Town of Castle Rock, Colorado, acting through its town council and individual council members, adopting an involuntary historic designation ordinance designating a house built in 1875 as a local historic landmark.


OVERVIEW: A house in Castle Rock, Colorado was built in 1875. It was one of the last remaining structures from the town's founding era. Plaintiff purchased the property in 1998. When she applied for a demolition permit, the town council voted to approve an ordinance designating the property a historic landmark. Plaintiff filed suit asserting claims under Colo. R. Civ. P. 106(a)(4) for review of a governmental body's decision and Colo. R. Civ. P. 57 for declaratory relief. The district court correctly concluded that the town's historic preservation code was not unconstitutionally vague. Its terms had a clear meaning to a person of ordinary intelligence. The Court of Appeals of Colorado held that the town council did not exceed its jurisdiction by allowing its staff to usurp the preservation board's authority by researching the history of the property, submitting a report, and advocating the adoption of a historic designation ordinance. The doctrine of equitable estoppel did not prevent the town from enacting an ordinance designating the property as a historic landmark. Plaintiff failed to establish an economic hardship.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Hopkins


Court of Appeals No. 07CA0662


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


190 P.3d 833; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1070



June 26, 2008, Decided 
September 1, 2008, Released for Publication


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Adams County District Court No. 02CR1853. Honorable Edward C. Moss, Judge.
People v. Hopkins, 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1461 (Colo. Ct. App., Aug. 31, 2006)



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the sentence imposed by the Adams County District Court (Colorado) following a remand for resentencing, arguing that the sentence imposed violated her right to due process because it unconstitutionally increased her punishment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a guilty plea to a charge of theft, and the district court sentenced defendant to 10 years in community corrections. Defendant appealed, and the appellate court found the sentence unconstitutional. The State sought review, and the state supreme court vacated the ruling and remanded for reconsideration. On remand, the appellate court again found that the original sentence was unconstitutional. The sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded to the district court for resentencing. On remand, the district court found that a prison sentence was more appropriate than a community corrections sentence and imposed a three-year term of incarceration. Defendant sought appellate view. On review, the appellate court held that the harsher sentence imposed on remand did not comport with the statutory resentencing requirements because the trial court did not rely on defendant's conduct occurring after the imposition of the original sentence or any other subsequent aggravating factors but imposed a sentence based upon what it would have done if it had been the original sentencing court; Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1-409(3) (2007) did not permit this.


OUTCOME: The sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

475 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Linares-Guzman


Court of Appeals No. 05CA2445


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


195 P.3d 1130; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1072



June 26, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: December 4, 2008, Released for Publication
Writ of certiorari denied Linares-Guzman v. People, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 1543 (Colo., Nov. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Arapahoe County District Court No. 04CR329. Honorable Cheryl L. Post, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, SENTENCES AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Arapahoe County District Court, Colorado, convicting him of first degree burglary, attempted aggravated robbery, criminal conspiracy to commit first degree burglary, aggravated robbery, and possession with intent to distribute a schedule II controlled substance. Defendant also appealed the imposed sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and several confederates agreed to steal money and drugs allegedly hidden inside the home occupied by the two victims and their parents. After the group went to the victims' home, one of defendant's confederates kidnapped one victim from the lawn in front of the home. While the kidnapping was occurring, another confederate entered the home, brandished a gun, and demanded that the second victim give him money. The confederate eventually shot the second victim, who suffered serious bodily injury. At trial, defendant's theory of the case was that he participated in the agreement and attempt to commit the robbery in which the group sought drugs and money, but that he did not intend or consider kidnapping the first victim. The appellate court ruled that because the jury unanimously agreed that defendant intended to commit aggravated robbery upon entry into the victims' home, any error in the failure to give a unanimity jury instruction was not plain error since there was no reasonable possibility that any error contributed to defendant's conviction. Also, the trial court misapprehended the applicable sentencing range.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed, the sentence on the conspiracy conviction was vacated, and the case was remanded for resentencing within the correct range. The remaining sentences were affirmed.

 

476 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Montalvo-Lopez


Court of Appeals No. 05CA2090


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


215 P.3d 1139; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 805



May 15, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 2, 2009.
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part Montalvo-Lopez v. People, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 818 (Colo., Oct. 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Mesa County District Court No. 04CR1299. Honorable Nicholas R. Massaro, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Mesa County District Court (Colorado), defendant was convicted of possession with intent to distribute 1000 grams of a schedule II controlled substance (cocaine) under Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 18-18-405(1)(a), (2)(a)(I)(A), and (3)(a)(III) (2007), and was sentenced as a special offender under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-18-407(1)(d) to enhanced incarceration of 16 years and one day. Defendant appealed the verdict and the sentence.


OVERVIEW: After a police officer pulled defendant over for a traffic offense, the officer requested to search the vehicle. The search revealed the cocaine. The search was not unconstitutional because the circumstances indicated that it was consensual. Under the balancing test of Colo. R. Evid. 403, purported drug-courier-profile evidence was properly admitted because the evidence was testimony regarding how drugs were transported and it aided the jurors' understanding of an activity with which they were not likely to be familiar. Assuming, without deciding, that Crim. P. 16(I)(a)(1)(I) imposed a duty to disclose witness statements given to another governmental authority, the court concluded that any error in not disclosing an admitted statement made by a codefendant to federal investigators inculpating defendant was harmless because defendant knew of the statement but failed to request disclosure. Defendant's sentence was the minimum that could be imposed because (1) the special offender sentence was greater under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-18-405 than under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-18-407; and (2) Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-18-405(3)(a) required that the regimen producing the greater sentence apply.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and the sentence.

People v. Rice


Court of Appeals No. 05CA0931


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


198 P.3d 1241; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 811; Unemployment Ins. Rep. (CCH) P8630



May 15, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 30, 2009.
Modified and rehearing denied by People v. Rice, 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1359 (Colo. Ct. App., July 10, 2008)
Writ of certiorari denied People v. Rice, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 76 (Colo., Jan. 12, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 04CR530. Honorable Sheila A. Rappaport, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) convicting her of computer crime in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-5.5-102(1)(c)-(d) (2007).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for lying when using the Colorado Department of Labor and Employment's interactive computer system and choosing the option indicating that she had not worked during the week for which she claimed unemployment benefits when in fact she had. On appeal, the court held that even though the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction, defendant was entitled to a new trial because, under plain error review, the variance from the complaint created by the prosecution's closing arguments and jury instructions prejudiced defendant's rights to notice and an ability to present a defense by expanding the scope of defendant's alleged purpose for obtaining money. The information put defendant on notice that she was charged under the theory that she accessed the system with the purpose of obtaining money from the Department, and she argued at trial that she believed the money she obtained belonged to her as it had been withheld from her paychecks. The prosecution argued that it could prove the crime by proving that defendant accessed the system with the purpose of obtaining unemployment benefits regardless of who she believed the money belonged to.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

McCool v. Sears


Court of Appeals No. 06CA 1922


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


186 P.3d 147; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 675



May 1, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Office of Outfitter Registrations No. OG20040001.
Sears v. Romer, 928 P.2d 745, 1996 Colo. App. LEXIS 75 (Colo. Ct. App., 1996)



DISPOSITION: ORDER SET ASIDE IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent revoked outfitter challenged an order issued by petitioner agency director that instructed him, inter alia, to cease and desist from acting as a booking agent or hunter referral source for Colorado outfitters.


OVERVIEW: The director misinterpreted the Outfitters and Guides Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. tit. 12, art. 55.5 (2007), by ordering the revoked outfitter to stop acting as a booking agent for outfitters because he was not registered. The director's interpretation of soliciting, found in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-55.5-102(5) (2007), did not give effect to each word in the phrase in which the term was found. Giving effect to each word, a person who solicited on behalf of others who provided outfitting services was not an outfitter. The director exceeded her statutory authority by promulgating Colo. Dep't Reg. Agencies Regs. No. D.17, 4 Code Colo. Regs. § 733-1, as nothing in the Act prevented a revoked outfitter from acting as a booking agent for registered outfitters. Moreover, the grant of authority to promulgate rules, coupled with the Act's stated purpose, did not authorize the promulgation of such rules. Finally, the director misinterpreted Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-55.5-102.5 (2007) by ordering the revoked outfitter to stop soliciting persons to hunt, fish, or take wildlife on land that he leased where the stipulated facts showed that he did not solicit to provide outfitting services on the land.


OUTCOME: Those portions of the director's order directing that the revoked outfitter cease and desist from acting as a booking agent or hunter referral source for registered outfitters and from soliciting persons to hunt or fish on land that he leased were set aside.

 

479 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Sperry v. Field


Court of Appeals No. 07CA0282


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


186 P.3d 133; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 677



May 1, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari granted Sperry v. Field, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 901 (Colo., Sept. 2, 2008)
Affirmed by Petitioner: Sperry v. Respondent: Sherry Field, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 344 (Colo., Apr. 13, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Pueblo County District Court No. 99CV1045. Honorable Dennis Maes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AND JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury awarded plaintiff damages for personal injuries resulting from defendant's negligence. Plaintiff moved for a modified judgment and an award of postjudgment interest. The Pueblo County District Court, Colorado, denied the motion for postjudgment interest calculated from the date of the accident. Plaintiff was awarded postjudgment interest, calculated from the date judgment was entered to the date of satisfaction. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue the court had to resolve was when postjudgment interest began to accrue on a personal injury judgment for money damages pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-21-101(1) (2007), in a case where a plaintiff was not entitled to prejudgment interest because it was not requested in the complaint. The plain language of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-21-101 (2007) was ambiguous and contradictory with respect to the date postjudgment interest began to accrue. The court found that where a plaintiff was not entitled to prejudgment interest and the judgment debtor appealed the judgment, the plaintiff was entitled to an award of postjudgment interest calculated from the date judgment was entered to the date of satisfaction. Plaintiff failed to request prejudgment interest in her complaint. Thus, the court rejected plaintiff's contention that she was entitled to postjudgment interest calculated from the date of her accident. The trial court did not err in awarding plaintiff postjudgment interest calculated from the date the judgment was entered to the date of satisfaction. The trial court had no jurisdiction to award interest accruing before the date judgment was first entered.


OUTCOME: The order and judgment were affirmed.
