People v. Laurent


Court of Appeals No. 06CA0885


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


186 P.3d 118; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 620



April 17, 2008, Decided 
October 1, 2008, Released for Publication


NOTICE: WITHDRAWN BY PUBLISHER


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Substituted opinion at, Withdrawn by publisher, Reported at, Rehearing granted by, Remanded by People v. Laurent, 194 P.3d 1053, 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1162 (Colo. Ct. App., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Adams County District Court No. 05CR432. Honorable Katherine R. Delgado, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Adams County District Court (Colorado) found defendant guilty of two counts under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-18-405(1) and (2)(a)(I)(A) (2007) (manufacture of methamphetamine), and of one count under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6-401(1)(c) (manufacture of methamphetamine with a child present). Defendant was sentenced to 12 years of intensive supervised probation and 90 days in jail. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant lived with his three-year-old daughter. After receiving a tip that defendant was manufacturing methamphetamine, a detective arranged to have an empty trash truck pick up defendant's trash so that the detective could inspect its contents. On pick-up day, defendant's roommate deposited the trash at the curb for collection. Police inspected the trash and discovered many items that are commonly used to manufacture methamphetamine, leading to their obtaining a search warrant. The court held that defendant did not have a reasonable expectation of privacy in his trash once it was left at the curb despite the fact that defendant kept his trash locked up until trash day, kept it in sealed opaque bags, and relied on the fact that the trash truck used a mechanical arm to throw the trash in the truck. A chemical expert's testimony was properly admitted under Colo. R. Evid. 702. Defendant did not have standing to argue that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6-401(1)(c) was overbroad because he was not charged under the portion of the statute contended to be overbroad. Section 18-6-401(1)(c) did not unconstitutionally infringe on parents' right to raise their children.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

People v. Carey


Court of Appeals No. 05CA1378


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SIX


198 P.3d 1223; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 623



April 17, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 30, 2009.
Rehearing denied by People v. Carey, 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1016 (Colo. Ct. App., June 12, 2008)
Writ of certiorari denied Carey v. People, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 72 (Colo., Jan. 12, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Arapahoe County District Court No. 03CR2536. Honorable Gerald J. Rafferty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction entered in the Arapahoe County District Court, Colorado, on a jury verdict finding him guilty of harassment by stalking, violation of a protection order, and violation of a bail bond condition.


OVERVIEW: In the first case, defendant was charged with harassment and domestic violence based on telephone calls he made to the victim. That case was resolved by defendant's plea of guilty to violation of a restraining order. He argued that his conviction for harassment by stalking in the second case violated his right to be protected against double jeopardy. The Court of Appeals of Colorado disagreed. Under the Blockberger test, the elements of the harassment by stalking offense were different from the elements of violating a restraining order. The testimony regarding defendant's repeated threats and their effect on victim's mental state was sufficient to support the harassment by stalking conviction under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-9-111(4)(b)(II). The trial court properly declined to instruct the jury on the offense of misdemeanor telephone harassment. The trial court did not err in refusing to give an instruction requiring the jurors to agree unanimously as to which communications established harassment by stalking.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Loveall


Court of Appeals No. 05CA2031


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


203 P.3d 540; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 437



March 20, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: April 2, 2009, Release for Publication.
Rehearing denied by People v. Loveall, 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 770 (Colo. Ct. App., May 8, 2008)
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part People v. Loveall, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 510 (Colo., Mar. 30, 2009)
Affirmed by, Remanded by People v. Loveall, 2010 Colo. LEXIS 377 (Colo., May 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Douglas County District Court No. 01CR191. Honorable Thomas J. Curry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's probation on an enticement of a child conviction was revoked by the Douglas County District Court (Colorado) on the grounds that he had violated several probation conditions. He was sentenced to an indeterminate sentence of two years to life. Defendant appealed the order revoking his probation.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had authority to order a deferred sentence because until defendant was sentenced for child enticement, the Lifetime Supervision Act did not apply. The claim that the trial court could only order a deferred sentence if defendant was represented by counsel was rejected as Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1.3-102 (2007) required the written consent of defense counsel only if a defendant was represented. Because defendant was pro se, counsel's consent was not required. The reliance on double and triple hearsay at the revocation hearing deprived defendant of his due process right to confront adverse witnesses where there was no good cause to deny confrontation or to find that the hearsay evidence was substantially reliable. Moreover, the evidence did not fall within a recognized hearsay exception, lacked meaningful detail, and contained material inconsistencies. Defendant was deprived of an opportunity to rebut as the prosecution did not disclose the declarants' identities until the day of the hearing. Defendant was entitled to a new hearing because without the hearsay evidence, the trial court could not have found that he knowingly violated several probation conditions.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed. The case was remanded for a new evidentiary hearing to determine whether defendant committed the alleged violations or whether to revoke probation solely because he failed to maintain employment.

Curious Theater Co. v. Colo. Dep't of Pub. Health & Env't


Court of Appeals No. 06CA2260


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


216 P.3d 71; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 442



March 20, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 2, 2009.
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part Curious Theatre Co. v. Colo. Dep't of Pub. Health & Env't, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 1732 (Colo., Dec. 2, 2008)
Affirmed by Curious Theatre Co. v. Colo. Dep't of Pub. Health & Env't, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 1158 (Colo., Dec. 14, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 06CV10876. Honorable Michael A. Martinez, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff theaters appealed a judgment of the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) denying their request for a preliminary injunction and a declaratory judgment against the enforcement of the Colorado Clean Indoor Air Act (Smoking Ban), Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 25-14-201 to 25-14-209 (2007), by defendants Colorado Department of Health and Environment and its executive director as applied to theatrical productions.


OVERVIEW: The theaters alleged that the Smoking Ban violated their constitutional rights under the First Amendment and Colo. Const. art. II, § 10 because it precluded conduct that could be presented as part of certain theatrical productions. On appeal of the district court's judgment, the court affirmed. The court held that the Smoking Ban did not violate the theaters' right to freedom of expression because, under the intermediate level of scrutiny: (1) the Colorado legislature had the authority to enact statutes designed to promote the public health under Colo. Const. art. V, § 1(4); (2) the Smoking Ban served an important governmental interest by protecting the health of Colorado's citizens; (3) the Smoking Ban was content neutral because it was justified by health concerns unrelated to expression; and (4) it was narrowly tailored, as it focused directly on the one form of conduct, smoking, upon which Colorado's announced interest in protecting public health depended. The Smoking Ban allowed other channels of expression, such as outdoor theatrical performances, and there were alternative channels for expression within indoor theaters, such as fake and prop cigarettes.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying the theaters' request for a preliminary injunction and a declaratory judgment was affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Arapahoe County District Court (Colorado) of first degree murder after deliberation and abuse of a corpse. Defendant was sentenced to life in the Colorado Department of Corrections. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress evidence because the stop and search were illegal. The court of appeals disagreed. Officers observed defendant's vehicle parked in violation of local ordinances in an area known for drug trafficking. The officers arrested defendant for carrying a concealed firearm, and because there was no one to retrieve the car, the officers impounded the car and inventoried its contents, including the trunk, where one officer observed a knife with blood on it lying along the fender well. The other officer uncovered a gym bag containing ski masks, handcuffs, a baton, and other items. Both officers observed what appeared to be bloodstains inside the trunk.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Marriage of Schmedeman


Court of Appeals No. 06CA0550


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


190 P.3d 788; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 238



February 21, 2008, Decided 
September 1, 2008, Released for Publication


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by In re Marriage of Schmedeman, 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 1131 (Colo. Ct. App., July 3, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Douglas County District Court No. 04DR168. Honorable Angela R. Arkin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the husband, sought review of the decision of the Douglas County District Court (Colorado), which divided the marital property and awarded child support as part of the permanent orders in the dissolution action between the husband and appellee, the wife.


OVERVIEW: The trial court divided marital property and awarded child support as part of the permanent orders in the action to dissolve the marriage between the husband and wife. The appellate court reversed the property division award, remanded for further proceedings, and affirmed the remainder of the judgment. The appellate court agreed with the husband's argument that the trial court erred in classifying a log cabin owned by his parents as marital property and dividing part of its value between the parties equally. Under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 14-10-113(1) and (2) (2007), the wife's objection to the husband's giving the logs and the cabin shell to his parents during the marriage did not preserve the wife's right to have the property classified as marital property under the Uniform Dissolution of Marriage Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 14-10-101 to 14-10-113 (2007). Further, the husband's father's intent to bequeath the cabin to the husband did not prove that the father had gifted his ownership interest in the cabin back to the husband and wife. Accordingly, the trial court erred in classifying the log cabin owned by the husband's parents as marital property.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed as to the property division and the case remanded for further proceedings. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

Seguna v. Maketa


Court of Appeals No. 07CA0840


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


181 P.3d 399; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 243



February 21, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
El Paso County District Court No. 06CV4979. Honorable Rebecca S. Bromley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER VACATED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The El Paso County District Court, Colorado, affirmed the denial by appellee El Paso County Sheriff's Office of appellant resident's application for renewal of a concealed handgun permit. The resident appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court noted that Colorado's legislature had made it clear that, for the purposes of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-12-108(1) (2007), it had to look to the other's state's law to determine whether a person had been convicted of a felony. It was undisputed that the set-aside conviction was for a felony in Michigan. Under Michigan law, the resident was not to be considered convicted of the set-aside felony, unless he fit within a specified exception. The set-aside conviction was for a drug offense, not for an offense involving weapons. Thus, none of the exceptions recognized by statute or in the Michigan attorney general's opinion applied. Thus, the resident was not convicted of a felony under any other state's law.


OUTCOME: The district court's order was vacated and the case remanded to the district court with directions to enter an order directing the Sheriff's Office to renew the resident's permit.

People v. Hotle


Court of Appeals No. 06CA1617


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


216 P.3d 68; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 240



February 21, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 2, 2009.
Writ of certiorari denied Hotle v. People, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 701 (Colo., June 30, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Adams County District Court No. 04CR891. Honorable Robert S. Doyle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Adams County District Court, Colorado, found that defendant's consent to extend probation and waiver of a hearing were valid. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he had both a due process and a Sixth Amendment right to counsel before signing the consent to extend probation and waiver of his right to a hearing. He argued that because he was not aware of that right and the probation department did not advise him of it, his consent and waiver were unconstitutionally obtained, and the district court lost jurisdiction to extend, and subsequently to revoke his probation. The appellate court found that an extension or modification of probation was not analogous to a probation revocation proceeding. A consent to extend probation merely continued a defendant's status on probation, and, should the defendant eventually be faced with revocation proceedings, he would then be entitled to the limited due process requirements attendant to that procedure. Due process did not require that a defendant be advised of, or receive counsel, before requesting an extension of probation and waiving a hearing. There was no Sixth Amendment right to counsel at this stage in the process.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. VanMatre


Court of Appeals No. 05CA2386


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


190 P.3d 770; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 157



February 7, 2008, Decided 
September 1, 2008, Released for Publication


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Van Matre v. People, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 972 (Colo., Aug. 4, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Weld County District Court No. 04CR301. Honorable James Hartmann, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Weld County District Court (Colorado) convicting him of aggravated driving with a revoked license in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 42-2-206(1)(b) (2007), driving under the influence (DUI) in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 42-4-1301(1)(b) (2007), and driving without insurance and sentencing him to three years in community corrections.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted after a trooper observed him drinking a can of beer in a parked car and attempting to start the car once he saw the trooper. On appeal, the court held that even though the trial court did not instruct the jury that it had to find that the vehicle was reasonably capable of being rendered operable, it did not err because there was undisputed testimony that the vehicle's alleged inoperability was a result only of a lack of fuel and a dead battery. These circumstances, as a matter of law, did not render a vehicle not reasonably capable of being rendered operable. Because defendant did not raise the constitutionality of Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 42-2-206(1)(b), 42-4-1301(1)(b) (2007), before the trial court, the court did not consider the issue on appeal. The court held that the trial court did not violate his right to due process in imposing an aggravated sentence of three years based on his five prior misdemeanor DUI convictions because a sentencing court could aggravated a sentence based on prior misdemeanor convictions pursuant to the prior conviction exception set forth in Blakely.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentence were affirmed.

Lobato v. People


Court of Appeals No. 06CA0733


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


216 P.3d 29; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 69



January 24, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 2, 2009.
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part Lobato v. State, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 898 (Colo., Sept. 15, 2008)
Reversed by, Remanded by Lobato v. State, 218 P.3d 358, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 998 (Colo., Oct. 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 05CV4794. Honorable Michael A. Martinez, Judge.
Lobato v. State, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 850 (Colo., Oct. 23, 2006)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, parents and school districts, brought an action against defendants, the State and others, that questioned the adequacy of Colorado's school finance system under the state constitution. Defendants moved to dismiss the complaint under Colo. R. Civ. P. 12(b)(1) and 12(b)(5). The City and County of Denver District Court, Colorado, dismissed the complaint for lack of standing and failure to state a claim. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The districts contended that the trial court erred when it concluded that, as political subdivisions, they lacked standing. The court found that the districts were properly dismissed for lack of standing because the Local Control Clause, Colo. Const. art. IX, § 15, did not give them authority to challenge how the Colorado General Assembly appropriated state funds to finance education. The parents had standing. The parents' claims were properly dismissed as a nonjusticiable political question because (1) the fashioning of a constitutional system for financing elementary and secondary public education in Colorado was not only the proper function of the Assembly, but this function was expressly mandated by the constitution; (2) the contours of a "quality" public education could not have been ascertained by judicially discoverable or manageable standards because the Education Clause, Colo. Const. art. IX, § 2, provided no principled basis for a judicial definition; and (3) finding and enforcing the parents' standard of a constitutionally adequate, quality public education presented a substantial risk of judicial intrusion into the powers and responsibilities of the Assembly.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Davis


Court of Appeals No. 05CA2665


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


182 P.3d 703; 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 6

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
El Paso County District Court No. 92CR3736. Honorable David L. Shakes, Judge.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: According to the mittimus imposing a prison term on defendant for his criminal conviction in the El Paso County District Court (Colorado), no restitution was ordered. The mittimus was not revised to reflect a later restitution order. However, the state department of corrections (DOC) began garnishing defendant's inmate account. The court denied defendant's motion for an order to show cause why the DOC had begun garnishment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's motion sought only to compel the DOC to show why it was garnishing defendant's account. The trial court ruled that the motion was without merit because the file contained the restitution order. On appeal, defendant contended that the restitution order increased his sentence after he had begun to serve it and, thus, violated double jeopardy principles and that the trial court violated his due process right to be present at sentencing when it entered the restitution order in his absence. The appellate court did not reach the merits of defendant's claims. According to the appellate court, (1) because defendant's challenges were to the constitutionality of his sentence, he should have filed a timely motion under Colo. R. Crim. P. 35; (2) nothing in the record showed that the trial court treated defendant's motion as having been filed under Colo. R. Crim. P. 35, as the trial court ruled only that there was no merit to the show cause motion and did not rule on any substantive claim regarding the propriety of the restitution order; and (3) accordingly, the motion was not a substantive postconviction motion and the order denying it was not a final appealable order.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed. The case was remanded for correction of the mittimus to reflect the restitution order.

People v. Valdez


Court of Appeals No.: 06CA0103


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


178 P.3d 1269; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 2493



December 27, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Valdez, 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 183 (Colo. Ct. App., Feb. 7, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 91CR3155. Honorable Robert L. McGahey, Jr., Judge.
People v. Valdez, 874 P.2d 415, 1993 Colo. App. LEXIS 272 (Colo. Ct. App., 1993)



DISPOSITION: ORDER VACATED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) denying his Colo. R. Crim. P. 35 request for postconviction relief from his convictions and sentence for three counts of sexual assault on a child (pattern of conduct) and three counts of sexual assault on a child (position of trust).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in 1992. In 1997, defendant was assigned a public defender to assist him in filing his postconviction petition. In 2004, the public defender filed a supplemental motion. The trial court held that the doctrine of laches applied and therefore dismissed defendant's petition due to the seven-year delay between defendant's letter seeking relief and the filing of the supplemental motion. On appeal, the court held that the doctrine of laches applied to defendant's case, as his letter was timely filed under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-5-402. Even though the trial court did not abuse its discretion by finding that the elements of laches had been satisfied, the court held that the ineffective assistance of the public defender, by failing to supplement the original Rule 35 motion for seven years, constituted excuse or excusable neglect. Because the court was unable to determine with particularity whether defendant acceded to the delay and waived his right to effective assistance of counsel, the case was remanded for a hearing.


OUTCOME: The order was vacated and the case was remanded to the trial court to conduct a hearing to determine whether defendant abandoned his claims or voluntarily waived his right to the effective assistance of counsel.

 

492 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Butler v. Lembeck


Court of Appeals No. 06CA1446


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


182 P.3d 1185; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 2376



December 13, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Jefferson County District Court No. 05CV2692. Honorable Christopher J. Munch, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowner sued appellee tenants after they moved out, alleging that they breached the parties' lease agreement by failing to pay rent and utilities and caused considerable damage to the property. The Jefferson County District Court, Colorado, awarded the homeowner damages, but denied her request for attorney fees and prejudgment and postjudgment interest. The homeowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the homeowner contended the trial court erred in failing to award her reasonable attorney fees based upon a fee-shifting provision in the lease. The appellate court agreed, finding first that contrary to the trial court's determination, the attorney fees in this case were not part of the substance of the homeowner's breach of contract action against the tenants, nor were they sought as a legitimate consequence of that breach of contract. Further, the fee-shifting provision at issue was valid: the fees sought by the homeowner were based on the work performed during the underlying litigation; and the homeowner was "required" to initiate legal action against the tenants to obtain the relief she sought because the tenants denied that they were liable to her for the asserted damages. It was also indisputable that the homeowner was the prevailing party, as evidenced by the jury verdict. Nor was the attorney fee provision at issue a penalty and therefore void, as argued by the tenants. The trial court also erred in failing to address the homeowner's request for prejudgment and postjudgment interest, pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 5-12-102 (2007).


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Campbell


Court of Appeals No. 06CA0582


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


174 P.3d 860; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 2299



November 29, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Mesa County District Court No. 04CR994. Honorable Amanda D. Bailey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A few months after entering a plea agreement, the Mesa County District Court (Colorado) revoked appellant inmate's probation for retaliating against the victim and resentenced him to concurrent terms of one and two years in the Colorado Department of Corrections (DOC) for the felony menacing and criminal extortion counts, and one year in jail on the failure to leave the premises count. His motion for postconviction relief was denied. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was involved in an altercation with his live-in girlfriend, the victim. He pointed a gun at the victim and ordered her to undress. The victim responded by saying, effectively, that she would rather be dead. He then fired a shot next to her. Accepting the inmate's plea when the criminal complaint did not include an annotation indicating that the underlying factual basis for the charges involved an act of domestic violence or, in the alternative, requiring the prosecutor to represent that he or she could not make a prima facie case on the original charge, was a violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6-801(3) (2007). However, because there was no dispute that the underlying factual basis included an act of domestic violence and the inmate was appropriately advised concerning the nature and consequences of his plea such that the placement of a domestic violence designation on the complaint would not alter his understanding of the agreement, the appropriate remedy for the trial court's technical violation of § 18-6-801(3) was to remand the case to allow the prosecution to amend the complaint to include a domestic violence designation.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's order denying the inmate's motion for postconviction relief, but remanded the case to the trial court to allow the district attorney to amend the complaint to comply with Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-21-103(2)(b)(II) (2007).

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Larimer County District Court (Colorado) convicting him of two counts of sexual assault on a child.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for sexually assaulting the victims, his six and seven-year-old nieces. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's challenge to a prospective juror for cause on the ground that the juror had previously worked for a victim advocacy organization because the record indicated that she was not a compensated employee of a public law enforcement agency under Colo. People v. Heimann


Court of Appeals No. 06CA0662


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION A


186 P.3d 77; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 2300



November 29, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Heimann v. People, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 674 (Colo., June 23, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Adams County District Court No. 04CR3158. Honorable Katherine R. Delgado, Judge.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Adams County District Court (Colorado), which revoked his probation and sentenced him to prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a guilty plea to a felony sexual offense. He was given probation, but later violated the terms of such by drinking alcohol and staying out past his curfew. Defendant admitted the violations and requested a community corrections placement. The trial court accepted defendant's admission and imposed a sentence of 4 years in prison. This appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the five day time limitation in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-11-206(5) was not jurisdictional in nature because time was not of the essence, there was no negative language denying the exercise of authority beyond that time, and there was no injury to public or private rights. Further, defendant consented to a hearing outside of the relevant time period. Next, there was no viable Blakely challenge because the trial court unmistakably identified defendant's prior felony conviction as a basis for imposing an aggravated range sentence. Defendant's 4-year sentence was within the range authorized under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1.3-401(1)(a)(V)(A), (6) and Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-405.3(1) (2007), and the trial court considered the appropriate factors during sentencing.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

People v. Guatney


Court of Appeals No. 06CA0704


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


183 P.3d 620; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 2094



November 1, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 30, 2008
Opinion Modified and Petition for Rehearing Denied December 13, 2007.
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part People v. Guatney, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 567 (Colo., May 27, 2008)
Vacated by People v. Guatney, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 591 (Colo., June 29, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Arapahoe County District Court No. 03CR2363. Honorable Nancy A. Hopf, Judge.
People v. Guatney, 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1331 (Colo. Ct. App., Aug. 17, 2006)



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: While defendant's appeal was pending from his attempted sexual assault on a child convictions, he received sex offender intensive supervision probation. After defendant refused to admit to any guilt in conjunction with the crimes for which he was convicted, his therapist recommended that the treatment program be terminated. The Arapahoe County District Court, Colorado, denied the State's request to revoke probation. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the State contended defendant's probation should have been revoked as he refused to admit guilt to any of the crimes for which he was convicted, contrary to the rules of the treatment program. The appellate court disagreed, finding that defendant had a reasonable fear of prosecution sufficient to pass constitutional muster concerning any admission to his therapist because the admission could have been used against him on retrial. In addition, he could have been subjected to charges of perjury because he had testified and denied the charges at trial. Hence defendant validly invoked his right against self-incrimination. Because of these circumstances, the State could not revoke defendant's probation and sentence him to imprisonment for an indeterminate term for, as a maximum, the duration of his life, based on defendant's invocation of his U.S. Const. amend. V right to remain silent. Defendant faced the "classic penalty situation" that the Fifth Amendment was designed to prohibit. Furthermore, defendant was in compliance with every other condition of probation except as related to an admission that he committed the acts for which he was convicted.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

497 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Alliance for Colorado's Families v. Gilbert


Court of Appeals No. 05CA2137


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


172 P.3d 964; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 2096



November 1, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Division of Administrative Hearings No. OS-2005-0006.



DISPOSITION: ORDER VACATED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner association challenged a decision from the Colorado Division of Administrative Hearings, which assessed a penalty against it in a case involving an alleged violation of Colorado's campaign finance law. Respondent objector also appealed the method of calculating the penalty assessed.


OVERVIEW: The association paid for an advertisement regarding a political candidate. The objector contended that this violated Colo. Const. art. XXVIII. After it was determined that the payment and sponsorship of the advertisement transformed the association into a "political committee" under Colo. Const. art. XXVIII, § 2(12)(a), a penalty was imposed. The association contended that its rights under the First and Fourteenth Amendments were violated. Both parties sought review. In reversing, the appellate court determined that the fact that the association's activities here involved expenditures, rather that contributions, meant that the restrictions upon it were subject to strict scrutiny. The construction of the term "political committee" as applied to a non-candidate organization was known as the "major purpose" test under the Buckley case. This test was not included in the definition of "political committee" under § 2(12)(a). A remand was necessary because, unlike the federal decision in Colorado Right to Life Committee, Inc., this record did not permit the appellate court to determine whether the "major purpose" test required by Buckley had been satisfied as to the association.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed, the penalty was vacated, and the case was remanded to an administrative law judge (ALJ) for further proceedings as guided by the federal decision. The ALJ was directed to determine if the association's "major purpose" was the nomination or election of candidates. It was also directed to make findings as to whether the association was a "political committee" and any other necessary findings.

Court of Appeals No. 04CA0514


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


178 P.3d 1225; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 1949

October 1, 2008, Released for Publication


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Baker, 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 363 (Colo. Ct. App., Mar. 6, 2008)
Writ of certiorari denied Baker v. People, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 934 (Colo., Sept. 2, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Baker, 2011 Colo. App. LEXIS 2067 (Colo. Ct. App., Dec. 15, 2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied, Dismissed by Baker v. Archuleta, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 46745 (D. Colo., Apr. 4, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Jefferson County District Court No. 01 CR480. Honorable Jack W. Berryhill, Judge.
People v. Baker, 104 P.3d 893, 2005 Colo. LEXIS 31 (Colo., 2005)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Jefferson County District Court, Colorado, which convicted him after a jury trial of extreme indifference first degree assault, second degree kidnapping, and five counts of sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his conviction for extreme indifference first degree assault had to be vacated because extreme indifference assault required proof of universal malice against human life generally, and not conduct directed against a single individual, and that his conduct was directed at a single individual. The instant court concluded that a finding of universal malice was not required to convict defendant of extreme indifference first degree assault under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-202 (2007). The trial court did not err when it admitted evidence that, seven years before the sexual assault charged in this case, defendant committed a sexual assault on a different victim in New Mexico, nor did it err when found the assault on the New Mexico victim occurred without providing defendant an opportunity to cross-examine her. However, the jury's finding of a class three felony aggravator had to be vacated because the evidence did not establish that defendant caused the submission of the victim by threatening to retaliate in the future against her.


OUTCOME: The jury's finding of the class three felony aggravator under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-402(4)(c) (2007), as to one sexual assault count was vacated, but the judgment and sentence were affirmed in all other respects.

People v. Richardson


Court of Appeals No. 04CA2121


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


181 P.3d 340; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 1852



September 20, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Richardson v. People, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 441 (Colo., Apr. 28, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Richardson, 2012 Colo. App. LEXIS 200 (Colo. Ct. App., Feb. 2, 2012)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, in part, Claim dismissed by Richardson v. Ploughe, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 142986 (D. Colo., Oct. 2, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Park County District Court No. 03CR47. Honorable Kenneth M. Plotz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Park County District Court (Colorado) convicting him of forgery, possession of forgery devices, wrongful possession of a journal or seal, violation of a restraining order, harassment by stalking, and offering a false instrument for recording.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for filing 13 lawsuits against the victim in violation of restraining orders that prohibited him from contacting her. On appeal, the court rejected defendant's facial challenges to the stalking statute, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-9-11(4)(b)(III) (2007), because the Supreme Court of Colorado had already held that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutionally overbroad as applied to him. Because the constitutional right to access to the courts did not encompass the right to file lawsuits abusively in a manner designed to deprive another of effective access to the courts in his or her own defense, defendant's activity of intentionally filing lawsuits without notice to the victim, with the intention to use them to harass her and cause her serious emotional distress, was not constitutionally protected. The county in which defendant was tried was the proper venue to prosecute the possession of forgery devices and possession of a journal or seal charges, even though the computer disks on which those charges were based were seized from defendant's home in another county.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

In re N.B.


Court of Appeals No. 06CA1325


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SIX


199 P.3d 16; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 1758



September 6, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 30, 2009.
Rehearing denied by In re N.B., 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 1991 (Colo. Ct. App., Oct. 11, 2007)
Writ of certiorari denied N.B. v. L.W.-E, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 320 (Colo., Mar. 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Jefferson County District Court No. 04JA42. Honorable Brian D. Boatright, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant stepmother challenged a judgment of the Jefferson County District Court (Colorado), which dismissed her petition to terminate the parental rights of appellee mother and to allow the stepmother to adopt the child in question, who was an Indian child.


OVERVIEW: The child was in his father's primary care since birth. Three years after the child's birth, the mother moved out of state. She saw the child only three times over the next three years and offered no support. The child believed that the stepmother was his biological mother. Neither the stepmother nor father corrected that belief. The stepmother petitioned to terminate the mother's parental rights and to adopt the child on grounds of abandonment. The trial court denied the requested relief. Affirming, the court held that the petition failed because the child was an Indian child who was subject to the provisions of the Indian Child Welfare Act of 1978 (ICWA), 25 U.S.C.S. § 1901 et seq., and the stepmother did not prove that active efforts were made to prevent the breakup of the Indian family as required by 25 U.S.C.S. § 1912(d). The court held that the ICWA applied in stepparent adoptions and in situations where the child would remain with one biological parent after the adoption because any action resulting in the termination of the parent-child relationship and in a final decree of adoption was considered a "child custody proceeding" under the ICWA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Lovato


Court of Appeals No. 04CA1177


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SIX


179 P.3d 208; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 1514



August 9, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Lovato v. People, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 269 (Colo., Mar. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Jefferson County District Court No. 03CR1370. Honorable Stephen M. Munsinger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Jefferson County District Court (Colorado) of robbery of an at-risk adult, aggravated robbery, and negligent bodily injury to an at-risk adult. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected defendant's argument that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6.5-103(2) (2006) created a sentence enhancer and not a substantive offense. Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6.5-103(2) did not merely incorporate the elements of another offense. Instead, it combined several elements to create a separate substantive offense. Defendant's vagueness challenge to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6.5-103(2)(c) also failed. Although broad, the statute was not so vague that persons of common intelligence must necessarily guess at its meaning. Additionally, any error in the jury instruction was harmless, as the error benefitted defendant by imposing a more demanding standard of culpability than the statutory standard. Further, defendant's convictions for aggravated robbery and criminally negligent bodily injury to an at-risk adult were not legally and logically inconsistent. However, defendant's conviction for robbery of an at-risk adult had to be vacated because it merged with her conviction for aggravated robbery under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-4-302(1)(c) (2006). Robbery of an at-risk adult was an enhanced form of robbery and not a separate offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated as to the conviction for robbery of an at-risk adult, and the case was remanded for correction of the mittimus as to that conviction. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

Garhart v. Columbia/HealthONE, L.L.C.


Court of Appeals No. 05CA1725


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


168 P.3d 512; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 1395



July 26, 2007, Decided 
September 27, 2007, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Adams County District Court No. 98CV2973. Honorable Chris Melonakis, Judge.
Garhart v. Columbia/Healthone. L.L.C., 95 P.3d 571, 2004 Colo. LEXIS 528 (Colo., 2004)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant hospital challenged a decision from the Adams County District Court (Colorado), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiff patient by requiring the hospital to purchase annuity contracts funded with the full amount of a jury award in a medical malpractice case.


OVERVIEW: The patient suffered from injuries that occurred during his birth. A verdict was entered in favor of the patient, but this amount was reduced under the Colorado Health Care Availability Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-64-101 et seq. (2006). The hospital proposed funding an annuity at an even lower amount, but the trial court rejected this argument. The hospital then sought review. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the trial court had the discretion to order the form and distribution of periodic payments under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-64-207(1) (2006). The hospital's reliance on Cal. Code Civ. Rev. Stat. § 13-64-205(1)(d) (2006). The trial court was not allowed to inquire into the deliberative process of the jury under Colo. R. Evid. 606(b). Finally, attorney fees under Colo. App. R. 38(d) were not awarded because the appeal was not frivolous in nature since an interpretation of the HCAA was proposed using California law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People ex rel. J.C.S.


Court of Appeals No. 06CA1868


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


169 P.3d 240; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 1308



July 12, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Huerfano County District Court No. 04JV29. Honorable Claude W. Appel, Judge.
People ex rel. J.C.S., 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 1325 (Colo. Ct. App., July 12, 2007)



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In this dependency and neglect proceeding initiated by the Huerfano County Department of Social Services, the Huerfano County District Court, Colorado, entered an adjudicatory order and subsequent judgment terminating appellant mother's parent-child legal relationship with her child. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that the statute authorizing service by single publication, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-3-502(8)(b) (2006), was unconstitutional on its face and as applied because it did not provide her with actual notice of her legal rights before she lost custody of her child through adjudication. The appellate court rejected these arguments because any lack of notice which caused the mother to lose custody of the child resulted from her actions in concealing herself from law enforcement, the trial court, and the department during the adjudicatory phase. Further, the mother did not prove the statute was unconstitutional as applied because she did not show that the department did not exercise due diligence in trying to find her, at least before the trial court adjudicated the child, if not earlier. Based on these findings, which encompassed the four months between service by publication and the adjudication, the appellate court concluded that the mother lacked standing to raise a due process challenge to the statute because her claimed injury was self-inflicted. Since standing was jurisdictional, inquiry into the merits of the mother's due process arguments was foreclosed.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Colo. Cmty. Health Network v. Colo. Gen. Assembly


Court of Appeals No. 05CA2577


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


166 P.3d 280; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 1113



June 14, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court No. 04CV9720. Honorable H. Jeffrey Bayless, Judge.
Colo. Cmty. Health Network v. Colo. Gen. Assembly, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 133 (Colo., Feb. 13, 2006)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from the judgment of the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) in favor of defendants, the Colorado General Assembly, the Governor of Colorado, and the Colorado State Controller, upholding the constitutionality of H.B. 04-1455 (Colo. 2005).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs alleged that H.B. 04-1455 (Colo. 2005) was unconstitutional because it conflicted with Amendment 35 to the Colorado Constitution and violated the initiative power of the citizens of Colorado pursuant to Colo. Const. art. V, § 1. Contrary to plaintiffs' argument, there was nothing in Amendment 35 mandating a certain level of funding for health-related purposes. Although Amendment 35 provided that the revenues generated from it would be used to "expand" and "increase" health-related programs and services, it did not restrict the General Assembly's ability to change the amount of appropriations for health-related purposes with respect to other existing sources of revenue. Therefore, the General Assembly could set the appropriations at zero. Additionally, the court disagreed that Colo. Const. art. V, § 1 was violated. H.B. 04-1455 (Colo. 2005) did not impose restrictions that limit in any way the right of the citizens to initiate proposed amendments. Indeed, it did not even pertain to the initiative process.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

Kenna v. Huber


Court of Appeals No. 06CA0608


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


179 P.3d 189; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 1114



June 14, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 2, 2009.
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part Huber v. Kenna, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 93 (Colo., Jan. 22, 2008)
Reversed by, Remanded by Huber v. Kenna, 2009 Colo. LEXIS 412 (Colo., Apr. 20, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
La Plata County District Court No. 05CV119. Honorable David L. Dickinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT VACATED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed a determination of the Colorado Department of Revenue with regard to a state tax assessment. The La Plata County District Court (Colorado) granted summary judgment in favor of the taxpayers. Defendant, the Department's executive director, sought review.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers, two married couples, owned property as tenants in common. In January 2000, they donated a conservation easement on the property. Pursuant to a provision of the Conservation Easement Tax Credit Act then in effect, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 39-22-522(2) (1999), the couples split the market value of the easement ($154,700) and each took a tax credit of $77,350. In 2000 and 2001, the couples received tax credits and refunds for the conservation easement. However, in 2002, the Department promulgated a regulation, 1 Colo. Code Regs. § 201-2, which limited to $100,000 the total credit generated by the donation of a perpetual conservation easement in gross by tenants in common. Relying on this, the Department issued notices of deficiency to recoup the credits and refunds. The court held that the 1999 version of § 39-22-522(2), unlike an amended 2006 version, did not require tenants in common to split a conservation easement tax credit, and that the Department's attempt to alter the meaning of § 39-22-522 by regulation was void. However, the court was unable to determine whether the 2006 version was retroactive, and, if so, whether its application would be unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was vacated and the case was remanded for determination whether the 2006 amendment applied retroactively.

Skyland Metro. Dist. v. Mt. West Enter., LLC


Court of Appeals No. 04CA2605


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


184 P.3d 106; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 1118



June 14, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Gunnison County District Court No. 02CV97. Honorable Charles R. Greenacre, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff special districts sued defendant developers, seeking to enforce statutory liens against the developers' property for failure to pay fees under the Special District Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 32-1-101 et seq. (2006). The Gunnison County District Court (Colorado) entered judgment enforcing the liens, dismissed the developers' counterclaims, and awarded attorney fees to the districts. The parties cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The districts brought in rem claims to foreclose liens as a result of the developers' failure to pay availability of service or facilities fees (ASF). The developers asserted counterclaims based on alleged overpayments of ASF and other fees made by them and previous owners. The appellate court determined that the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction because the service of the notice of intent was unnecessary to preserve the districts' liens because the liens were perpetual and perfected under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 32-1-1001(1)(j)(I) (2006). No ASF were owed to one of the districts for 2002 and 2003, because the district's lease purchase agreement could not properly be used to calculate ASF, since it was not indebtedness within the meaning of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 32-1-1006(1)(h)(I)(C) and (E) (2006). The trial court correctly determined that ASF were limited to budgeted debt service less the amount budgeted and expected to be produced by the mill levy allocable to such debt service as certified to the county by the districts. Also, the trial court erred in ruling that the districts were required to use amended budgets to calculate ASF. Certain counterclaims were untimely.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed that aspect of the judgment in favor of the districts, foreclosing their liens on their claim for unpaid availability of service or facilities fees, late fees, and attorney fees, and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings. The appellate court affirmed the judgment in all other respects.

 

507 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Trujillo


Court of Appeals No. 05CA1389


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO


169 P.3d 235; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 1031



May 31, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Trujillo, 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 1067 (Colo. Ct. App., May 31, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Trujillo v. Colorado, 128 S. Ct. 123, 169 L. Ed. 2d 86, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 9420 (U.S., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court. No. 00CR2436. Honorable Shelley I. Gilman, Judge. Honorable Larry J. Naves, Judge. Prior Opinion Announced April 19, 2007 WITHDRAWN. Petition for Rehearing GRANTED.
People v. Trujillo, 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 718 (Colo. Ct. App., Apr. 19, 2007)



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED IN PART AND ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a postconviction motion claiming that his aggravated range sentence was unconstitutionally imposed and that his appellate counsel provided ineffective assistance. The City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) denied his motion. Defendant appealed. Defendant also filed a supplemental postconviction motion alleging ineffective assistance of trial counsel.


OVERVIEW: Because defendant's supplemental postconviction motion had not been ruled upon at the time defendant filed his notice of appeal, the court declined to address it. Defendant was convicted of first degree assault under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-202(1)(a) (2006). That was a class three felony that was a per se crime of violence and an extraordinary risk crime. It therefore triggerred a special penalty range of 10 to 32 years. Defendant's sentence was within the special penalty range defined by the legislature. It therefore did not violate Apprendi or Blakely. The court also concluded that the district court correctly denied defendant's claims of ineffective assistance of appellate counsel. Because defendant failed to allege that the potential appellate issues were stronger or had a better chance of prevailing than the confrontation and insufficiency of evidence claims which appellate counsel raised in the direct appeal, the district court was correct in denying defendant's motion without a hearing. The bare allegation of failure to assert the additional claims did not overcome the presumption that appellate counsel's choice was the result of a strategic election.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed as to defendant's supplemental postconviction motion, and the order was affirmed.

 

508 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. McGlotten


Court of Appeals No.: 02CA1014


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


166 P.3d 182; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 820; 38 A.L.R.6th 695



May 3, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. McGlotten, 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 1213 (Colo. Ct. App., June 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Arapahoe County District Court. No. 00CR2666. Honorable Frederick B. Skillern, Judge. Honorable Anthony F. Vollack, Judge.
People v. McGlotten, 134 P.3d 487, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1947 (Colo. Ct. App., 2005)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Arapahoe County District Court, Colorado, convicting him of racketeering activity under the Colorado Organized Crime Control Act (COCCA), Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-17-101 et seq. (2006), two counts of conspiracy to commit first degree murder, attempted manslaughter, prohibited use of weapons, false imprisonment, felony menacing, conspiracy to distribute a controlled substance, and first degree criminal trespass.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his convictions should be reversed because he was deprived of his due process right to a meaningful and speedy appeal. The appellate court agreed. Defendant filed a notice of appeal in May 2002, and the five-year delay was clearly excessive and inordinate. Delays in the preparation of transcripts were generally attributable to the government, and it was generally appropriate to view defendant's filing of a notice of appeal as an assertion of the right to a speedy appeal. It was no longer possible to obtain a reliable answer to the factual questions presented. The witnesses on remand were unable to recall the pertinent events with any degree of specificity or certainty, and there was no reason to think that still further efforts toward reconstruction would be productive. Since the appellate court could not evaluate defendant's substantive contention, the appellate court found that he has been prejudiced by appellate delay and defendant was entitled to a new trial. Also, the COCCA was not so vague that persons of common intelligence must necessarily guess at its meaning.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded with directions.

 

509 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Trujillo


Court of Appeals No. 05CA1389


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SIX


2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 718



April 19, 2007, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION IS NOT THE FINAL VERSION AND IS SUBJECT TO REVISION UPON FINAL PUBLICATION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, On rehearing at, Appeal dismissed by, in part People v. Trujillo, 169 P.3d 235, 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 1031 (Colo. Ct. App., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court. No. 00CR2436. Honorable Shelley I. Gilman, Judge, Honorable Larry J. Naves, Judge.
People v. Trujillo, 2003 Colo. App. LEXIS 1616 (Colo. Ct. App., Oct. 16, 2003)



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED IN PART, ORDER AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) of first degree assault, among other crimes. Defendant filed a postconviction motion claiming that his aggravated range sentence was unconstitutionally imposed and that his appellate counsel provided ineffective assistance for, inter alia, not timely seeking a Colo. R. Crim. P. 35 sentence reduction. The trial court denied defendant's motion and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to concurrent prison terms of 32 years for first degree assault, 24 years for attempted murder, and 18 months for tampering with physical evidence. Defendant argued that he was entitled to relief under Apprendi and Blakely. Defendant did not receive an aggravated range sentence. First degree assault was a class three felony and a per se crime of violence and an extraordinary risk crime. It therefore triggered a special penalty range of ten to thirty-two years under the combined operation of four related statutes. Defendant's thirty-two-year sentence lay within the special penalty range defined by the legislature. It therefore did not violate Apprendi and Blakely. The appellate court also concluded that the trial court correctly denied all but one of defendant's claims of ineffective assistance of appellate counsel. Defendant sufficiently stated a claim that appellate counsel provided ineffective assistance in not timely seeking a reduction of his sentence pursuant to Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(b). Thus, defendant was entitled to a hearing on his claim that counsel disregarded his timely instruction to seek sentence reconsideration.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was reversed as to the ineffective assistance claim concerning sentence reconsideration, and the case was remanded for further proceedings on that claim. The order was affirmed in all other respects. The part of defendant's appeal concerning the supplemental claims was dismissed.

People v. Welsh


Court of Appeals No. 04CA2581


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


176 P.3d 781; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 608



April 5, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Welsh, 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 989 (Colo. Ct. App., May 24, 2007)
Writ of certiorari denied People v. Welsh, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 137 (Colo., Feb. 4, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: El Paso County District Court No. 97CR205. Honorable Gilbert A. Martinez, Judge.
People v. Welsh, 80 P.3d 296, 2003 Colo. LEXIS 961 (Colo., 2003)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, CROSS-APPEAL DISMISSED IN PART, AND RULING APPROVED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the El Paso County District Court (Colorado), where she was convicted on a jury verdict finding her guilty of first degree murder. The People cross-appealed under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-12-102(1) (2006), challenging two evidentiary rulings made by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed her boyfriend after he attempted to end their relationship. She was charged with first degree murder and pled not guilty by reason of insanity. Her conviction was reversed on appeal. On retrial, the jury again rejected defendant's insanity defense and found her guilty of first degree murder. The appellate court concluded that defendant's contentions of error regarding jury instructions, prosecutorial misconduct, expert testimony, and hearsay evidence, whether considered singly or cumulatively, did not warrant reversal. The people cross-appealed regarding whether, inter alia, a 911 call was testimonial and had to be decided on a case-by-case basis, considering, for example, whether the call was made for the purpose of getting help or to provide information for investigative purposes. On appeal, however, the People made only conclusory statements regarding this inquiry, without specific citation to the record, beyond a reference to the tape itself, to support their statements. In these circumstances, the appellate court declined to disapprove the district court's ruling, and, instead, dismissed the cross-appeal as to this contention.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment of conviction was affirmed. The cross-appeal was dismissed as to the ruling on the 911 call evidence, and the district court's ruling on the sanity examination evidence was approved.

 

511 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Stanley


Court of Appeals No. 04CA2164


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


170 P.3d 782; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 609



April 5, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Rehearing denied by People v. Stanley, 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 1100 (Colo. Ct. App., June 14, 2007)
Writ of certiorari denied Stanley v. People, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 1088 (Colo., Nov. 19, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Stanley v. Colorado, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 3003 (U.S., Mar. 31, 2008)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Adams County District Court (Colorado) where he was convicted of two counts of attempting to influence a public official. Defendant claimed, among other things, that the statute he was convicted of violating, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-8-306 (2006), was applied to him in violation of his right to freedom of speech under the First Amendment to the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: After his conviction, defendant sent "notices" expressly threatened two judges with "arrest" by a militia, an act in which the prospect of physical violence was inherent. They also threatened a "charge" of treason, an offense punishable by death. Defendant argued that § 18-8-306 was unconstitutionally overbroad because his statements did not constitute "true threats." While the appellate court agreed that the threats of violence prohibited by § 18-8-306 were limited to "true threats," it disagreed with defendant's contention that the People did not prove that his statements constituted true threats because the appellate court rejected defendant's argument that the First Amendment required the People to prove that he subjectively intended to threaten the judges. There was also no case law holding that a criminal defendant had a First Amendment privilege to threaten violence against a judge if he did so in the context of a pro se court proceeding. Finally, a reasonable juror could find, based on the evidence submitted, that the notices contained true threats, whether viewed from the perspective of a reasonable speaker or a reasonable recipient.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the district court's judgment of conviction.

 

512 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Brighton Pharm., Inc. v. Colo. State Pharm. Bd.


Court of Appeals No. 05CA2358


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


160 P.3d 412; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 611



April 5, 2007, Announced


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Colorado State Pharmacy Board No. 3.00.21.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a pharmacy and a pharmacist, sought review of the rulemaking action of the Colorado State Pharmacy Board (Board) following which it promulgated Colo. Dep't Reg. Agencies Regs. No. 3.00.21, 3 Colo. Code Regs. § 719-1 (rule). The case implicated the Colorado Administrative Procedure Act (APA), Colo. Rev. Stat. § 24-4-101 et seq. (2006).


OVERVIEW: The Board held a rulemaking hearing to consider a rule prohibiting pharmacists from dispensing prescription drugs resulting from Internet-based questionnaires, Internet-based consultation, or a telephonic consultation without a valid preexisting patient-practitioner relationship. The court first concluded that the agency substantially complied with the APA requirement of providing a statement of basis and purpose. The pharmacy and pharmacist next asserted that the Board had not maintained an adequate and appropriate record of the rulemaking hearing proceeding. However, the appellate court disagreed. The hearing was tape recorded and subsequently transcribed. The transcript contained numerous omissions, but the substance of and core testimony at the hearing appeared to be intact and was sufficient for public inspection and appellate review. Therefore, the appellate court concluded that the Board substantially complied with APA rulemaking provisions. Finally, the appellate court was satisfied that the Board's regulation of the sale and dispensing of drugs in this manner did not exceed its statutory authority and the terms and phrases in the rule were not vague or ambiguous.


OUTCOME: The Board's order adopting Colo. Dep't Reg. Agencies Regs. No. 3.00.21, 3 Colo. Code Regs. § 719-1 was affirmed.

 

513 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Valencia


Court of Appeals No. 05CA0572


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SIX


169 P.3d 212; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 613



April 5, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Writ of certiorari denied Valencia v. People, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 890 (Colo., Oct. 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Washington County District Court. No. 03CR25. Honorable Steven E. Shinn, Judge. Honorable Douglas R. Vannoy, Judge.
State v. Jackson, 596 N.W.2d 262, 1999 Minn. App. LEXIS 660 (1999)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's motion to suppress was denied, he was convicted of possession of marihuana with intent to distribute and possession of eight ounces or more of marihuana, in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-18-406(4)(b)(I) and (8)(b)(I) (2006). The Washington County District Court (Colorado) adjudicated and sentenced defendant as a habitual criminal pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1.3-803(1) (2006). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a passenger in his car when it was stopped. When defendant and the driver provided inconsistent answers to two troopers, the troopers questioned them again and asked for permission to search the vehicle, which defendant granted. The appellate court determined that defendant's motion to suppress was properly denied under the Fourth Amendment and Colo. Const. art. II, § 7 because the record supported the findings that, inter alia, (1) it was a consensual encounter at least until the troopers obtained reasonable suspicion, (2) only 15 minutes had elapsed between the stop and the consent, and (3) there was no coercive conduct. The trial court did not err in allowing the prosecution to use defendant's name and an alias, because the evidence was relevant under Colo. R. Evid. 401 to issues of identification, ownership of the car, and possession of the marihuana. Defendant's separate marihuana convictions were sustainable. A continuance of the habitual criminal hearing did not violate the statutory mandate of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1.3-803(1) to conduct the hearing "as soon as practicable" after trial and did not violate double jeopardy principles.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgments of conviction and sentences.

Avalanche Indus., Inc. v. Indus. Claim Appeals Office


Court of Appeals No. 06CA0716


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


166 P.3d 147; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 488



March 22, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Writ of certiorari granted Avalanche Indus. v. Indus. Claim Appeals Office, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 811 (Colo., Aug. 27, 2007)
Affirmed by Avalanche Indus. v. Clark, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 1742 (Colo., Dec. 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado WC No. 4-471-863.
Avalanche Indus., Inc. v. Indus. Claim Appeals Office, 2004 Colo. App. LEXIS 1966 (Colo. Ct. App., Oct. 28, 2004)



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a workers' compensation proceeding, petitioner employer and its insurers, sought review of a final order of respondent Industrial Claim Appeals Office (panel), which affirmed the order of the administrative law judge (ALJ) that the average weekly wage (AWW) of respondent claimant should be recalculated to reflect her higher earnings from a subsequent employer and to include the cost of her group health insurance.


OVERVIEW: The employer's argument, that it was denied its rights to equal protection and due process guaranteed by Colo. Const., art. II, § 25, failed. The due process clause did not guarantee a party an order setting out every finding on which the order was based, and the employer cited to no examples of the pertinent AWW statutes being applied to other employers with a different degree of severity. Additionally, because a reopening under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-43-303(1) reopened an "award" and not just specific issues raised by a claimant in a petition to reopen, the ALJ properly determined that claimant's entire award had been reopened and that claimant was entitled to seek an increase in her average weekly wage. Also, the ALJ did not abuse his discretion in determining that claimant's AWW should be calculated based upon her wages nearly five years after she initially sustained her injury because the calculation was a fair approximation of claimant's wage loss. Finally, the ALJ correctly determined that claimant's cost of continuing health insurance coverage should be included in her AWW despite her decision not to purchase continuing coverage from employer.


OUTCOME: The order of the panel was affirmed.

 

515 of 734 DOCUMENTS


JJR 1, LLC v. Mt. Crested Butte


Court of Appeals No. 05CA2553


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


160 P.3d 365; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 490



March 22, 2007, Announced


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Gunnison County District Court. No. 05CV101. Honorable J. Steven Patrick, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, property owners, appealed from the Gunnison County, Colorado, District Court which dismissed their Colo. R. Civ. P. 57, 106(a)(4) and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims against defendants, a town and a developer. The court held it lacked jurisdiction to hear the owners' state law claims. Regarding the owners' facial constitutional challenge and their § 1983 claim, the court determined that the owners did not have a protected property interest.


OVERVIEW: The owners were absentee owners of a property in the town containing three townhouses that had unobstructed mountain views. The developer filed an application with the town planning commission to develop a parcel of land adjacent to the owners' property. Because the owners' claims for declaratory relief under Colo. R. Civ. P. 57 that sought review of quasi-judicial decisions were untimely, there were properly dismissed. Although the owners' claim against the town for monetary damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 also sought review of quasi-judicial decisions, it requested a uniquely federal remedy and, therefore, was not subject to the filing deadline of Colo. R. Civ. P. 106(b). However, the owners pointed to no provision in the town zoning code, nor did the court find any, that forbade the elimination of scenic views or required the planning commission to deny building permit requests for structures that would adversely affect existing scenic views. Because the owners did not have any constitutionally recognized property interest in the preservation of scenic views, the owners also did not have a protected property interest in notice of and participation in the proposed design review.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court which granted judgment in favor of the town and the developer was affirmed.

 

516 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Barber v. Ritter


Court of Appeals No. 05CA0752


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


170 P.3d 763; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 480



March 22, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part Barber v. Ritter, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 1052 (Colo., Nov. 13, 2007)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Petitioners/Cross-Respondents: Barber v. Respondents/Cross-Petitioners: Bill Ritter, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 999 (Colo., Nov. 3, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court. No. 04CV6602. Honorable R. Michael Mullins, Judge.
Barber v. Owens, 2005 Colo. LEXIS 501 (Colo., May 23, 2005)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND ORDER AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff real estate broker, oil company owner, and paint company sued defendant Governor and State Treasurer, alleging that cash transfers from certain special funds violated the Taxpayer's Bill of Rights (TABOR), Colo. Const. art. X, § 20, and Colo. Const. art. XI, §§ 3-4. The City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) dismissed several claims and granted summary judgment in favor of defendants. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The individual claims of the broker and owner were moot as the funds at issue had either been abolished or the transfers had been repaid. Plaintiffs had standing to challenge the constitutionality of the cash fund transfers because they had an interest in having general tax dollars spent in compliance with TABOR and Colo. Const. art. XI, §§ 3 and 4. The paint company lacked standing to raise individual challenges as it did not pay the workers' compensation surcharges. The acts authorizing the transfers from the cash funds into the general fund did not violate TABOR as the transfers did not change the special funds into tax funds. The acts also did not violate Colo. Const. art. XI, §§ 3 and 4, because, with the exception of three funds expressly described as trusts, the cash funds were not public trusts. The legislature had the authority to transfer the special funds into the general fund as none of them were constitutionally created and thus, they were subject to the legislature's inherent power to alter or amend them. The transfers did not create debt as they did not pledge future revenues or revenues from taxes that were otherwise available for general purposes.


OUTCOME: The portion of the order concluding that plaintiffs lacked standing to bring their constitutional claims and granting defendants summary judgment as to the Colorado children's trust, the severance tax trust fund, and the unclaimed property trust fund was reversed. The case was remanded to reinstate the constitutional claims as to those three funds and for further proceedings. The judgment and order were otherwise affirmed.
