People v. Martinez


Court of Appeals No.: 05CA0096


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SIX


165 P.3d 907; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 388



March 8, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Writ of certiorari denied Martinez v. People, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 699 (Colo., Aug. 13, 2007)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Martinez v. Kurtz, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 129489 (D. Colo., Oct. 26, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Fremont County District Court No. 02CR260. Honorable Charles M. Barton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fremont County District Court (Colorado) denied defendant's motions to suppress and for acquittal. Defendant was convicted of sexual exploitation of children (possession of sexually exploitative materials) under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6-403(3)(b.5) (2006), unlawful manufacture of a schedule II controlled substance under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-18-405(1)(a) (2006), and unlawful possession of a schedule II controlled substance. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Based on allegations against defendant's father, officers executed a warrant to search his parents' home for child pornography, drugs, and firearms. The officers searched defendant's room, which he allegedly rented from his parents. The appellate court determined that the search of defendant's bedroom was reasonable under the Fourth Amendment and Colo. Const. art. II, § 7 because the facts known to the officers established that defendant's father, the person whose unlawful activities formed the basis for the search warrant, had ready access to defendant's bedroom. The special offender provision established by Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-18-407(1)(f) (2006), under which defendant was sentenced for the possession conviction, was not unconstitutionally overbroad as applied, because the handgun found in his bedroom appeared to be capable of firing a bullet. Sufficient evidence supported the manufacturing conviction because items indicative of a methamphetamine manufacturing operation were found. Sufficient evidence supported the sexual exploitation of children conviction because defendant used a computer that contained numerous images depicting children engaged in sexual conduct.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment and sentence.

 

518 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Saxe v. Bd. of Trs. of Metro. State College of Denver


Court of Appeals No. 05CA1251


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


179 P.3d 67; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 395; 29 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1487



March 8, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Saxe v. Bd. of Trs. of Metro. State College of Denver, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 251 (Colo., Mar. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
City and County of Denver District Court. No. 04CV3017. Honorable Shelley I. Gilman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tenured professors brought two claims in an action for declaratory and injunctive relief against appellee the board of trustees of a metropolitan state college alleging that the 2003 changes to the handbook breached their employment contract and denied them due process. The City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) held there was no breach of contract and dismissed the due process claim. The professors appealed.


OVERVIEW: The board asserted it had both statutory and contractual authority to modify the employment handbook provisions incorporated into the employment contract. Inter alia, the appellate court held that to the extent certain tenure provisions in the 1994 handbook afforded the professors vested rights, the board did not have statutory or contractual authority to unilaterally modify those provisions or to dismiss the professors. The intent of the 2004 handbook was to modify the original employment contract between the faculty and the college and to apply it retroactively to the professors. The appellate court held that the 2003 changes to the priority and relocation provisions, involved substantive rights, but that the remaining changes were procedural. The rights to priority and relocation could not be characterized as procedural because they laid at the heart of the concept of tenure; tenure provided job security and, thereby encouraged academic freedom. The loss of that job security in the event of a reduction on force (RIF) would strip tenure of its very substance. The rights to priority and relocation were essential to the contractual right to tenure and were substantive in nature.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed to the extent the trial court: (1) held that the president's decision of dismissal was final; and (2) denied the professors' claims regarding their tenure rights to priority and relocation. The case was remanded for a determination whether certain provisions of the handbook regarding priority and relocation involved vested rights, and, if so, whether those changes were retrospective. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

519 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Grant


Court of Appeals No. 03CA1034


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


174 P.3d 798; 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 104



January 25, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Rehearing denied by People v. Grant, 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 381 (Colo. Ct. App., Mar. 1, 2007)
Rehearing denied by People v. Grant, 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 671 (Colo. Ct. App., Apr. 12, 2007)
Writ of certiorari denied Grant v. People, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 26 (Colo., Jan. 14, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Jefferson County District Court. No. 00CR2287. Honorable Jane A. Tidball, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Jefferson County District Court (Colorado) found defendant guilty of first degree murder, attempted first degree murder, first degree assault, second degree assault, and resisting arrest. The trial court sentenced him to life without parole for the murder, 20 years the attempted murder, 10 years the first degree assault, eight years for the second degree assault, and 12 months for resisting arrest. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The prosecution did not request that defendant be examined by another expert simply because the prior experts' opinions regarding his sanity were not favorable, but rather, because the prior experts' opinions were incomplete, that was, a potentially new and significant diagnosis had been proposed that could dramatically affect an assessment of defendant's behavior on the day of the incident. Thus, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in permitting another examination under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-8-106(1) (2006). Also, because no evidence had been presented that defendant's mental condition was unconnected to his use of drugs, the evidence was insufficient to support an insanity defense and to require the prosecution to prove defendant's sanity beyond a reasonable doubt. Thus, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's mid-trial motion for acquittal. Finally, because reasonable minds could differ about whether defendant's conscious objective was to stab or kill demons or to stab and kill humans, the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's convictions for first degree murder and first degree assault, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-102(1)(a), 18-3-202(1)(a) (2006).


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

520 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Renander


Court of Appeals No. 06CA1546


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION SIX


151 P.3d 657; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1990



November 30, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 19, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Jefferson County District Court No. 05CR3006. Honorable R. Brooke Jackson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with 47 felony and misdemeanor counts, including sexual exploitation of a child pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6-403(3)(a), (b), and (b.5) (2006). The Jefferson County District Court (Colorado) ordered the prosecutor to reassemble 31 of the counts by victim rather than by image, which effectively resulted in the dismissal of 11 of the original charges. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The charges against defendant pertained to the alleged possession and production of photographic images of children engaged in various acts of explicit sexual conduct. Several different counts involved photographs of the same child, sometimes in a different pose or act. The trial court ordered that the counts be restructured to avoid juror confusion and potential inconsistent verdicts. The appellate court determined that the trial court's dismissal of 11 of the counts filed against defendant violated the separation of powers doctrine under Colo. Const. art. III. The grounds of juror confusion and potential inconsistent verdicts did not provide a permissible basis on which effectively to dismiss charges otherwise properly filed. Also, constitutional principles of double jeopardy and multiplicity under U.S. Const. amend. V and Colo. Const. art. II, § 18 did not require the charges to be grouped by victim rather than by image because, under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6-403, each offending image constituted a separate and distinct sexual exploitation and therefore was a separate, chargeable offense.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the order and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

People v. Collier


Court of Appeals No. 05CA0897


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


151 P.3d 668; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1993



November 30, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 19, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court No. 00CR3039. Honorable Herbert L. Stern, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) denying his Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(a) motion to correct an illegal sentence. The trial court treated the motion as having been brought pursuant to Rule 35(c) because it challenged the constitutionality of defendant's sentence and held that it was time barred pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-5-402 (2006). The trial court also denied the motion on the merits.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court concluded that the trial court properly denied defendant's motion because all of his claims were time barred. Defendant's claims--that the trial court aggravated his sentence in violation of Apprendi and Blakely, that the trial court sentenced him to two punishments for the same crime in violation of the Fifth Amendment prohibition against double jeopardy, that the Colorado Sex Offender Lifetime Supervision Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1.3-1001 et seq. (2006), violated his equal protection and due process rights, and that his due process rights were violated because the trial court used an unreliable test in sentencing him--were cognizable under Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c) and, thus, were time barred as defendant filed his motion more than three years after sentencing. Defendant's claim that he was not given the complete range of psychological and physiological testing required for his sex offender evaluation before he was sentenced was properly brought under Rule 35(a) but had to be asserted within 120 days of sentencing. Thus, it was also time barred. The court also held that the trial court did not err in declining to appoint counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's order.

Evans v. Dep't of Revenue


Court of Appeals No. 05CA1797


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO


159 P.3d 769; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1921



November 16, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 21, 2007.
Writ of certiorari denied Evans v. Dep't of Revenue, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 433 (Colo., May 21, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Jefferson County District Court No. 05CV940. Honorable Jane A. Tidball, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought judicial review of the decision by the Jefferson County District Court (Colorado) affirming the revocation of his driver's license by the Colorado Department of Revenue based upon his refusal to submit to testing as required by the express consent statute, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 42-4-1301.1 (2006).


OVERVIEW: The driver's due process rights were not violated. He did not dispute that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 42-4-1301.1(2)(a)(II) (2006) applied to his circumstances and that he did not have the option of choosing a breath test. The record also reflected that the deputy fully complied with the requirements of § 42-4-1301.1(2)(a)(II) by offering the driver a blood test. Because the driver was given the clear choice of either consenting to or refusing the blood test, his due process rights were not violated. Next the driver argued that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 42-4-1301.1 (2006) violated his rights to equal protection under the federal and state constitutions. A rational basis existed for the statute's differential treatment of individuals who received medical treatment at locations without breath testing equipment because providing such individuals with the option of choosing a breath test would cause delays in obtaining test samples. Finally, § 42-4-1301.1 was not unconstitutionally vague. The words and phrases of § 42-4-1301.1 were readily comprehensible to persons of ordinary intelligence without further definition.


OUTCOME: The decision of the district court was affirmed.

People v. Sherman


Court of Appeals No. 04CA2424


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


172 P.3d 911; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1927



November 16, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by People v. Sherman, 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 457 (Colo. Ct. App., Mar. 15, 2007)
Writ of certiorari denied Sherman v. People, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 832 (Colo., Sept. 10, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court. No. 86CR2049. Honorable Larry J. Naves, Judge.
Sherman v. People, 1990 Colo. LEXIS 542 (Colo., July 30, 1990)



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who, 17 years earlier, had been convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to life in prison with the possibility of parole, sought review of a decision of the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado), which denied his motion for postconviction relief under Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c) without a hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's counsel was not ineffective for failing to initiate plea negotiations because defendant adamantly maintained his innocence before and after trial. Further, it would have been speculative to conclude that there was a reasonable possibility that defendant would have accepted a plea bargain, and the trial court made sufficient findings of fact and conclusions of law as to the allegations. In addition, the trial court did not err in concluding that defendant's allegation of instructional error did not state a cognizable claim under Rule 35(c). Although the People, having not raised the issue in the trial court, could not assert the affirmative defense of abuse of process, the trial court did not err in denying the claim without a hearing because it did not raise a constitutional claim, and, further, there was no due process right in a lesser included offense instruction. Finally, the trial court did not err in denying the motion without a hearing because it, together with the files and the record, clearly established that defendant was not entitled to relief.


OUTCOME: The state appellate court affirmed.

People v. Versteeg


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA1227


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


165 P.3d 760; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1830



November 2, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Rehearing denied by People v. Versteeg, 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 2176 (Colo. Ct. App., Dec. 28, 2006)
Writ of certiorari granted People v. Versteeg, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 786 (Colo., Aug. 27, 2007)
Motion granted by, Appeal dismissed by, Remanded by Petitioner: the People of Colo. v. Respondent: William P. Versteeg, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 447 (Colo., May 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Arapahoe County District Court No. 96CR2645. Honorable James F. Macrum, Jr., Judge, Honorable Gerald J. Rafferty, Judge.
Versteeg v. People, 2000 Colo. LEXIS 488 (Colo., 2000)



DISPOSITION: ORDER REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who had been convicted of first degree murder and attempted first degree murder, appealed an order of the Arapahoe County District Court, Colorado, denying his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The instant court held that defendant was entitled to relief on his first postconviction claim that the trial court plainly erred when it gave an erroneous jury instruction on, and allowed the prosecutor to make erroneous statements about, self-induced intoxication under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1-804(1) (2006). It reached this conclusion based on a change in the law that occurred after defendant was tried but before his conviction was final. The instruction improperly focused on whether, as a result of self-induced intoxication, defendant lacked the capacity to form specific intent, instead of whether he in fact formed specific intent. The prosecutor exacerbated the instruction's deficiency by telling the jury that intoxication was irrelevant to the element of deliberation. The instruction and prosecutor's comments were plainly erroneous because the law at the time of trial was settled and contrary to the law in effect when the trial court considered defendant's postconviction claim. The trial court did not sufficiently address defendant's remaining postconviction claims. Although some of defendant's assertions were properly rejected, other assertions required additional findings.


OUTCOME: The order denying defendant's motion for postconviction relief was reversed, and the case was remanded. Regarding remedy, the trial court was directed to either order a new trial on the charges of first degree murder and attempted first degree murder or enter a judgment of conviction for second degree murder and attempted second degree murder and resentence defendant on those lesser offenses. The People would select the remedy.

Sanger v. Dennis


Court of Appeals No.: 06CA1944


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION A


148 P.3d 404; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1619; 180 L.R.R.M. 2838; 153 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P60,277



September 28, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 19, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court No. 06CV9214. Honorable John N. McMullen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Colorado Secretary of State appealed a judgment of the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado), granting a preliminary injunction in favor of plaintiff teacher's unions enjoining the implementation of Colo. Admin. R. 1.14, 8 Colo. Regs. § 1505-6 (Rule 1.14), which would force labor organizations to get written permission before using an individual's dues to fund political campaigns.


OVERVIEW: Voters passed the Campaign and Political Finance Amendment, Colo. Const. art. XXVIII, an initiative regulating campaign financing. The district court found that the unions had shown a reasonable probability of success on the merits as to their allegations that the Secretary exceeded her authority and that the rule violated the First Amendment. The court affirmed, noting that the district court referred to the Rathke standards in its ruling. Also, the district court clarified that it was enjoining the enforcement of Rule 1.14(b) as applied to the unions. The court agreed that the rule imposed a restriction that was not supported by Colo. Const. art. XXVIII. The Secretary's definition of "member" was neither a reasonable interpretation nor consistent with art. XXVIII. Even applying an intermediate review, the court concluded that the unions showed a reasonable probability of success on their First Amendment freedom of association claim in that by employing an "opt out" procedure, the unions complied with constitutional requirements. Yet Rule 1.14(b) effectively denied the First Amendment rights of the majority of union members for the benefit of dissenting members.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the district court.

People v. Elie


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA0940


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


148 P.3d 359; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1487



September 7, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication December 19, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court No. 03CR1362. Honorable Sheila A. Rappaport, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS AFFIRMED, SENTENCE REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury before the City and County of Denver District Court, Colorado, of attempted first degree murder, first degree assault, and felony menacing. Defendant appealed the convictions, and he also appealed his aggravated range sentence for one of the felony menacing convictions.


OVERVIEW: One of the victims was shot in the ankle in defendant's home. Defendant and another man forced the victims into the back seat of a car. After a brief exchange, the victims were shot. Defendant asserted the trial court erred in admitting the victim's videotaped statement, without previously viewing the tape. He also asserted only those portions of the videotape should have been admitted that were consistent with the direct examination testimony. The appellate court disagreed; it was proper for the jury to consider all the statements the victim had given. Defendant cross-examined the victim on almost every aspect of his account of the crime. Further, defendant did not object at trial that there were new matters in the videotape. The appellate court disagreed with defendant's contention that the trial court erred in instructing the jury on complicity liability. The trial court in this case gave a properly reformulated instruction. As to the sentence, plain error review applied to an unpreserved alleged Apprendi error with respect to the felony menacing conviction. The error was obvious, and it so undermined fundamental fairness as to cast serious doubt on the sentence's reliability.


OUTCOME: The judgments of conviction were affirmed. The sentence for felony menacing was reversed, and the case was remanded for resentencing on that conviction.

September 7, 2006, Decided

Modified and rehearing denied by People v. Al-Yousif, 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 2183 (Colo. Ct. App., Dec. 28, 2006)
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part Naif Al-Yousif v. People, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 399 (Colo., May 14, 2007)
Writ of certiorari denied, Review improvidently allowed by Al-Yousif v. People, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 246 (Colo., Mar. 7, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Naif Al-Yousif, 2011 Colo. App. LEXIS 2100 (Colo. Ct. App., Dec. 15, 2011)
Writ of habeas corpus granted Al-Yousif v. Trani, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 7655 (D. Colo., Jan. 22, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court No. 01CR1861. Honorable Gloria A. Rivera, Judge.
People v. Al-Yousif, 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1513 (Colo. Ct. App., Sept. 7, 2006)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) of first degree-felony murder, robbery, accessory to a crime, concealing a death, and theft by receiving. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in instructing the jury on a class three felony theft by receiving charge. The court of appeals agreed. At the close of the evidence, defendant requested that the trial court give the jury an instruction on the class four felony offense of theft by receiving, arguing that theft by receiving was a lesser nonincluded offense of the robbery count. The People objected to the instruction, contending that the correct theft by receiving charge was the class three felony, because the evidence showed that defendant withdrew nearly $ 20,000 from the victim's checking account. The trial court granted the People's request and instructed the jury on the class three theft by receiving charge, as well as the class four theft by receiving charge. The court reasoned that defendant was on notice of the underlying facts supporting the class three felony. However, defendant was originally charged with the class four felony of robbery, but as a result of the People's tendered lesser nonincluded offense, he ultimately was convicted of a higher offense, namely the class three felony of theft by receiving. Accordingly, the trial court erred.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated as to defendant's convictions for theft by receiving and for robbery. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed. On remand, the trial court was instructed to correct the mittimus.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) convicting him of of six counts of securities fraud in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 11-51-501, 11-51-603 (2005), two counts of theft from an at-risk adult in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6.5-103(5) (2005), and one count of computer crime in violation of 1983 Colo. Calvert v. Indus. Claim Appeals Office


Court of Appeals No. 05CA1201


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO


155 P.3d 474; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1388



August 24, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 19, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Calvert v. Indus. Claim Appeals Office, 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1821 (Colo. Ct. App., Oct. 26, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 4-355-715.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee sought review of an order from respondent, the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado (Panel), which denied his petition to reopen his claim for additional permanent partial disability benefits from respondents, an employer and its insurer.


OVERVIEW: The employee sustained an injury to his tailbone in 1997. He was denied permanent total disability benefits, but awarded future medical benefits. In 2004, he underwent back surgery. He filed a petition to reopen the 1997 claim, seeking additional temporary disability benefits. An administrative law judge (ALJ) denied the petition to reopen, finding that it was filed outside the time limits set forth in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-43-303(1) and (2)(a) (2005). The Panel upheld the order. On appeal, the court found that the petition to reopen was clearly filed more than six years after the accidental injury and more than two years after the last payment of disability benefits. The fact that the employee was entitled to the 2004 back surgery as a Grover-type benefit did not extend the limitations period for reopening his disability benefit claim. Because the employee's petition to reopen was not filed within the applicable limitations period, the ALJ properly denied it on that basis. Further, the ALJ's application of the time limits in § 8-43-303 to bar the employee's petition to reopen did not violate his right to either substantive due process or equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Panel's judgment.

Hathaway Lighting, Inc. v. Indus. Claim Appeals Office


Court of Appeals No.: 05CA1630


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


143 P.3d 1187; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1389



August 24, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 20, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Hathaway Lighting, Inc. v. Indus. Claim Appeals Office of Colo., 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 2100 (Colo. Ct. App., Dec. 14, 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied Hathaway Lighting, Inc. v. Pinnacol Assur., 2007 Colo. LEXIS 253 (Colo., Mar. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 4-608-932.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a hearing in a workers' compensation proceeding, an administrative law judge (ALJ) found that, although the contract of hire between petitioner claimant and petitioner employer was executed in Colorado, no jurisdiction existed under the extraterritorial provisions of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-41-204 (2005). The claimant and the employer sought review of the final order issued by respondent, the Colorado Industrial Claim Appeals Office.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was a resident of the State of Washington. He was hired by the employer, a Colorado corporation, to work on out-of-state projects related to the installation of commercial lighting. He was injured when he fell off a ladder while working in Oregon. He was not present in Colorado during the hiring process or between the date he was hired and the date he was injured. The employer and the claimant contended that the ALJ and the Panel erred when they determined that the Division of Workers' Compensation lacked jurisdiction to hear the claim. Section 8-41-204 was the extraterritorial provision of the Workers' Compensation Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-40-101 et seq. (2005). Under the second sentence of § 8-41-204, the claimant was only entitled to compensation for injuries received within six months of his physically departing from Colorado. The appellate court rejected the employer's and the claimant's assertion that where the employee was not physically present at the time of hire, the six-month period ran from the date of hire. The appellate court also rejected the argument that requiring a physical presence in Colorado violated equal protection and due process guarantees.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Giguere v. SJS Family Enters.


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA0947


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


155 P.3d 462; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1276


August 10, 2006, Announced  
August 10, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 19, 2007.
Opinion Modified, and As Modified, Petition for Rehearing DENIED.
Modified and rehearing denied by Giguere v. SJS Family Enters., Ltd., 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1620 (Colo. Ct. App., Sept. 28, 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied Giguere v. SJS Family Enters., 2007 Colo. LEXIS 301 (Colo., Apr. 16, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Larimer County District Court No. 03CV417. Honorable John David Williams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDERS AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Larimer County District Court, Colorado, granted judgment in favor of appellee developer on appellant landowners' action seeking a declaratory judgment that the developer could not develop Lot 2A or that development was subject to the original building and access envelope. The trial court dissolved the injunction. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowners argued that the trial court erred in dissolving the injunction based on the Ratification Agreement, which approved the 1991 amended plat of Lot 2A, as well as various other changes. The appellate court agreed with the trial court that under the Colorado Common Interest Ownership Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 38-33.3-101 et seq. (2005), the Ratification Agreement validly eliminated the building and access envelope on Lot 2A. Colo. Rev. Stat. § 38-33.3-117 expressly provided for application to preexisting common interest communities. The Ratification Agreement was signed by 70 of the 85 lot owners, thus, its approval was valid. The landowners were properly seeking an injunction to prevent imminent construction on Lot 2A. The trial court erred in determining the case was to construe the landowners' declaration, not to enforce it. Pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 38-33.3-123(1)(C), the landowners prevailed and were entitled to attorney fees. Eliminating the building and access envelope on Lot 2A was an amendment to the Declaration which required, but did not receive, three-fourths owner approval. The developer did not waive its right to construct multiple units.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was affirmed as to the dissolution of the injunction and reversed on its order declining to award attorney fees, and remanded for further proceedings on attorney fees.

People v. Holwuttle


Court of Appeals No. 03CA1163


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO


155 P.3d 447; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1277



August 10, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 19, 2007.
Writ of certiorari denied Holwuttle v. People, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 245 (Colo., Mar. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Arapahoe County District Court No. 01CR3267. Honorable Richard D. Turelli, Judge Honorable Michael Spear, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Arapahoe County District Court (Colorado), which convicted him of unlawful sexual contact with force and unlawful sexual contact, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-404 (2005), and which imposed sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court's jury instructions defining physical force, physical violence, and consent permitted the jury to find that he was guilty of unlawful sexual contact with force even though the force he applied to the victim's body was just or warranted. On appeal, the court disagreed. The instructions mirrored the language of Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 18-3-404 and 18-3-402(4)(a) (2005), and were, thus, adequate and proper. The court next rejected defendant's argument that Colo. R. Crim. P. 25 was violated because his present sentence, imposed as a result of his postconviction motion, was not imposed by the same judge who had presided over his trial and who had imposed the original sentence. Rule 25 did not apply to resentencing proceedings. Next, the court rejected defendant's argument that the trial court erred in determining that he was not eligible for probation for the unlawful sexual contact with force offense. Finally, the court held that because the offenses defined by the two statutes that defendant violated had different elements and did not address exactly the same conduct, defendant's equal protection challenge had to be rejected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and defendant's sentence.

 

534 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kendrick


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA2156


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


143 P.3d 1175; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1279



August 10, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 20, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] El Paso County District Court. No. 01CR3138. Honorable Timothy J. Simmons, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The El Paso County District Court, Colorado, denied defendant movant's request for postconviction relief, pursuant to Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to aggravated robbery, a class three felony. As part of the plea agreement, defendant stipulated to a 15-year sentence in the Department of Corrections and agreed that he would not file any Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(b) motions. Defendant contended that the imposition of his sentence violated his right to be tried by a jury at sentencing. The appellate court noted, however, that defendant was charged with a crime of violence. The appellate court further concluded that the presumptive range of penalties referred to in Apprendi and Blakely was only that portion of the sentence that subjected a defendant to incarceration or imprisonment. When a defendant received a sentence of imprisonment within the presumptive range established for the crime, plus a period of mandatory parole, the sentence was constitutional under Apprendi and Blakely. Defendant's sentence was within the presumptive range, and it was neither unconstitutional or illegal. Finally, the appellate court disagreed that the trial court erred in denying the defendant's motion without a hearing because the motion, the files, and the record clearly established that defendant was not entitled to relief.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the conviction.

Town of Foxfield v. Archdiocese of Denver


Court of Appeals No. 05CA0202


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


148 P.3d 339; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1282



August 10, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 19, 2006.
Writ of certiorari granted Town of Foxfield v. Archdiocese of Denver, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 987 (Colo., Dec. 18, 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied, Review improvidently allowed by Town of Foxfield v. Archdiocese of Denver, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 385 (Colo., May 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Arapahoe County District Court. No. 01CV3299. Honorable Nancy A. Hopf, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED, CROSS-APPEAL DISMISSED, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant archdiocese challenged the constitutionality of an ordinance appellee Town adopted which restricted parking that affected church property. The Arapahoe County District Court, Colorado, granted the Town's motion for summary judgment and granted the archdiocese's request to stay enforcement of the ordinance. The archdiocese appealed.


OVERVIEW: In granting the Town summary judgment, the trial court concluded there was no jurisdictional basis to apply the provisions of the Religious Land Use and Institutionalized Persons Act (RLUIPA), 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000cc et seq., and that Colorado's Freedom to Gather to Worship Act (FGWA), Colo. Rev. Stat. § 29-1-1201 et seq. (2005) did not apply to the ordinance in question. On review, the archdiocese challenged these conclusions. The appellate court found that the jurisdictional prerequisite under 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000cc(a)(2)(B) was met as the rectory and the chapel on its property were religious buildings actively used as the site and dynamic for a full range of religious activities. As such, the activity sufficiently affected commerce to invoke jurisdiction under the RLUIPA. The RLUIPA also applied because the ordinance was only enforceable through an individualized assessment as the citizens had exclusive enforcement authority. Thus, the trial court erred in granting summary judgment in favor of the Town as there was a genuine issue of material fact as to the merits of the archdiocese's RLUIPA claim. Similarly, the trial court was wrong in finding the FGWA was a general parking law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for trial.

Rutt v. Poudre Educ. Ass'n


Court of Appeals No. 05CA1718


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION A


151 P.3d 585; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1173; 180 L.R.R.M. 2033



July 20, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 19, 2007.
Writ of certiorari granted Colo. Educ. Ass'n v. Rutt, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 92 (Colo., Feb. 5, 2007)
Reversed by, Remanded by Colo. Educ. Ass'n v. Rutt, 2008 Colo. LEXIS 495 (Colo., May 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Rutt v. Poudre Educ. Ass'n, 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1198 (Colo. Ct. App., July 20, 2006)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizens filed a complaint with the Colorado Secretary of State's office alleging that respondent labor organizations illegally contributed to the campaign of a candidate for state senate. An administrative law judge (ALJ) dismissed the citizens' claims and denied the organizations' request for attorney fees. The citizens appealed, and the organizations cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the citizens contended the ALJ erred in concluding the labor organizations did not contribute to the candidate's campaign in violation of Colo. Const. art. XXVIII, §§ 2(5)(a)(IV), 3(4)(a) of Colorado's Campaign and Political Finance Amendment, and Colo. Rev. Stat. § 1-45-117 (2005) of the Colorado Fair Practices Act. The appellate court agreed with the citizens that the organizations' coordinated activities in (1) receiving from the candidate's campaign thousands of flyers and numerous yard signs for distribution, (2) having the candidate make personal appearances at the volunteer site, and (3) discussing campaign strategy with the candidate's campaign manager constituted coordinated actions, and that the practical effect of the organizations' efforts was the same as if they had contributed a dollar amount to the campaign. Further, the organizations' collective, volunteer efforts went beyond individual volunteer efforts. The appellate court concluded that these coordinated activities constituted an illegal contribution. The ALJ adequately considered the probative value of evidence the citizens may have collected by trespass, and its admission was not arbitrary or unfair.


OUTCOME: The ALJ's order was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings. On remand, the ALJ was directed to consider the merits of the labor organizations' request for attorney fees.

People v. Starkweather

COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE

Brown v. Davidson


Court of Appeals No. 04CA2455


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


192 P.3d 415; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1015



June 29, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified and Petition for Rehearing Denied June 28, 2007.
Modified and rehearing denied by Brown v. Davidson, 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 1216 (Colo. Ct. App., June 28, 2007)



DISPOSITION: ORDER REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff candidates challenged a decision from the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado), which refused to award attorney fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 in a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action brought against defendant secretary of state.


OVERVIEW: The candidates wanted to be placed on the ballot for United States President and Vice President. They contended that requiring unaffiliated candidates to file a statement 120 days before the general election was unconstitutional under the First and Fourteenth Amendments. In a hearing under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 1-1-113 (2005), the secretary was ordered to place the candidates on the ballot under the substantial compliance test of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 1-1-103 (2005). The constitutional issues were not addressed, and attorney fees were not awarded. Thereafter, the candidates sought review. In reversing, the appellate court determined that it had jurisdiction to hear the matter under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-4-102(1) Next, the remedies of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 1-1-113 (2005) were not exclusive; therefore, an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 was permitted. The appellate court determined that the candidates' case raised substantial constitutional claims for purposes of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. The claims were not wholly frivolous, nor did they conflict with any United States Supreme Court decisions. The trial court improperly used the test applicable to unintended irregularities.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Wenzinger


Court of Appeals No. 04CA2322


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


155 P.3d 415; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 784



June 1, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 19, 2007.
As Modified.
Modified and rehearing denied by People v. Wenzinger, 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 1111 (Colo. Ct. App., July 13, 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied Wenzinger v. People, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 73 (Colo., Jan. 22, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Wenzinger v. Colo., 127 S. Ct. 2919, 168 L. Ed. 2d 249, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 6884 (U.S., June 4, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court No. 00CR4352. Honorable H. Jeffrey Bayless, Judge. Honorable Robert S. Hyatt, Judge.
People v. Wenzinger, 2003 Colo. App. LEXIS 128 (Colo. Ct. App., Jan. 30, 2003)



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED. Opinion Modified, and As Modified, Petitions for Rehearing DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to harassment by stalking in 2001, and the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) convicted her of that offense and sentenced her to ten years in prison. In July 2004, defendant filed a motion for correction of an illegal sentence, pursuant to Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(a), claiming that her sentence was illegal under Blakely v. Washington. The district court denied the motion, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The district court convicted defendant of harassment by stalking, a class four felony, and although the offense carried a presumptive sentencing range of two to six years' imprisonment, the court found extraordinary aggravating circumstances and sentenced defendant to ten years in prison. Defendant appealed, arguing that the district court violated the rule which the U.S. Supreme Court announced in Apprendi v. New Jersey when it determined her sentence, but state appellate courts denied her appeal. After the Supreme Court issued its decision in Blakely v. Washington, defendant filed a motion for correction of an illegal sentence, pursuant to Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(a), arguing that her sentence was illegal under Blakely. The court of appeals held that (1) defendant's motion was not cognizable under Rule 35(a), but was reviewable under Rule 35(c)(2)(I); and (2) defendant was not entitled to relief under Blakely because the rule which the Supreme Court announced in Blakely was a new rule of criminal procedure that did not apply retroactively to cases on collateral review, and defendant's conviction became final before the Supreme Court announced its decision.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the district court's judgment.

Estate of Harper v. Denver Health & Hosp. Auth.


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA2398


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


140 P.3d 273; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 625



May 4, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 18, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court No. 04CV4010. Honorable J. Stephen Phillips, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff children challenged a decision from the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado), which granted a motion to dismiss in a wrongful death case filed against defendant hospital authority and awarded attorney fees under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-17-201 (2005).


OVERVIEW: A decedent sought medical treatment at the authority's clinic after a business trip. She was improperly diagnosed with influenza, and she died shortly thereafter from malaria. The children then filed a wrongful death action against the authority. The case was dismissed and attorney fees were awarded. The children then sought review. In affirming, the appellate court determined that dismissal was appropriate on the claim for vicarious liability. The Colorado Health Authority Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 25-29-101 (2005) et seq., did not create a statutory exception to the corporate practice of medicine doctrine. A contrary conclusion would have defeated the expressed intent of the Colorado Legislature to preserve the corporate practice of medicine in Colorado. The authority's clinic was not explicitly authorized or required to practice medicine, and it was unable control the independent medical judgment of its employees. Attorney fees were mandatory after a dismissal under Colo. R. Civ. P. 12(b), and the successful defense of a dismissal order on appeal entitled the authority to those fees as well.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed, and the case was remanded for an award of attorney fees incurred on appeal.

People v. Nunn


Court of Appeals No. 03CA0939


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


148 P.3d 222; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 481



April 6, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 19, 2006.
Rehearing denied by People v. Nunn, 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 780 (Colo. Ct. App., May 25, 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied Nunn v. People, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 948 (Colo., Nov. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] City and County of Denver District Court Nos. 01CR4599 & 02CR1491. Honorable R. Michael Mullins, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the City and County of Denver District Court, Colorado, convicting him of forty-seven substantive felony counts and twelve habitual criminal counts, and imposing a prison sentence of forty-eight years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in two consolidated cases with numerous felony counts, all arising out of his theft and forgery of checks totaling over $ 130,000 and his use of false identification to cash the checks. Defendant admitted having cashed the forged checks but raised the affirmative defense of duress, asserting that others were threatening to harm him and his family if he did not do so. Defendant argued that his habitual criminal sentence must be vacated because it was based on facts found by a judge rather than a jury. The appellate court ruled that the factual determinations made by the trial court neither deprived defendant of his constitutional rights nor rendered his sentence illegal. The fact that defendant was convicted of more than three prior felonies based upon charges separately brought and tried, and arising out of separate and distinct criminal episodes could be definitively established based on the judicial records introduced at the habitual criminal trial. Also, the jury instruction of the affirmative defense of duress was not legally and constitutionally deficient, because the instructions adequately made clear that the burden of proof remained on the prosecution.


OUTCOME: The judgment and sentence was affirmed.

Modified and rehearing denied by People ex rel. T.D., 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 635 (Colo. Ct. App., May 4, 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied T.D. v. People ex rel. T.D., 2006 Colo. LEXIS 576 (Colo., June 26, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by T. D. v. Colorado, 127 S. Ct. 565, 166 L. Ed. 2d 419, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 8464 (U.S., Nov. 6, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by M. A. v. Colorado, 127 S. Ct. 564, 166 L. Ed. 2d 411, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 8403 (U.S., Nov. 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Adams County District Court. No. 03JV762 Honorable Chris Melonakis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, appellants, a mother and father, appealed from a judgment of the Adams County District Court (Colorado) terminating their parent-child legal relationships with their two children.


OVERVIEW: The parents' two children were removed from the home by appellee, the Denver, Colorado, Department of Human Services, because of concerns about its unsafe physical condition. A dependency and neglect petition was filed, an adjudication order was entered, and the children were placed in a foster home. The evidence was sufficient to terminate the father's rights to the children under Colo. Rev. Also, the evidence was sufficient to terminate the mother's parental rights because (1) the mother was pregnant with her third child; (2) although the mother had separated from the father, the trial court was concerned that the separation was not permanent as she still continued to have contact with the father; and (3) the trial court believed that the addition of a third child would frustrate the mother's ability to meet the other children's needs.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Further, a finding that there were no viable alternatives to termination was supported by the evidence.

Jam Rest. v. City of Longmont


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA1705


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


140 P.3d 192; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 211



February 23, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 18, 2006.
Writ of certiorari denied City of Longmont v. Jam Rest., Inc., 2006 Colo. LEXIS 631 (Colo., July 31, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Boulder County District Court No. 02CV458. Honorable Carol Glowinsky, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed an order of the Boulder County District Court (Colorado) that precluded the amortization of the sexually oriented business operated by plaintiff restaurant under a city zoning ordinance, and that upheld the constitutionality of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 38-1-101(3)(a) (2005). The restaurant challenged the trial court's holding that the judicial review provisions of the city ordinance did not violate U.S. Const. amends. I and XIV.


OVERVIEW: The city passed a zoning ordinance that limited the location of sexually oriented businesses to general industrial or mixed industrial zones and required the businesses to obtain licenses. The restaurant had been operating as a sexually oriented business and challenged the city's ordinance. The legislature passed Colo. Rev. Stat. § 38-1-101(3)(a), which prohibited local governments from enacting ordinances that terminated or amortized nonconforming uses that were lawful at their inception. The trial court found that § 38-1-101 prevailed over the city's ordinance. On appeal, the court held that although zoning regulations were typically a matter of local concern, § 38-1-101(3)(a) was not a zoning regulation; rather, it addressed the statewide concern of protecting property interests against the unconstitutional taking of property without just compensation. Therefore § 38-1-101(3)(a) prevailed over the city's zoning ordinance and did not violate the home rule amendment, Colo. Const. art. XX, § 6. The court noted that because the city did not attempt to enforce the zoning ordinance until after the effective date of § 38-1-101(3)(a), no retroactive application occurred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order.

People v. Rossman


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA0425


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


140 P.3d 172; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 136



February 9, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 18, 2006.
Writ of certiorari denied Rossman v. People, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 573 (Colo., June 26, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Weld County District Court No. 02CR1216. Honorable Daniel S. Maus, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Weld County District Court, Colorado, denying his motion to modify a condition of his probation requiring him to submit to the collection of a biological sample for DNA testing, and to declare Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-11-204.3 (2005), unconstitutional as applied to him and other persons on probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with second degree burglary and forgery. Defendant pled guilty to both offenses and was sentenced to three years probation and 180 days of electronic home monitoring. Defendant later violated his probation and was resentenced to three years of intensive supervision probation. As a condition of his probation, the trial court ordered defendant to submit biological samples for DNA testing pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-11-204.3. The appellate court ruled that the privacy interests of a probationer did not outweigh the governmental interests advanced by Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-11-204.3(1)(b.5). DNA databases assisted in exonerating the innocent, solving past as well as future crimes, and deterring recidivism. The appellate court was not persuaded that the privacy interest probationers had in their biological samples outweighed the governmental interests advanced by DNA databases and justified a greater protection from warrantless searches and seizures under Colo. Const. art. II, § 7, than that afforded by the federal constitution.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

In re Marriage of McSoud


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA2682


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


131 P.3d 1208; 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 138



February 9, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication on April 18, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Douglas County District Court No. 01DR336. Honorable Richard D. Turelli, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, ORDERS AFFIRMED, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of an order from the Douglas County District Court (Colorado), which, pursuant to the dissolution of the parties' marriage, allocated decisionmaking responsibilities regarding the religious upbringing and medical care of the parties' child to appellee father. The mother also challenged the denial of her motions for relief under Colo. R. Civ. P. 59 and 60, and her motion for disqualification of the judge.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the dissolution of the parties' marriage, the trial court allocated decisionmaking responsibilities relating to their child's religious upbringing and medical care to the father, ordered that all other decisions should be shared by the parties, and increased the father's parenting time. The mother later sought relief under Rules 59 and 60, and sought to disqualify the trial judge. The trial court declined to recuse and denied the mother's motion for relief. On appeal, the court found that the order allocating the decisionmaking responsibility for the child's medical care to the father was supported by the record. Shared decisionmaking regarding medical care was not in the child's best interests pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 14-10-124(1.5)(b)(I) (2005) where the parties were utterly incapable of listening to one another. Finally, a special advocate's recommendation that the mother be allowed to continue to take the child to her church during her parenting time, but only so long as she supported the child's participation and attendance at church with the father as well, violated the mother's rights under the First Amendment to the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the adoption of the recommendation that the mother could be denied the right to take the child to her own church if she failed to support the child's participation and attendance at activities chosen by the father. The court affirmed the allocation of medical decisionmaking to the father. The court affirmed the denial of the mother's motions for relief and disqualification. The court remanded the case for further proceedings.

People v. Ramirez


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA1741


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


140 P.3d 169; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 2043



December 15, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 18, 2006.
Writ of certiorari denied, En banc Ramirez v. People, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 577 (Colo., June 26, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court No. 02CR5181. Honorable Martin F. Egelhoff, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: City and County of Denver District Court convicted defendant upon jury verdicts of second degree kidnapping, sexual assault, and robbery. Defendant appealed the convictions and also his sentence for the kidnapping conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant forced the victim into his truck, struck her in the face, then sexually assaulted and robbed her. On appeal, he claimed the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress DNA evidence that had been obtained pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-2-201(5)(g)(I) (2005) while he was in prison for an unrelated sexual assault. However, the special needs exception to the Fourth Amendment's warrant requirement permitted collection of blood samples from convicts for use in assembling a DNA database. He claimed the trial court erred by imposing an aggravated range sentence on the kidnapping conviction based on a finding of aggravators that were not determined by the jury. He committed the offense while on bond for a felony for which he was convicted by the time of sentencing in the instant case. Therefore, the trial court had to sentence him pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1.3-401(9) (2005). His sentence was enhanced because he committed this kidnapping while on bond for a felony for which he was convicted, so because the prior felony was the event that triggered the enhanced sentencing, the enhancement fell within the prior conviction exception to the Apprendi rule.


OUTCOME: The judgment and sentence were affirmed.

 

549 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Bruce v. City of Colo. Springs


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA1572


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


131 P.3d 1187; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 2048



December 15, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication on April 18, 2006.
Writ of certiorari denied Bruce v. City of Colo. Springs, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 237 (Colo., Apr. 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: El Paso County District Court No. 03CV3082. Honorable Kirk S. Samelson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After two city ordinances were challenged by plaintiff taxpayer, the El Paso County District Court (Colorado) entered summary judgment in favor of the city. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer contended a street light service charge and cable television charge constituted taxes imposed in violation of the state and city Taxpayers' Bill of Rights (TABOR). The appellate court disagreed, concluding the service charges under the ordinances were not taxes, but service fees. The parties conceded, the trial court found, and the appellate court agreed that the street light charge was not an ad valorem tax, an excise tax, or a special assessment. The street light service charge was reasonably related to the overall cost of operating street lights. Although the city might have chosen a different calculation for imposing the service charge, there was nothing inherently unsound in its methodology. Accordingly, the street light service charge was a special fee reasonably related to the overall cost of providing the city's street lights. The taxpayer also contended that cable television charges were actually taxes the city imposed on the cable provider, which were then passed on to consumers in violation of TABOR. The charges were not taxes, and thus, TABOR was inapplicable. The charges listed in the cable bill represented the cost of doing business with the city.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. McNally


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA1654


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


143 P.3d 1062; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1950



December 1, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Released for Publication October 20, 2006.
Writ of certiorari denied McNally v. People, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 788 (Colo., Oct. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: El Paso County District Court No. 02CR1342. Honorable G. David Miller, Jr., Judge.
People v. McNally, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1994 (Colo. Ct. App., Dec. 1, 2005)



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The El Paso County District Court (Colorado) sentenced defendant in connection with his theft conviction and adjudication as an habitual criminal. Defendant appealed his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Because defendant's underlying theft conviction was a class four felony, and he had three prior felonies, the trial court was required to impose a sentence of 24 years, four times the maximum presumptive range sentence. Defendant argued that a 24-year sentence was unconstitutionally disproportionate under the Eighth Amendment because his conviction stemmed from a commercial dispute and because his prior convictions were not sufficiently grave and serious. A threshold comparison of defendant's offense and sentence imposed yielded no inference of gross disproportionality. Defendant's triggering offense was theft of property worth $ 500 or more but less than $ 15,000. This was a class four felony under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-4-401(2)(c). At least two of defendant's prior offenses -- second degree burglary and attempted second degree burglary -- were crimes characterized as grave or serious for purposes of proportionality analysis. The sentence did not yield an inference of gross disproportionality under the governing precedents.


OUTCOME: The sentence was affirmed.

 

551 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. McIntier


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA2276


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


134 P.3d 467; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1951



December 1, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Adams County District Court No. 02CR3167. Honorable C. Scott Crabtree, Judge. Honorable John J. Vigil, Judge. Honorable Thomas R. Ensor, Judge.
People v. McIntier, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1967 (Colo. Ct. App., Dec. 1, 2005)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Adams County District Court (Colorado) that found him guilty of retaliation against a witness under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-8-706 (2005) and entered judgment on the conviction. Defendant challenged the sufficiency of the information charging him with the retaliation offense and the sufficiency of the evidence to support his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the information charging him was insufficient to invoke the trial court's jurisdiction because it omitted the requisite specific intent mens rea for the offense. The court noted that the requirement under Colo. R. Crim. P. 7(b)(2) that the information identify the essential elements of the crime was satisfied where the language in the information tracked the language of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-8-706(1), which included the terms "retribution" and "retaliation" that were by definition required intentional conduct. The court held that defendant's conviction was supported by sufficient evidence that showed he sent a letter to the deputy district attorney (DA) explicitly communicating a threat, as opposed to a description of a fantasy, against the witness who testified against him in a prior drug case and that defendant expected the DA to inform the witness of the threats. The court held that nothing in § 18-8-706(1) required that the threat be directly communicated to or received by the person protected under § 18-8-706(1) but only that it be "directed to" such person. The court rejected defendant's claims that § 18-8-706(1) was unconstitutionally vague or overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

People v. Veren


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA1820


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


140 P.3d 131; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1957



December 1, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 18, 2006.
Reported at People v. Veren, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1963 (Colo. Ct. App., Dec. 1, 2005)
Rehearing denied by People v. Veren, 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 112 (Colo. Ct. App., Feb. 2, 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied People v. Veren, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 615 (Colo., July 17, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Teller County District Court No. 02CR214. Honorable Edward S. Colt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Teller County District Court (Colorado) convicting him of possession of pseudoephedrine with intent to use it as a precursor in manufacturing a controlled substance (methamphetamine), possession of chemicals or supplies with intent to manufacture a schedule II controlled substance, and driving under restraint and imposing concurrent 10-year sentences on the drug offenses and six months on the driving charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress and by admitting the lay opinion testimony of police officers concerning the amount of Sudafed possessed by defendant. The court held that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress because the police stopped and arrested defendant after they observed him committing a traffic violation and found that his license had been revoked; thus, the search of his truck and seizure of drugs was incident to his lawful arrest based upon probable cause. The court held that the trial court erred in allowing the officers to testify that the possession of a large amount of Sudafed often indicated the possibility of manufacturing methamphetamine because it required specialized knowledge and thus constituted expert opinion testimony admitted without pretrial disclosure and expert qualification as required by Colo. R. Evid. 702. The court concluded that the lack of pretrial disclosure of the officers' expert testimony and the bases of their opinions deprived defendant of an opportunity to evaluate the testimony before trial or to obtain his own expert witness.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment as to defendant's two possession convictions and remanded the case for a new trial on those charges and further consistent proceedings. The court affirmed the judgment in all other respects.

People v. Lopez


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA0241


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


140 P.3d 106; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1958



December 1, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 18, 2006.
Rehearing denied by People v. Lopez, 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 298 (Colo. Ct. App., Mar. 9, 2006)
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part People v. Lopez, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 702 (Colo., Aug. 14, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Montrose County District Court. No. 02CR57. Honorable Dennis P. Friedrich, Judge.
People v. Lopez, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1962 (Colo. Ct. App., Dec. 1, 2005)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND SENTENCE REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appeals from the judgment entered by the Montrose County District Court (Colorado) upon the 18-month sentence imposed following a jury verdict finding him guilty of failure to register as a sex offender, second offense. He also appealed the 18-month sentence imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was serving a 90-day jail term. While incarcerated, he attempted to register as a sex offender but was informed that he was not allowed to register while incarcerated. He also did not register upon his release. The statute applicable to defendant required that he register quarterly and notify authorities of any change of address. The appellate court therefore concluded the offense of failure to register as a sex offender, under which defendant was charged, was a continuing offense and he was not entitled to acquittal. However, the variance in defendant's case required reversal and remand for a new trial. Defendant was charged with failing to register as a convicted sex offender "on or about October 23, 2001." Defendant was given no notice he could be convicted for his failure to register on any date other than the one contained in the information. The evidence of defendant's conduct on occasions other than the day charged in the information impaired his ability to defend against the charge and prejudiced him in preparing and presenting his defense. Therefore, the variance constituted reversible error, and defendant was entitled to a new trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial. On remand, the trial court was to reconsider defendant's waiver of counsel.

People v. Harte


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA1366


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


131 P.3d 1180; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1861



November 17, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication on April 18, 2006.
Writ of certiorari denied Harte v. People, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 234 (Colo., Apr. 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court No. 02CR14. Honorable Sheila A. Rappaport, Judge. Honorable Martin F. Egelhoff, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) convicted defendant of obtaining a controlled substance by fraud and deceit and attempting to obtain a controlled substance by fraud and deceit. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested at a hospital after a doctor called a local pharmacy, which informed him that it had filled five prior prescriptions for defendant for narcotics in the prior month and that the pharmacy had a narcotic alert on him. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the statute. The appellate court perceived no vagueness. Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-18-415(1)(b) (2005) operated as an exception to the physician-patient privilege found at Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-90-107(1)(d) (2005). When Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-18-415(1)(b) applied, there was no privilege and, thus, no waiver was required. The trial court properly instructed the jury regarding the presumption of innocence, the burden of proof, and the requirement that the prosecution prove each element of each offense beyond a reasonable doubt. The evidence was substantial and sufficient to support the conclusion by a reasonable person that defendant obtained the prescription medication by deceit and misrepresentation; that is, by conveying a false understanding regarding the purpose of his visit, his medical condition, past treatment for it, and existing prescriptions for narcotic pain relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Watkins


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA1697


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


126 P.3d 309; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1757



November 3, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication: January 24, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Jefferson County District Court No. 00CR1257. Honorable Jane A. Tidball, Judge.
People v. Watkins, 83 P.3d 1182, 2003 Colo. App. LEXIS 1382 (Colo. Ct. App., 2003)



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Jefferson County District Court (Colorado) denying her postconviction motion challenging the constitutionality of her sentence for reckless child abuse resulting in death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a psychotherapist, was convicted of reckless child abuse resulting in death based on a "rebirthing" therapy session that caused the death of a 10-year-old girl. The conviction was affirmed on direct appeal but the appellate court declined to address defendant's equal protection challenge to her 16-year sentence because she had not raised it below. Thereafter, she filed a Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(b) motion for sentence reconsideration, asserting that her sentence violated constitutional equal protection guarantees. The trial court denied her motion. On appeal, she contended that the sentencing scheme under which she was sentenced violated equal protection guarantees. Defendant was properly sentenced. (2005), and that those statutes prescribed a lesser penalty for the same conduct. The appellate court disagreed. She was convicted of having recklessly caused the child's death. She was therefore not similarly situated to persons having negligently caused death to an at-risk juvenile.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Associated Bus. Prods. v. Indus. Claim Appeals Office


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA2370


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


126 P.3d 323; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1759



November 3, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication: January 24, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado WC No. 42-57-682.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, an employer and its insurer, sought review of a final order of the Industrial Claim Appeals Office, Colorado, upholding the imposition of a $ 24,900 penalty for the employer's failure to pay $ 107 in bills incurred by respondent, a workers' compensation claimant.


OVERVIEW: The claimant sustained an industrial injury in 1995 that included a traumatic brain injury and paralysis. As a result, the claimant was permanently and totally disabled. Because of the severity of the claimant's disability and his confinement to a wheelchair, cell telephone service for emergency calls was medically necessary for claimant and therefore was provided by the employer. The administrative law judge (ALJ) found that the claimant submitted requests for payment of the telephone charges to employer, and the employer neglected to pay those bills within the mandated time limits. While recognizing that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-43-304(1) (2005) allowed a penalty of up to $ 500 per day, the ALJ concluded that a penalty of $ 300 per day was sufficient to deter future violations, and the aggregate penalty imposed for the eighty-three days of nonpayment was $ 24,900. The court ruled that the penalty was not unconstitutionally excessive. The employer did not offer any evidence or explanation for its conduct, and the delays in payment had worked a hardship on the claimant's family, including the wife, who provided claimant with attendant care.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

557 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Felder


Court of Appeals No. 03CA2068


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


129 P.3d 1072; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1677



October 20, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 21, 2006.
Writ of certiorari denied Felder v. People, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 219 (Colo., Mar. 20, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court No. 03CR203. Honorable Morris B. Hoffman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of unlawful possession of a schedule II controlled substance and unlawful possession of a schedule II controlled substance with intent to distribute in the City and County of Denver District Court, Colorado. He appealed, asserting that his confrontation rights were violated where a confidential informant was not disclosed and that his sentencing as a habitual criminal was in violation of the rule in Apprendi v. New Jersey.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found defendant's claim was limited to the narrow question of whether, under the United States Supreme Court's decision in Crawford v. Washington, his right of confrontation was violated by the admission, at the pretrial suppression hearing, of hearsay statements made by an unidentified confidential informant. Crawford addressed a defendant's rights of confrontation at trial. The right to confrontation was basically a trial right. The protections afforded by the Confrontation Clause did not apply at pretrial suppression hearings. Thus, defendant's first claim was rejected. Defendant also argued that a detective's testimony at the suppression hearing, identifying him by his nickname, was hearsay that violated his right of confrontation because the detective learned the nickname from the confidential informant. However, any possible error was harmless because a codefendant testified at trial and also identified defendant by his nickname. Finally, as to defendant's sentencing as a habitual criminal under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1.3-801 (2005), the prior conviction exception exempted habitual criminal proceedings from the constitutional jury requirement.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

People v. Tweedy
