CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgments of the conviction entered in the Jefferson County District Court, Colorado, upon the jury verdicts finding him guilty of possession with intent to distribute a schedule II controlled substance, possession of drug paraphernalia, and special drug offender.


OVERVIEW: Hotel staff contacted the police after observing individuals come and go from a particular room throughout the night. The jury's original special offender verdict reflected an obvious mistake. The trial court did not err in resubmitting the issue to the jury.

Droste v. Bd. of County Comm'rs


Court of Appeals No. 04CA0637


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


141 P.3d 852; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1620



October 6, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 15, 2006.
Writ of certiorari granted Droste v. Bd. of County Comm'rs of Pitkin, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 705 (Colo., Aug. 28, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Pitkin County District Court No. 03CV120. Honorable T. Peter Craven, Judge.
Droste v. Bd. of County Comm'rs, 85 P.3d 585, 2003 Colo. App. LEXIS 1371 (Colo. Ct. App., 2003)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After appellee county passed an ordinance creating a temporary moratorium on accepting, processing, and approving development applications concerning certain lands, appellant property owners sought a declaratory judgment that the temporary moratorium was void and requested injunctive relief. The Pitkin County District Court, Colorado, denied injunctive relief and granted the county a summary judgment. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the owners contended the trial court erred in concluding that the moratorium was authorized or permissible under the Colorado Government Land Use Control Enabling Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 29-20-101 et seq. (2005). The appellate court disagreed, holding that the ability to enact such a temporary moratorium was necessarily implied in the Act. The Act and the county planning statute, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 30-28-101 et seq. (2005), had different, though complementary, purposes, and the limitation on temporary zoning in the county planning statute did not prohibit or limit a moratorium on development for the purpose of studies under the Act. Finally, the appellate court disagreed with the owners' characterization of the moratorium as "open ended"; while the stated duration of the moratorium might have been read as "open ended," it was nevertheless constrained by its stated purpose and its length measured by the time reasonably necessary to conduct the requisite studies and prepare the plans. Therefore, the trial court did not err in finding the county had authority under the Act to impose the temporary moratorium.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Cruz-Cesario v. Don Carlos Mexican Foods


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA1272


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


122 P.3d 1078; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1513



September 22, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication: November 23, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Pueblo County District Court No. 04CV224. Honorable David A. Cole, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Alleging that her condition worsened, appellant employee filed a petition to reopen her workers' compensation claim. Appellee employer filed a motion to strike the petition because a medical report was not attached as required by a department of labor and employment rule. The employee sought declaratory relief was unconstitutional. The Pueblo County District Court, Colorado, granted the employer's motion to dismiss. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted the employer's motion to dismiss pursuant to Colo. R. Civ. P. 12(b) on grounds that the employee failed to join the director of the division of workers' compensation as an indispensable party under Colo. R. Civ. P. 19. On review, the employee contended the trial court erred in finding that the director was an indispensable party. The appellate court disagreed as the director was the very party charged with promulgating the rules and administering the Colorado Workers' Compensation Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-40-101 et seq. The employee also contended that the trial court erred in failing to give her the opportunity to join the director once it was determined that the director was an indispensable party. On this point the appellate court agreed; the trial court's reliance on the employee's failure to file a motion to join was not dispositive because the employee had no particular motivation to file such a motion until the trial court determined that the director was indispensable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

561 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Pepper v. Indus. Claim Appeals Office


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA0457


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


131 P.3d 1137; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1514



September 22, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication on April 18, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Pepper v. Indus. Claim Appeals Office, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1828 (Colo. Ct. App., Nov. 10, 2005)
Writ of certiorari granted City of Florence v. Booth, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 314 (Colo., Apr. 17, 2006)
Affirmed by City of Florence v. Pepper, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 796 (Colo., Oct. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 4-578-846.



DISPOSITION: ORDER SET ASIDE AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner volunteer reserve police officer sought workers' compensation benefits when he suffered mental impairment and experienced stress as a result of a shooting incident while performing his duties. The administrative law judge determined that officer was not the city's employee and denied benefits. The Colorado Industrial Claim Appeals Panel affirmed. The officer sought review.


OVERVIEW: On review, the officer challenged the validity of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-40-202(1)(a)(I)(A) (2005) of the Workers' Compensation Act of Colorado on equal protection grounds, claiming there was no rational basis for allowing a governing body to exclude volunteer police from being considered employees under the Act, when all other similarly situated groups listed in the statute, whether regularly employed or volunteers, were deemed employees. The appellate court agreed, finding no valid purpose for allowing police volunteers to be excepted from workers' compensation coverage, while mandating that all other volunteers, who similarly served a vital function and were subject to similar risks and perils, be covered. Thus, even though reducing costs might have been a legitimate government interest, the appellate court concluded that the statute was not rationally related to achieving that purpose because it provided coverage for some volunteers but not others who were similarly situated. Therefore, the officer was entitled to relief from the harsh result of excluding volunteer police, at the government's option, from the definition of an "employee."


OUTCOME: The order denying relief was set aside, and the case was remanded for the administrative law judge's reconsideration of the officer's entitlement, as an employee, to workers' compensation benefits.

People v. Couillard


Court of Appeals No. 03CA1747


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


131 P.3d 1146; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1520



September 22, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication on April 18, 2006.
Rehearing denied by People v. Couillard, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1899 (Colo. Ct. App., Nov. 23, 2005)
Motion granted by People v. Couillard, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 247 (Colo., Apr. 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Jefferson County District Court No. 02CR1752. Honorable Stephen M. Munsinger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction in the Jefferson County District Court (Colorado) entered on a jury verdict finding her guilty of accessory to attempted first degree murder. Defendant was also charged with eluding a police officer but was found not guilty of that charge.


OVERVIEW: A shooting took place at defendant's boyfriend's home when neither defendant nor her boyfriend were present. Defendant contended that the statements she made while under arrest for eluding were inadmissible. The court held that the police had probable cause to arrest defendant in that they had a warrant to arrest defendant's passenger, her cousin, and defendant did not come to a full stop until physically restrained by an officer. The court also held that the term "suspected of" in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-8-105(4) was not unconstitutionally vague because vagueness challenges to prior versions of the accessory statute had been previously rejected, and the court found no grounds for reaching a contrary conclusion. However, the cousin's guilty plea was improperly admitted because it was testimonial under Crawford. Further, under either Crawford or the Roberts-Dement test, the victim's statements made to an officer were inadmissible because defendant did not have opportunity to cross-examine the victim and the prosecution made no showing of the victim's unavailability. The court reversed because the improperly admitted statements were central to establishing an element of the offense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for a new trial.

 

563 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Powell v. City of Colo. Springs


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA2030


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


131 P.3d 1129; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1448



September 8, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication on April 18, 2006.
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part City of Colo. Springs v. Powell, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 252 (Colo., Apr. 10, 2006)
Affirmed by City of Colo. Springs v. Powell, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 296 (Colo., Apr. 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: El Paso County District Court No. 98CV3231. Honorable Timothy J. Simmons, Judge.
City of Colorado Springs v. Powell, 48 P.3d 561, 2002 Colo. LEXIS 513 (Colo., 2002)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a mother and a conservator, brought a negligence complaint against appellee city after the son died and the conservator was injured when they fell into a storm ditch owned and operated by the city. The El Paso County District Court, Colorado, dismissed the complaint. Appellants sought review.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the General Assembly clearly intended the 2003 legislation amending the Colorado Governmental Immunity Act (GIA), Colo. Rev. Stat. § 24-10-101 et seq., to expressly exclude storm water facilities from the definition of "public sanitation facility" to be retroactive. Appellants argued that this was error. The appellate court determined that there was no clear legislative intent that the pertinent statute was to be applied retroactively. Given prior decisions before the adoption of the GIA, the court must have been expected to conclude that drainage facilities fell within the concept of "sanitation facilities" for purposes of municipal liability. The analysis of the separation of powers doctrine under the federal constitution was equally applicable to a consideration of the proper exercise of governmental powers under the state constitution. Any resulting final appellate determination of the jurisdiction of the court under the GIA rendered in a proceeding under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 24-10-108 had to be treated as a final judicial resolution of that issue. The appellate court could not interpret the statute as having a retroactive effect.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

People v. Flippo


Court of Appeals No. 02CA1831


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


134 P.3d 436; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1349



August 25, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by People v. Flippo, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1639 (Colo. Ct. App., Oct. 13, 2005)
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part People v. Flippo, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 491 (Colo., May 30, 2006)
Motion granted by, Writ of certiorari dismissed People v. Flippo, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 977 (Colo., Nov. 28, 2006)
Reversed by, Remanded by People v. Flippo, 159 P.3d 100, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 430 (Colo., 2007)
On remand at, Remanded by People v. Flippo, 2007 Colo. App. LEXIS 2432 (Colo. Ct. App., Dec. 20, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Weld County District Court No. 01CR813. Honorable Jonathan W. Hays, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Weld County District Court (Colorado) of sexual assault. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim testified that defendant penetrated her digitally and raped her. The police recorded a phone conversation between the victim and defendant during which defendant apologized to her for what he had done. During police questioning, defendant, who had not been Mirandized, initially insisted that he had consensual sex with the victim; after an officer told him of the tape recording and accused him of rape, defendant admitted to a detective that he raped the victim. The trial court excluded expert testimony about his developmental disability on the basis that mental retardation was a mental condition within the meaning of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-8-107(3) (2004) and defendant had waived this defense by not raising it at arraignment. The appellate court held that this was reversible error. Defendant sought to admit this evidence not to support a impaired mental condition or insanity defense but only to attack the credibility of his statements to police and his apology to the victim by showing that he was highly susceptible to suggestion, especially by persons of authority. Thus, § 16-8-107(3) and Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-8-103.6 were inapplicable and the evidence was admissible.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

Abromeit v. Denver Career Serv. Bd.


Court of Appeals No. 04CA0653


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


140 P.3d 44; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1277



August 11, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 18, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Abromeit v. Denver Career Serv. Bd., 2006 Colo. App. LEXIS 300 (Colo. Ct. App., Mar. 9, 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied Abromeit v. Denver Career Serv. Bd., 2006 Colo. LEXIS 694 (Colo., Aug. 14, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court Nos. 02CV720 & 02CV4160. Honorable Martin F. Egelhoff, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The City and County of Denver District Court, Colorado, affirmed appellee Denver Career Service Authority Board's (Board) denial of administrative review regarding plaintiff employees' requests for classification to higher pay grades. The employees appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employees argued that the amendments to Career Services Rules 19-10 and 7-66 were not properly adopted as notice was not published in the official newspaper of record. The appellate court found that the rule amendments were the result of a quasi-legislative proceeding that had to be reviewed pursuant to Colo. R. Civ. P. 57. The effectiveness of the amendments could not be reviewed under Colo. R. Civ. P. 106(a)(4). The matter was not within the scope of the appellate court's review as the employees did not seek leave to amend in the district court. There was no indication that the Board intended simply to clarify the law by amending the rules to eliminate administrative appeals; therefore, the appellate court deferred to the Board's conclusion that amendment of Career Services Rule 19-10 and the repeal of Rule 7-66(h) changed the law and eliminated the right to appeal the classification decision of the Personnel Director. Retroactive application of the amendments was reasonable and warranted by the record. This application was merely procedural or remedial and did not impair a vested right. The Board was not equitably estopped from declining to hear the employees' appeals.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

People v. Krutsinger


Court of Appeals No. 04CA0286


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


121 P.3d 318; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1287

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Douglas County District Court No. 02CR674. Honorable Paul A. King, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Douglas County District Court (Colorado), which found him guilty of 10 counts each of sexual assault on a child, sexual assault on a child by one in a position of trust, and aggravated incest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction and the court stated that the trial court erred in excluding a psychologist's testimony. The victim testified in detail regarding statement that she made to the psychologist during the counseling sessions. Thus, she waived her psychologist-patient privilege. Defendant had yet to establish that the trial court's error was of constitutional dimension, so the court remanded for the trial court to make that determination. The psychologist was to testify and the trial court was to determine whether her testimony would have been material to the case, Colo. R. Evid. 103(a), Colo. R. Crim. P. 52(a), and Colo. App. R.35(e). After hearing the testimony, the trial court was to determine whether the evidence, had it been admitted at trial, would have affected the outcome of the case. Although a comment by the prosecutor was improper, in the context of the entire argument and in light of the other evidence before the jury, the court concluded that it was not flagrantly, glaringly, or tremendously improper as to warrant reversal.


OUTCOME: The court remanded for further proceedings and correction of the mittimus.

People v. Patnode


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA1072


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


126 P.3d 249; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1290



August 11, 2005 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]

Released for Publication: January 24, 2006.
Writ of certiorari denied Patnode v. People, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 16 (Colo., Jan. 9, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Larimer County District Court No. 01CR1799. Honorable Daniel J. Kaup, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED, SENTENCE VACATED, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Larimer County District Court (Colorado), which convicted him of one count of possession of a schedule II controlled substance with intent to distribute and one count of resisting arrest. He was sentenced as a habitual offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from the judgment of conviction entered on a jury verdict finding him guilty of one count of possession of methamphetamine with intent to distribute and one count of resisting arrest. He also appealed his sentence as a habitual offender. The court affirmed the conviction, vacated the sentence, and remanded for further sentencing proceedings. The actions of the officers were objectively reasonable and proper, and the resulting search of the passenger compartment incident to his arrest did not violate defendant's Fourth Amendment rights. In addition, the court held that his sentence was improper pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 42-2-206 (2004) because his driving offenses did not amount to grave and serious crimes. While the court recognized that State did have a valid interest in preventing drivers from driving with revoked licenses, an offense under § 42-2-206 was essentially a violation of an administration order. Without additional evidence indicating a greater degree of danger to he public, the two driving offenses could not be considered grave and serious offenses. An extended review of the sentence was necessary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, vacated the sentence, and remanded for further proceedings.

Sereff v. Steedle


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA1445


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


148 P.3d 192; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1291



August 11, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 19, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Sereff v. Steedle, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1716 (Colo. Ct. App., Oct. 27, 2005)
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part Steedle v. Sereff, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 774 (Colo., Sept. 11, 2006)
Reversed by, Remanded by Steedle v. Sereff, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 823 (Colo., Sept. 10, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court No. 96CV6912. Honorable John N. McMullen, Judge. Honorable Robert S. Hyatt, Judge.
Sereff v. Waldman, 30 P.3d 754, 2000 Colo. App. LEXIS 2146 (Colo. Ct. App., 2000)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff husband and children challenged the judgment of the City and County of Denver District Court, Colorado, dismissing their medical malpractice case against defendant resident physician and supervisor.


OVERVIEW: The medical malpractice action arose from the death of the husband's wife. Plaintiffs argued that the trial court erred in finding that the supervisor was a public employee for purposes of the Colorado Governmental Immunity Act (GIA), Colo. Rev. Stat. § 24-10-101 (2004) et seq. The appellate court found that although plaintiffs argued that it was unfair and illogical to allow the supervisor, who was a doctor engaged in private practice, to be covered by the GIA when the doctor was supervising a resident at a private hospital, the policy choice had been made by the Colorado General Assembly. Based on the General Assembly's definition of "public employee" in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 24-10-103(4)(b)(II) (2004), the trial court did not err in determining that the supervisor was a "public employee" for purposes of the GIA. Also, neither the GIA nor the Wrongful Death Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-21-201 (2004) et seq., limited plaintiffs collective recovery to $ 150,000. Each plaintiff potentially could recover the maximum amount of $ 150,000 in damages in the wrongful death action, up to a collective limit of $ 450,000.


OUTCOME: The determination that the supervisor was a public employee was affirmed, and the finding concerning the amount of damages that could be awarded to plaintiffs and dismissal of plaintiffs' claims against defendants was reversed and remanded to the trial court to reinstate plaintiffs' claims.

People v. Hinojos-Mendoza


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA0645


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


140 P.3d 30; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1206



July 28, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 18, 2006. Opinion Modified, and as Modified, Petitions For Rehearing Denied.
Modified and rehearing denied by People v. Hinojos-Mendoza, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1643 (Colo. Ct. App., Oct. 13, 2005)
Rehearing denied by People v. Hinojos-Mendoza, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1839 (Colo. Ct. App., Nov. 10, 2005)
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part Hinojos-Mendoza v. People, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 688 (Colo., Aug. 14, 2006)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Hinojos-Mendoza v. People, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 825 (Colo., Sept. 10, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Adams County District Court No. 98CR1884. Honorable Donald W. Marshall, Judge, Honorable Thomas R. Ensor, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Adams County District Court (Colorado) that convicted him of and sentenced him for possession with intent to distribute 1000 grams or more of a schedule II controlled substance, under a former version of Colo. Rev. Stat § 18-18-405(3)(a) (2004). An informant had set up a buy from defendant and police found a wrapped block containing 1004.5 grams of white powder, which tested as cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the admission of a laboratory report on the block of cocaine violated his right to confrontation under Crawford v. Washington; and that the report was a hearsay document. The trial court had admitted the report under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-3-309(5) (2004), which allowed admission of laboratory reports without the testimony of the preparing technician if a defendant failed to give notice and demand that the technician testify. On appeal, the court held that defendant failed to preserve his constitutionality challenge of § 16-3-309(5) for appeal. The court also held that the report was not "testimonial" and thus, Crawford did not require its exclusion; and that the report was admissible under the hearsay business record exception in Colo. R. Evid. 803(6). The court found that any error resulting from the admission of the police officer's testimony regarding the informant's statements was harmless because defendant objected in part and the objected-to hearsay testimony was cumulative of the unobjected-to hearsay. The court rejected defendant's claims of error regarding the jury instructions, his Batson challenge, the prosecution's remarks, and his sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that convicted and sentenced defendant for possession with intent to distribute cocaine.

Rice v. Auraria Higher Educ. Ctr.


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA0086


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


131 P.3d 1096; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 928



June 16, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication on April 18, 2006.
Reported at Rice v. Auraria Higher Educ. Ctr., 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 936 (Colo. Ct. App., June 16, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Colorado State Personnel Board No. 2002B092(C).



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, two former employees of a state university media center, were laid off when administrative control of the media center was transferred from the university to respondent higher education center. The employees appealed the Colorado State Personnel Board's decision concluding that the actions of the education center in failing to transfer the employees were not arbitrary, capricious, or contrary to law.


OVERVIEW: After the transfer of administrative control, the media center's structure was modified only by a reduction in the number of positions, and the positions continued to be substantially similar. The employee who worked as an electronic specialist filed an application for a transfer to the education center, but the other employee, who worked as a media specialist, did not. The media specialist signed a notice of intention to exercise his retention rights, but the electronic specialist did not. Because the education center did not consider seniority or performance as required by Colo. Dep't Pers. Regs. No. 7.4, an administrative law judge (ALJ) found that the education's center's actions with respect to the electronic specialist were arbitrary and capricious. On appeal, the court held that the ALJ's findings were supported by the evidence and that the Board's reversal of the ALJ's conclusion had no reasonable basis. By failing to apply for a position with the education center, the media specialist did not provide notice of his intent to protect his tenure right; thus, the media specialist was precluded from challenging the education center's hiring decisions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Board's order regarding the media specialist, reversed the Board's order regarding the electronic specialist, and remanded the matter with directions to reinstate the ALJ's order requiring the education center to appoint the electronic specialist pay him back pay and benefits.

People ex rel. C.M.


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA1144


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION A


116 P.3d 1278; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 839



June 2, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication: August 16, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Morgan County District Court No. 02JV97. Honorable Douglas R. Vannoy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT VACATED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a dependency or neglect proceeding, the Morgan County District Court (Colorado) awarded permanent legal custody of appellant father's child to appellees, the child's maternal grandfather and his wife (grandparents). The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: Due to the child's mother's drug use and neglect, the trial court sustained the department of social service's petition in dependency or neglect and placed the child in the grandparents' temporary custody. The father reasonably complied with a treatment plan, but after he separated from his girlfriend and moved to another city, his instability caused the department seek an award of custody to the grandparents. The trial court did not find the father unfit but found him "unsuitable" to be the custodian based on his instability and drug use. The appellate court held that the trial court erred in relying on Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 19-1-102, -104, -115, and 19-3-508 (2004) in awarding the grandparents permanent custody. As the dependency or neglect proceeding had been pending for over 12 months when the department sought permanent custody, the trial court should have applied Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-3-702 (2004). It rejected the father's argument that the custody order was erroneous because he had not been deemed unfit; under the dependency or neglect statutes, an award of permanent custody to a nonparent could be made even if a parent was not found to be unfit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated, and the case was remanded with directions to determine the issue of permanent custody in accordance with the applicable statute.

People v. Silva


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA0661


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


131 P.3d 1082; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 843



June 2, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication on April 18, 2006.
Rehearing denied by People v. Silva, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1072 (Colo. Ct. App., July 7, 2005)
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part Silva v. People, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 306 (Colo., Apr. 17, 2006)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Silva v. People, 2007 Colo. LEXIS 350 (Colo., Apr. 23, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Mesa County District Court No. 98CR57. Honorable Nicholas R. Massaro, Judge.
People v. Silva, 2003 Colo. App. LEXIS 726 (Colo. Ct. App., May 8, 2003)



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED IN PART AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate filed a postconviction motion under Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c), alleging, inter alia, that his postconviction counsel provided ineffective assistance and had a conflict of interest. The Mesa County District Court (Colorado) denied the motion on grounds that it was untimely; he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate also challenged his conviction, his sentence, and the effectiveness of appellate counsel. The appellate court held that as the time bar in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-5-402(1) was not tolled during the litigation of the inmate's first postconviction motion, his second motion was untimely as to all claims except those involving postconviction counsel's alleged ineffectiveness and conflict of interest. The inmate alleged his postconviction counsel, a deputy public defender, had a conflict of interest because the inmate had alleged ineffective assistance against another deputy public defender, now postconviction counsel's superior, who had briefly represented the inmate before appointment of alternative defense counsel for the trial. The inmate's ineffective assistance claims, other than the alleged conflict of interest, failed because he had no constitutional or statutory right to postconviction counsel. However, under Coleman, appointment of counsel with a conflict of interest could constitute a "factor external to the defense" impeding counsel's efforts, akin to "interference by officials"; therefore, that claim was cognizable in a postconviction proceeding.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed solely as to the dismissal of the inmate's claims that his postconviction counsel had a conflict of interest. On remand, the district court had to determine if justifiable excuse or excusable neglect existed for the untimely filing and if so, whether a separate hearing was required on the merits.

Court of Appeals No.: 04CA0680


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


121 P.3d 301; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 845

Rehearing denied by Dillard v. Indus. Claim Appeals Office, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1053 (Colo. Ct. App., June 30, 2005)
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part Dillard v. Pepsi Bottling Group, 2005 Colo. LEXIS 950 (Colo., Oct. 17, 2005)

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant sought review of the decision of respondent, the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado (Panel), which found in favor of respondent employer and determined that her claim was subject to the benefit cap in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-42-107.5 (2004).


OVERVIEW: The claimant appealed a final order of the Panel determining that her claim for temporary and permanent partial disability payments against her employer was subject to the $ 60,000 benefit cap in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-42-107.5 (2004). The court affirmed, stating that based on the legislative history and the purpose of the statutory changes, it agreed with the employer and Panel that a mental impairment rating could not be combined with a nonscheduled impairment rating to determine whether a claimant's whole person impairment exceeded 25 percent for purposes of determining the applicable benefits cap under § 8-42-107.5. OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Grady


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA0830


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION A


126 P.3d 218; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 758



May 19, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]

Released for Publication: January 24, 2006.
Writ of certiorari denied Grady v. People, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 15 (Colo., Jan. 9, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Arapahoe County District Court No. 02CR978. Honorable James F. Macrum, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: RULING DISAPPROVED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with thirty-nine counts of sexual exploitation of a child, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-6-403 (2004), based on photographs seized in a search of his photography studio and photographs appearing on his website. Defendant was acquitted of all charges. The People sought review of the Arapahoe County District Court's (Colorado) ruling and jury instructions concerning the elements of the charge of sexual exploitation of a child.


OVERVIEW: The trial court interpreted the requirement in the definition of "erotic nudity" that the material be for the purpose of real or simulated overt sexual gratification or stimulation of one or more of the persons involved subjectively, so as to refer only to the sexual gratification of defendant. The People asserted that the trial court erred in adopting a subjective test to define "erotic nudity" and in instructing the jury according to that definition. The People argued that an objective test, so as to include a reasonable viewer of sexual materials that have been distributed, furthered the intent of protecting children from sexual exploitation. The appellate court ruled that the trial court erred in its ruling limiting the scope of the statute subjectively to defendant, and rejected defendant's argument that extending the meaning of "involved" objectively to others who view such material would render the statute unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The People must prove that a person knowingly took sexually explicit photographs of a child and that the content of those photographs, viewed objectively, would lead to sexual gratification or stimulation of a reasonable viewer.


OUTCOME: The ruling of the trial court was disapproved.

Leske v. Golder

DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED IN PART AND ORDER AFFIRMED.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's conviction for incidents related to the sexual assault of a child were affirmed on appeal, a writ of habeas corpus in federal district court was denied, and the denial was affirmed. The denial of defendant's subsequent motions for postconviction relief were also affirmed. The Logan County District Court, Colorado, then denied defendant's petition for writ of habeas corpus. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended, inter alia, that the State's answer brief should have been stricken because it was not timely filed. The appellate court disagreed, ruling that under Colo. His claims regarding his conviction and sentence had already been ruled on adversely to him in previous motions and appeals, the appellate court refused to consider them again. As a bond under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 20-1-201 (2004) was discretionary, and defendant failed to establish that the deputy district attorney who prosecuted him was required to file a bond, the appellate court rejected his contention that the prior court had no jurisdiction to prosecute him.


OUTCOME: Defendant's complaints on appeal as to his conviction and sentence were dismissed. Otherwise, the judgment was affirmed.

McLane W., Inc. v. Dep't of Revenue


Court of Appeals No. 03CA2471


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


126 P.3d 211; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 672



May 5, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication: January 24, 2006.
Writ of certiorari denied McLane Western, Inc. v. Dep't of Revenue, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 6 (Colo., Jan. 9, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by McLane Western, Inc. v. Colo. Dep't of Revenue, 127 S. Ct. 42, 166 L. Ed. 2d 18, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 5703 (U.S., 2006)
Related proceeding at McLane Western, Inc. v. Dep't of Revenue, 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 2080 (Colo. Ct. App., Nov. 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court Nos. 02CV5118 & 02CV5777. Honorable Joseph E. Meyer, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation brought suit against appellee department of revenue seeking refunds pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 39-28.5-101 et seq. (2004) of what it asserted were excess "other tobacco products" (OTP) excise taxes it paid. The City and County of Denver District Court, Colorado, granted the department's motion for summary judgment. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the corporation contended the excise tax imposed by Colorado on the sale, use, consumption, handling, or distribution of certain tobacco products in the state under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 39-28.5-102 (2004) violated the Commerce Clause of the U.S. Constitution, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3. While the appellate court agreed with the corporation's assertions that the tax base would be higher the later in the distribution network the product was taxed, it disagreed with the corporation's conclusion that this fact rendered the tax unconstitutional. Under the third prong of the Complete Auto test, the OTP tax neither facially discriminated nor had the effect of discriminating against out-of-state competitors. Further, the OTP tax scheme did not pressure out-of-state businesses to move to Colorado. Out-of-state manufacturers or distributors could engage in commerce within Colorado without suffering any burden from which local distributors or manufacturers are exempted.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Lassek


Court of Appeals No.: 02CA2142


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


122 P.3d 1029; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 586



April 21, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: November 23, 2005.
Rehearing denied by People v. Lassek, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 1456 (Colo. Ct. App., Sept. 8, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Douglas County District Court. No. 01CR674. Honorable Paul A. King, Judge.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE AND ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to leaving the scene of an accident involving death, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 42-4-1601(1) (2004), leaving the scene of an accident involving serious bodily injury, § 42-4-1601(1), tampering with physical evidence, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-8-610(1)(a) (2004), and careless driving, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 42-4-1402(1) (2004). Defendant appealed the sentence and restitution order entered by the Douglas County District Court (Colorado).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court's consideration of evidence regarding the character of the deceased victim violated defendant's Sixth Amendment confrontation right and rendered the sentencing proceedings fundamentally unfair in violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Colo. Const. art. II, § 25. Finding no authority that either recognized a constitutional right of confrontation in sentencing proceedings or treated receipt of victim character evidence as a due process violation, the court rejected defendant's constitutional arguments. Because defendant's sentence did not exceed the cap in his plea bargain, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1-409(1) (2004) precluded review of defendant's nonconstitutional challenges. The restitution order properly included a payment to the deceased victim's parents for burial expenses and travel costs to attend a memorial service and court appearances; defendant's conduct was the proximate cause of the parents' attendance at the memorial service, and the trial court did not err in refusing to reduce restitution by the insurance settlement paid to the parents by defendant's insurer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence and the restitution order.

 

578 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Colo. Crim. Justice Reform Coalition v. Ortiz


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA0879


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


121 P.3d 288; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 515



April 7, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: October 20, 2005.
Writ of certiorari denied Colo. Crim. Justice Reform Coalition v. Ortiz, 2005 Colo. LEXIS 944 (Colo., Oct. 17, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] City and County of Denver District Court. No. 03CV7725. Honorable John N. McMullen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, prison reform coalition and individuals, appealed from a judgment of the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) that was entered in favor of defendants, executive director of the Corrections Department, the governor, the State, and members of the Board of Regents of Colorado University, in plaintiffs' declaratory action challenging the constitutionality of H.B. 1256, Gen. Assem. (Colo. 2003).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs claimed H.B. 1256 violated the single subject requirement of Colo. Const. art. V, § 21 because funding for a prison and for academic facilities constituted two separate subjects. Plaintiffs also claimed it violated the Taxpayer's Bill of Rights (TABOR), Colo. Const. art. X, § 20(4)(b), which required voter approval in advance for the creation of any multiple-fiscal year debt or other financial obligation by the State. The court held that H.B. 1256 did not violate the single subject rule because it contained only one subject, which was the use of lease-purchase agreements to fund capital construction of certain state facilities, and the fact that it authorized two specific agreements for the construction of two projects did not convert the single subject into two disconnected and incongruous matters. The court held that H.B. 1256 did not violate the TABOR because it did not create multiple-year debt or other financial obligations, thus it was not subject to voter approval. The court concluded that the lease-purchase agreements did not pledge the credit of the State nor require the borrowing of funds. Also the trial court did not err in granting judgment on the pleadings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

In re Petition of R.A.


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA0503


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


121 P.3d 295; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 525



April 7, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication: October 20, 2005.
Rehearing denied by In re Petition of R.A., 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 974 (Colo. Ct. App., June 23, 2005)
Writ of certiorari granted In re Adoption of C.A. v. R.A., 2005 Colo. LEXIS 889 (Colo., Oct. 3, 2005)
Reversed by, Remanded by N.F. v. R.A., Jr. ( In re Adoption of C.A.), 2006 Colo. LEXIS 559 (Colo., June 26, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: El Paso County District Court No. 99JA11. Honorable David L. Shakes, Judge.
In re Petition of R.A. for the Adoption of C.A., 66 P.3d 146, 2002 Colo. App. LEXIS 1684 (Colo. Ct. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: ORDER VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the adoptive parents (parents), sought review of the decision of the El Paso County District Court (Colorado), which found in favor of respondents, the natural paternal grandparents (grandparents), and entered an order reinstating visitation rights to the grandparents.


OVERVIEW: The child was born in May 1992; his father died just before he turned two and his mother died just before he turned 5. The parents currently appealed from the trial court's order reinstating visitation rights to the grandparents and the court vacated the order on appeal, stating that it was not persuaded by the grandparents' assertion that adoptive parents' wishes were not entitled to as much weight as those of natural parents. Because the court discerned no statutory basis pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-5-211(1) (2004) for differentiating between the rights of natural and adoptive parents in the area, it concluded that, in a dispute over grandparent visitation, the wishes of adoptive parents were entitled to the same consideration as those of natural parents. The magistrate was not free to disregard the parents' wishes simply because it would have been in the child's best interests to do so. The magistrate had to find either that the parents were unfit or that their decisions to regulate visitation would have substantially endangered the emotional health of the child. The magistrate found neither, nor would the record have supported such a finding.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and order.

Cericalo v. Indus. Claim Appeals Office


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA1514


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


114 P.3d 100; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 541; Unemployment Ins. Rep. (CCH) P8626



April 7, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication: July 07, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. DD No. 28872004.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant sought review of a final order of the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado (the panel), which found that claimant's unemployment benefits were properly reduced pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-73-110(3)(a)(I)(A) (2004).


OVERVIEW: The claimant suffered complications of diabetes and had been receiving Social Security Disability Insurance (SSDI) benefits for a number of years. After the claimant was laid off from a part-time job, he sought and received unemployment. The Division of Employment later learned that the claimant was receiving SSDI benefits and it determined that, because of the offset, the claimant could not be paid unemployment benefits pursuant to § 8-73-110(3)(a)(I)(A). On appeal, the court found that the panel properly ruled that § 8-73-110(3)(a)(I)(A) required that the claimant's unemployment benefits be reduced by half of the prorated weekly amount of his SSDI benefits, resulting in his ineligibility to receive any unemployment benefits. The court found no violation of the nondiscrimination provisions of the Americans with Disabilities Act by the application of the statutory offset requirements and rejected the claimant's arguments that § 8-73-110(3)(a)(I)(A) was otherwise unconstitutional. Finally, the court noted that the issue of whether the claimant was overpaid was not adjudicated in the administrative proceedings and was thus not properly before the court on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

 

581 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Fullerton v. County Court


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA2317


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION A


124 P.3d 866; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 674



April 5, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication: December 23, 2005.
Writ of certiorari denied Fullerton v. County Court in & for the Boulder, 2005 Colo. LEXIS 1109 (Colo., Dec. 19, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Boulder County District Court No. 02CV834. Honorable Carol Glowinsky, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee citizen was arrested for failing to appear in another state. After being released when he posted a cash bond, the citizen filed a complaint arguing that appellant county court exceeded its jurisdiction by setting bail in the form of a "cash only" bond. The charges were later dismissed and the bond refunded. The Boulder County District Court, Colorado, found that the "cash only" bond was not authorized. The county court appealed.


OVERVIEW: While the undisputed facts showed that a ruling by the instant court would have had no practical legal effect on the citizen, the instant court determined that the question of whether the county court could impose a "cash only" bond on a defendant pending extradition prior to service of a governor's warrant merited resolution here. As Colorado had adopted the Uniform Criminal Extradition Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-19-101 et seq., (2004), the instant court determined that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-19-117 (2004), which expressly applied to the setting of bail pending extradition. After reviewing case law in several jurisdictions, the instant court concluded that in reference to bail, the term "sureties" referred to a broad range of guarantees used for the purpose of securing the appearance of the defendant. Such guarantees included, but were not limited to, bonds secured by cash. Therefore, prior to service of a governor's warrant, a trial court was authorized to require bond for a defendant pending extradition in any type necessary to secure his or her appearance. Accordingly, the county court was within its jurisdiction to impose a "cash only" bond.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

People v. Golden


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA0191


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


140 P.3d 1; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 343



March 10, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 18, 2006.
Reported at People v. Golden, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 377 (Colo. Ct. App., Mar. 10, 2005)
Rehearing denied by People v. Golden, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 2161 (Colo. Ct. App., Dec. 29, 2005)
Writ of certiorari denied People v. Golden, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 568 (Colo., June 26, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Adams County District Court. No. 02CR650. Honorable Thomas R. Ensor, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Adams County District Court (Colorado), which convicted him of sexual assault through application of force or violence and sexual assault by means calculated to cause submission against the victim's will in violation of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-402(1)(a), (4)(a) (2004).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his sexual assault conviction, contending that the trial court erred in limiting his cross-examination of the victim by excluding under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-3-407 (2004), the rape shield statute, an inquiry into whether she was in a "committed romantic relationship" with a roommate at the time of the alleged assault. The purpose of the inquiry was to establish that the victim had a motive to lie concerning whether the sex was consensual. The court agreed and reversed and remanded for a new trial. The statute would not have been violated had defendant been allowed to inquire into the victim's prior inconsistent statements acknowledging a committed romantic relationship. The victim would not have been subjected to a fishing expedition into her past sexual conduct. Rather, the inquiry would have called into question her credibility and her possible motive in telling her roommates that she had been sexually assaulted. Such an inquiry was proper under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 16-10-201 (2004) and Colo. R. Evid. 607 and 613. The court was also unable to conclude that the trial court's error did not contribute to the verdict.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a new trial.

Parker v. City of Golden


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA1946


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


119 P.3d 557; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 344



March 10, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication: September 19, 2005.
Reported at Parker v. City of Golden, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 381 (Colo. Ct. App., Mar. 10, 2005)
Writ of certiorari granted in part and denied in part City of Golden v. Parker, 2005 Colo. LEXIS 722 (Colo., Aug. 22, 2005)
Reversed by, Remanded by City of Golden v. Parker, 2006 Colo. LEXIS 558 (Colo., June 26, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Jefferson County District Court. No. 02CV1810. Honorable Jane A. Tidball, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and case remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer challenged a decision from the Jefferson County District Court (Colorado), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, several developers and a city, in a declaratory action seeking to determine the applicability of the city's charter amendment concerning the payment of incentives and subsidies.


OVERVIEW: The city established an economic incentive program that allowed for the reimbursement of local property taxes. Later, the city's charter was amended to require voter approval for development subsidies or incentives of $25,000. The taxpayer brought a declaratory action to determine the applicability of the charter amendment. After summary judgment was granted, the taxpayer sought review. In reversing, the court determined that the charter amendment was not unconstitutionally retrospective. The developers did not have a vested right under the incentive agreements. The agreements precluded the existence of financial obligations beyond one year. The city's implied duty of good faith and fair dealing did not create any vested rights either. Next, the court held that the retrospective application of the amendment would not have resulted in the creation of a new disability, duty, or obligation with respect to transactions already past. The developers only had a mere expectancy interest; therefore, there was no disability of constitutional magnitude. Since there were no vested rights, there was no violation of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 or Colo. Const. art. II, § 11.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court for a determination of whether the charter amendment was intended to apply retroactively to the incentive agreements in the case. The trial court was also ordered to reconsider the claims regarding the validity of an ordinance.

People v. Smith


No. 02CA1515


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


121 P.3d 243; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 253



February 24, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: October 20, 2005.
Writ of certiorari denied People v. Smith, 2005 Colo. LEXIS 902 (Colo., Oct. 11, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] City and County of Denver District Court No. 01CR3471. Honorable Sheila A. Rappaport, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and sentence affirmed in part and vacated in part; case remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado), which convicted defendant of attempted criminally negligent homicide, vehicular assault, theft from a person, forgery, and unauthorized use of a financial transaction device. Defendant also appealed the sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant drove companions to a store where the companions took a fanny pack from a victim's grocery cart. The victim followed them out of the store and was injured by being thrown back as defendant sped away. The court held that even if the counts had been tried separately, evidence of the use of the stolen credit card would have been admissible to prove that defendant was involved. The court further held that the theft from the victim's shopping cart did not constitute an invasion of the victim's person pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-4-401(5). However, defendant's actions did constitute theft under § 18-4-401(1). As to the vehicular assault, defendant justified her actions by indicating that a strange woman had grabbed her car, and so the record was replete with evidence that defendant's actions caused the victim's injuries. The trial court did not state where it obtained the facts on which it based the aggravated sentence, and the facts were not found by the jury to be aggravating. Therefore, the sentence violated defendant's Sixth Amendment right to a jury trial. Finally, attempted criminally negligent homicide was not a cognizable offense in Colorado and had to be removed.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of conviction for theft from a person and remanded for correction of the mittimus to remove the conviction for attempted criminally negligent homicide and for resentencing on the theft and vehicular assault convictions. The judgment and sentence were otherwise affirmed.

People v. Orth


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA0969


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


121 P.3d 256; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 255



February 24, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication: October 20, 2005.
Rehearing denied by People v. Orth, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 792 (Colo. Ct. App., May 19, 2005)
Writ of certiorari denied Orth v. People, 2005 Colo. LEXIS 915 (Colo., Oct. 11, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: El Paso County District Court. No. 01CR1212. Honorable G. David Miller, Jr., Judge. Honorable Peter W. Booth, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of criminal mischief and conspiracy to commit criminal mischief in the El Paso County District Court, Colorado. Defendant appealed, challenging his sentence for the conspiracy conviction. He asserted that his aggravated range sentence was unconstitutional because it was imposed based on a factual determination of extraordinary aggravating circumstances impermissibly made by the sentencing court, rather than by a jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant also asserted the trial court erred by granting the prosecution's challenge for cause to a prospective juror. However, the prosecution did not use all its peremptory challenges. Thus, any possible error was harmless. The appellate court noted that pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1.3-301(1)(b) (2004), the statutory framework under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1.3-401(6) (2004) also governed the length of direct sentences to community corrections. Secondly, a defendant's prior criminal convictions could constitute an extraordinary aggravating circumstance within the meaning of § 18-1.3-401(6). A Sixth Amendment violation occurred when the sentencing court found facts other than a prior conviction and aggravated a defendant's sentence based thereon. In the latter case, a defendant had a right to a jury trial, and such factors had to be proven beyond a reasonable doubt. In the instant case, the trial court found defendant had committed a previous felony and numerous misdemeanors, "facts" that legitimately could be employed by a sentencing court in imposing a sentence without running afoul of the Sixth Amendment. Thus, defendant's sentence was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

People v. Blankenship


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA0665


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


119 P.3d 552; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 171



February 10, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: September 19, 2005.
Writ of certiorari denied Blankenship v. People, 2005 Colo. LEXIS 744 (Colo., Aug. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Adams County District Court Nos. 96CR1953 & 96CR2081. Honorable John E. Popovich, Jr., Judge. Honorable John J. Vigil, Judge.
People v. Blankenship, 30 P.3d 698, 2000 Colo. App. LEXIS 1888 (Colo. Ct. App., 2000)



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, sought review of the decision of the Adams County District Court (Colorado), which denied his post-conviction motion under Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who ran away from his home in Illinois, was convicted on jury verdicts in two separate trials for kidnapping, robbery, burglary, and murder of an elderly woman. Following his arrest and after signing a form waiving his Miranda rights, he made incriminating statements to the police that were later admitted at trial. The verdicts were affirmed on an earlier direct appeal and defendant's post-conviction motion was subsequently denied. On appeal, the court affirmed, stating that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-2-511(2)(a)(III) (2004), did not confer a fundamental right. Section 19-2-511 did not diminish Fifth Amendment protections. Rather, it provided for additional protection. The provision did not abrogate Miranda's protections, but required that a runaway juvenile's statements were not admissible unless he made a valid waiver pursuant to § 19-2-511(2)(a). His equal protection challenge failed to show that the disparate treatment bore no rational relationship to a legitimate legislative purpose or governmental objective. Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-2-511 (2005) was thus constitutional under a rational basis standard.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re D.C.


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA0249


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


116 P.3d 1251; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 175



February 10, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: August 16, 2005.
Rehearing denied by In re D.C., 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 808 (Colo. Ct. App., May 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Larimer County District Court No. 02JV504. Honorable Cynthia Marie Hartman, Magistrate.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner grandparents appealed from an order of the Larimer County District Court (Colorado) dismissing their petition for grandparent visitation under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-1-117 (2004) for lack of standing.


OVERVIEW: The grandmother contended that the trial court erred in determining that it lacked jurisdiction to grant grandparent visitation with respect to the two older children. The grandmother argued that she had standing to proceed under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 19-1-117(1) (2004) because the children did not reside with their father, and the case did not involve an intact family. The appellate court concluded that the plain language of § 19-1-117 did not authorize the trial court to hear the grandmother's petition because there had been no judicial intervention into the marriage of the children's parents under § 19-1-117(1)(a), judicial placement of the children outside their family under § 19-1-117(1)(b), or death of the grandparent's child under § 19-1-117(1)(c). The children were in the care and custody of their mother, the grandmother's daughter, and she was making determinations regarding the level of contact that the children had with her own family. Under the circumstance, the appellate court found no reason to deviate from the plain meaning of the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Negron v. Gillespie


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA1977


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


111 P.3d 556; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 107



January 27, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 24, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Negron v. Gillespie, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 354 (Colo. Ct. App., Mar. 10, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: El Paso County District Court. No. 01CV3299. Honorable David A. Gilbert, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sought review of a decision of the El Paso County District Court (Colorado), which dismissed the inmate's claims against defendant prison officials. The inmate had sought mandamus relief under Colo. R. Civ. P. 106(a)(2) because the inmate claimed that the prison's charges for medication were excessive and that the amount of time that the inmate had to wait for treatment violated his Eighth Amendment right to medical care.


OVERVIEW: The inmate challenged a policy of the Colorado Department of Corrections that required co-payments for medical visits medication. The inmate also alleged that a wait of 13 days to see the nurse for a headache violated his Eighth Amendment rights. The trial court dismissed the complaint, and the court affirmed. The court held that the inmate failed to establish an Eighth Amendment violation because the mere failure to provide aspirin for a headache for 13 days, without more, did not constitute deliberate indifference to medical needs. The co-payments were not unreasonable and they were authorized by Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-1-113(2). The inmate failed to state any grounds for mandamus relief because he did not show that the amount of the co-payments at issue was unreasonable. The inmate had not shown that he had attempted to obtain a waiver of the co-payment from the DOC, or that he had been denied treatment because of his inability to make the co-payment. The inmate's claim that the co-payments impacted his ability to pay for postage for legal mail or service of other legal papers did not allege a claim for denial of access to the courts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the inmate's claim.

Rector v. City & County of Denver


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA0857


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


122 P.3d 1010; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 110



January 27, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication: November 23, 2005.
Writ of certiorari denied Rector v. City & County of Denver, 2005 Colo. LEXIS 972 (Colo., Oct. 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court. No. 02CV6255. Honorable Robert L. McGahey, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part; case remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a putative class action, plaintiff motorists appealed a judgment of the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado) that dismissed with prejudice their claims against defendants, city, county, and ticket processing company, concerning fines and late fees assessed for parking violations. The motorists sought return of the late fees and declaratory and injunctive relief as to their rights under the Denver Municipal Revised Code (DMRC).


OVERVIEW: The motorists claimed that late fees on parking violations under Denver, Colo., Rev. Mun. Code. 54-829 violated the DMRC provisions that prohibited the collection of fees for ordinance violations unless specifically provided for in the DMRC. The trial court dismissed the motorists' claim based on unjust enrichment because immunity was not waived by the Colorado Governmental Immunity Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 24-20-202 et seq. (2004), and recovery was precluded under the voluntary payment rule. The trial court dismissed their claims under the Federal and Colorado Fair Debt Collection Practices Acts, 15 U.S.C.S. § 1692 et seq. and Colo. Rev. Stat. § 12-14-101 et seq. (2004), and the Colorado Consumer Protection Act, Colo. Rev. Stat. § 6-1-101 et seq. (2004), concluding that parking ordinances did not give rise to a commercial transaction. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred in dismissing the motorists' claim for declaratory and injunctive relief because the requested relief addressed future conduct and was not barred under the voluntary payment rule and the motorists' allegations were sufficient to make them "interested persons" under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-51-106.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the judgment that dismissed the motorists' declaratory and injunctive relief claim and that awarded attorney fees to the ticket processing company and remanded the case for further consistent proceedings. The court affirmed the remainder of the trial court judgment.

People v. Owen


Court of Appeals No.: 02CA2369


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FOUR


122 P.3d 1006; 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 61



January 13, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: November 23, 2005.

 [**1]
Writ of certiorari denied Owen v. People, 2005 Colo. LEXIS 1023 (Colo., Nov. 15, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court No. 01CR1163. Honorable Sheila A. Rappaport, Judge.
People v. Owen, 2000 Colo. App. LEXIS 695 (Colo. Ct. App., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado), which denied his Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c) motion for postconviction relief that asserted that he had been denied his statutory right to a speedy trial under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1-405 (2004).


OVERVIEW: The trial court concluded that defendant had waived his statutory speedy trial rights by entering a guilty plea. Defendant argued that the trial court improperly denied his motion to dismiss based on violation of his statutory speedy trial rights and that the court thereafter lacked jurisdiction to proceed. The court affirmed and held that under the vast weight of authority, the category of nonwaivable jurisdictional defects did not include statutory speedy trial violations. After the trial court denied his motions to dismiss premised on an alleged statutory speedy trial violation, defendant entered an unconditional guilty plea. He did not challenge the voluntariness of that plea either in the trial court or on appeal. At the providency hearing, the prosecutor specifically noted the understanding that, by pleading guilty, defendant would be forgoing any claim of violation of his speedy trial rights. Thus, by thereafter unconditionally pleading guilty, defendant waived or withdrew any objection he had based upon the speedy trial statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

 

591 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Misenhelter


Court of Appeals No.: 02CA2090


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION A


121 P.3d 230; 2004 Colo. App. LEXIS 2421



December 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion Modified, and as Modified Petition For Rehearing Denied. Released for Publication: October 20, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court No. 01CR3262. Honorable Sheila A. Rappaport, Judge.
People v. Misenhelter, 2004 Colo. App. LEXIS 2482 (Colo. Ct. App., Dec. 30, 2004)



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the City and County of Denver District Court (Colorado), which accepted defendant's plea of guilty to aggravated incest and negligent child abuse and imposed an aggravated sentence of 25 years, which was nine years beyond the presumptive sentence.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a plea agreement, defendant entered a plea of guilty to an aggravated incest charge and negligent child abuse. The parties' agreement provided for a probated sentence on the aggravated incest count and a prison sentence for the negligent child abuse count that was not to exceed 25 years. Defendant did not expressly agree that there were aggravating circumstances on the incest count or that the trial court was authorized to consider the issue of their existence. The trial court imposed a sentence of 25 years, which fell within the aggravated sentencing range. The court concluded that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1-409 (2004) did not preclude review of the case. Section 18-1-409(1) did not prohibit an appeal if the issue raised was based on some irregularity or impropriety in the proceedings that led to the imposition of the sentence. Guided by Apprendi and Blakely, the court determined that a sentence within the aggravated range could not be imposed in this case without having aggravating factors found by a jury or admitted to by defendant.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the sentence imposed by the trial court and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

592 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lehmkuhl


Court of Appeals No.: 02CA0149


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


117 P.3d 98; 2004 Colo. App. LEXIS 2423; 38 A.L.R.6th 743



December 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication: August 16, 2005.
Rehearing denied by People v. Lehmkuhl, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 122 (Colo. Ct. App., Jan. 27, 2005)
Writ of certiorari denied Lehmkuhl v. People, 2005 Colo. LEXIS 719 (Colo., Aug. 8, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Lehmkuhl v. Colorado, 546 U.S. 1109, 126 S. Ct. 1064, 163 L. Ed. 2d 888, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 664 (2006)
Related proceeding at People v. Lehmkuhl, 2008 Colo. App. LEXIS 108 (Colo. Ct. App., Jan. 31, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Lehmkuhl, 2013 Colo. App. LEXIS 1137 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Logan County District Court No. 00CR141. Honorable Douglas R. Vannoy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, sought review of the decision of the Logan County District Court (Colorado), which convicted and sentenced him for two counts of first-degree burglary, two counts of sexual assault, second-degree kidnapping, first-degree aggravated motor vehicle theft, and three counts of menacing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was 17-years-old at the time, was convicted after arriving at a home with a gun and wearing a mask. On appeal, the court affirmed his convictions and sentence, stating that his consent was invalid. Thus, the trial court did not err in failing to grant his motion to suppress the results of blood, saliva, and hair samples taken from him. While defendant was in custody, he and his mother twice consented to the search and seizure of his blood, saliva, and hair samples. While still at defendant's home, the deputies discussed with defendant's mother, in his presence, the possibility of doing some forensic testing. Defendant spontaneously interjected that he did not commit the crimes and wanted to take a blood test to prove it. Further, the trial court did not err in qualifying the prosecution's DNA expert pursuant to Colo. R. Evid. 702, as the expert had extensive experience in serology before he began performing DNA analysis and he had specialized education, experience, and training in DNA testing. Consecutive sentences were appropriate, as the sentencing court was required to abide by the statutes that increased his sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

593 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Starcher


Court of Appeals No. 04CA0241


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION ONE


107 P.3d 1127; 2004 Colo. App. LEXIS 2431



December 30, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] El Paso County District Court No. 97CR4358. Honorable Larry E. Schwartz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: ORDER AFFIRMED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant had previously been convicted in the El Paso County District Court, Colorado, for second-degree assault and crime of violence. He was later convicted for possession of contraband. Thereafter, he filed a motion for postconviction relief in which he alleged that his consecutive sentences were illegal, which the trial court denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced on his first two convictions to seven years in prison, plus three years of mandatory parole. While in prison, he pleaded guilty to possession of contraband and was sentenced to a consecutive 18 months in prison, plus 1 year of mandatory parole. Thereafter, he filed his postconviction motion requesting the trial court to order his 3-year mandatory parole period concurrently with his 18-month sentence. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, defendant contended that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1.3-401(1)(a)(V)(E) (2004) applied to offenders who had multiple convictions and sentences received at the same time in the same case or two or more cases disposed of at the same time. The appellate court held that, pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-22.5-101, defendant's consecutive sentences for second-degree assault and possession of contraband were one continuous sentence, with one period of mandatory parole, and that nothing in Colo. Rev. Stat. § 18-1.3-401(1)(a)(V)(E) or Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-22.5-101 stated that the sentences had to be served at the same time in the same case or that two or more cases had to be disposed of at the same time.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed, and the case was remanded to the trial court with directions to issue a corrected mittimus.

 

594 of 734 DOCUMENTS


Boone v. Bd. of County Comm'rs


Court of Appeals No. 03CA1850


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


107 P.3d 1114; 2004 Colo. App. LEXIS 2305



December 16, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Boone v. Bd. of County Comm'rs, 2005 Colo. App. LEXIS 66 (Colo. Ct. App., Jan. 20, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Elbert County District Court No. 02CV63. Honorable Angela R. Arkin, Judge. Honorable John P. Leopold, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant board of county commissioners challenged a decision from the Elbert County District Court (Colorado), which entered partial summary judgment in favor of plaintiff owners in a dispute over rezoning regulations.


OVERVIEW: The owners had a large tract of land, which they divided into separate parcels. Each of the four parcels had more than 35 acres. Thereafter, they were informed that any building permit would be denied until they received approval for the appropriate land use application. The owners then filed a declaratory action seeking a judgment that the rezoning regulations were illegal and unenforceable under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 30-28-101(10)(b). The trial court granted the owners' motion, and the board appealed. In reversing, the court determined that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 30-28-133 (2004) only authorized subdivision regulations controlled parcels of land smaller than 35 acres. However, this exemption did not preclude the board from requiring them to rezone their parcels that were larger than 35 acres. The exemption did not limit a county's power to enact zoning regulations based on lot size, pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 30-28-111(1) (2004). The county was not prohibited from imposing reasonable fees in connection with rezoning. Finally, the court was unable to determine from the sparse record whether any of the overlapping rezoning requirements reasonably furthered lawful zoning objectives.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.
