Div. of Child Support Enforcement v. Indus. Claim Appeals Office


Court of Appeals No.: 04CA0523


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


109 P.3d 1042; 2004 Colo. App. LEXIS 2215



December 2, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: April 22, 2005.
Writ of certiorari denied Indus. Claim Appeals Office v. Div. of Child Support Enforcement, 2005 Colo. LEXIS 369 (Colo., Apr. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado. WC No. 4501441.



DISPOSITION: Order set aside and case remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Division of Child Support Enforcement (CSE), sought review of the decision of respondent, the Industrial Claim Appeals Office of the State of Colorado (Panel), which concluded that a workers' compensation settlement awarded to respondent claimant was not subject to attachment.


OVERVIEW: In the workers' compensation proceeding, the CSE sought review of the final order issued by the Panel, concluding that a lump sum settlement awarded to the claimant was not subject to attachment and lien for unpaid child support under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 8-43-204(4) (2004). The court set aside the order and remanded with directions, stating that § 8-43-204(4) represented a procedural amendment to the law of workers' compensation, and could therefore be applied retroactively to lump sum settlements reached in cases where the industrial injury occurred before the amendment was enacted. Thus, the Panel erred in determining that the claimant's settlement was not subject to the lien filed by CSE.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the order and remanded for reinstatement of the determination that the claimant's lump sum settlement was subject to the lien filed by CSE.

 

596 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sa'ra


Court of Appeals No.: 02CA2146


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION THREE


117 P.3d 51; 2004 Colo. App. LEXIS 2120



November 18, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]

Released for Publication: August 16, 2005.
Writ of certiorari denied Iemhotep Sa'Ra v. People, 2005 Colo. LEXIS 706 (Colo., Aug. 8, 2005)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by Sa-Ra v. Leyba, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 13515 (D. Colo., Feb. 13, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Arapahoe County District Court No. 01CR709. Honorable John P. Leopold, Judge.
People v. Sa'ra, 2004 Colo. App. LEXIS 1917 (Colo. Ct. App., Oct. 21, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was placed on mandatory parole for two years following service of a prison sentence for forgery and was required to establish a residence of record as a condition of his parole. Defendant designated his wife's residence as his residence of record. Defendant was convicted in the Arapahoe County District Court (Colorado) of escape from intensive supervised parole (ISP). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, defendant argued that the court erred in omitting the "extended limits" language of Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-27.5-104 (2004) from the jury instruction that set forth the elements of escape. The appellate court disagreed. The court defined "custody and confinement," as used in the escape statute, as including the status of an individual who was on ISP from the department of corrections. The instructions as a whole instructed the jury on the crime of escape from ISP. The elements instruction essentially tracked the pattern instruction. Further, the court's definition of custody and confinement informed the jury that ISP constituted custody and confinement. Defendant contended that the trial court violated his right to present a defense by excluding his sister's testimony that he lived with her. The appellate court disagreed. As a condition of ISP, defendant signed a parole agreement that he had to establish a residence of record and would reside there and not change his residence without the consent of his parole officer. The trial court found that evidence was irrelevant to the escape charge, because the escape occurred when defendant left his residence of record.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Vista Resorts, Inc. v. Goodyear Tire & Rubber Co.


Court of Appeals No.: 02CA1690


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


117 P.3d 60; 2004 Colo. App. LEXIS 2119



November 18, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]

Released for Publication: August 16, 2005.
Writ of certiorari denied Goodyear Tire & Rubber Co. v. Vista Resorts, 2005 Colo. LEXIS 704 (Colo., Aug. 8, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Arapahoe County District Court No. 98CV2772. Honorable Timothy L. Fasing, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; remanded for a hearing on attorney's fees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant rubber company appealed a judgment of the Arapahoe County District Court (Colorado) entered in favor of plaintiff builder in a product liability action for breach of implied warranty, strict product liability, failure to warn, negligence, fraud, and violation of the Colorado Consumer Protection Act (CCPA), Colo. Rev. Stat. § 6-1-113. The builder sold luxury homes with radiant heating systems containing rubber hoses that were defective.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the rubber company claimed the homeowners' claims for punitive and treble damages under the CCPA were not assignable and that the trial court erred in admitting evidence of prior complaints about the hoses. The court held that the invited error doctrine precluded the company from asserting that the homeowners' claims were not assignable, as the company moved for the complete substitution of the builder as the real party in interest under Colo. R. Civ. P. 25(c) and asserted that all interests were transferred. The court held that the admission of evidence regarding prior complaints about defects in the hoses was not grounds for reversal, because the evidence was admitted to show the company had notice, not to show the defective nature of the hoses, and did not result in unfair prejudice. The court held that notice was relevant, because, to recover punitive damages under Colo. Rev. Stat. § 13-21-102(1)(a) (2004), the builder needed to prove the company acted willfully. The court rejected the company's equal protection and procedural and substantive due process claims and held that the protection of the public was a rational basis for treble damages under the CCPA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment entered in favor of the builder and remanded the case for an award of attorney fees and costs incurred during the appeal.

Thorpe v. State


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA0243


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


107 P.3d 1064; 2004 Colo. App. LEXIS 1896



October 21, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Writ of certiorari denied Thorpe v. State, 2005 Colo. LEXIS 125 (Colo., Feb. 14, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Thorpe v. Colo., 126 S. Ct. 545, 163 L. Ed. 2d 459, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 7861 (U.S., Oct. 31, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court. No. 99CV2974. Honorable Lawrence A. Manzanares, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers brought a class-action suit challenging the constitutionality of limiting certain tax refunds. The parties cross-moved for summary judgment. The City and County of Denver District Court, Colorado, entered a judgment in favor of defendant State and defendant Executive Director of the Colorado Department of Revenue and Colorado Tax Collector. The taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State was required to refund excess revenue under the Taxpayer's Bill of Rights (TABOR), Colo. Const. art. X, § 20. To comply with TABOR, and to avoid federal income tax implications for recipients, the Colorado General Assembly decided to refund a portion of sales tax collected to full-year residents. The State enacted Colo. Rev. Stat. § 39-22-120 (2004) and Colo. Rev. Stat. §§ 39-22-2001 to 39-22-2003 (2004) to accomplish these objectives. The Colorado General Assembly concluded that proportional refunds were not feasible. The taxpayers claimed that the tax refunds violated U.S. Const. art. IV, § 2. The appellate court disagreed. The relevant inquiry was who paid the most taxes overall, not who paid the most sales tax. The general assembly determined that full-year residents paid most of the taxes. The distinctions were justified. Further, the taxpayers made no specific allegation as to how their right to travel was hindered. Applying a rational basis test, the appellate court also rejected the taxpayers' equal protection argument. Finally, the taxpayers did not establish that the refund statutes have anything more than an incidental burden on interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Jackson


Court of Appeals No.: 03CA0744


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION FIVE


109 P.3d 1017; 2004 Colo. App. LEXIS 1829



October 7, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication: April 22, 2005.
Writ of certiorari denied Jackson v. People, 2005 Colo. LEXIS 231 (Colo., Mar. 21, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: El Paso County District Court No. 99CR2429. Honorable G. David Miller, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c) motion in the El Paso County District Court, Colorado, asserting various grounds upon which to set aside either an additional period of supervision or a sex offender condition of his release from prison. The trial court denied the motion, but subsequently entered an order effectively staying the parole board's supervision of defendant's release. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: After pleading guilty to felony menacing, defendant was sentenced to two years in prison and two years of mandatory parole. Defendant's parole was later revoked and he was reincarcerated for the remainder of his parole period. Near the end of his reincarceration period, defendant was told that he would be required to complete an additional one-year period of post-release supervision. Defendant argued that Colo. Rev. Stat. § 17-22.5-403(9) (a)-(f) was unconstitutional, that he should not have been subject to additional supervision, as he was not advised as such when he entered his plea, and that his sex offender treatment as a condition of supervised release was error. The appellate court noted that defendant's first argument was not preserved for appellate review. The appellate court held that the possibility that a defendant could be subjected to post-release supervision was not a direct consequence of a guilty plea, and thus, the trial court was not obliged to advise defendant of it at the providency hearing. The appellate court concluded that the Colorado Department of Correction's sex offender classification did not fall within the purview of Colo. R. Crim. P. 35(c)(2).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

600 of 734 DOCUMENTS


People v. Allen


Court of Appeals No.: 02CA1061


COURT OF APPEALS OF COLORADO, DIVISION TWO


111 P.3d 518; 2004 Colo. App. LEXIS 1833



October 7, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]

Released for Publication May 24, 2005.
Writ of certiorari denied Allen v. People, 2005 Colo. LEXIS 458 (Colo., May 16, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: City and County of Denver District Court No. 01CR3654. Honorable Gloria A. Rivera, Judge.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of robbery and theft. The trial court adjudicated defendant a habitual criminal based on his prior convictions. The City and County of Denver District Court, Colorado, sentenced defendant to 24 years in the custody of the Colorado Department of Corrections. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: During the second phase of defendant's criminal trial for robbery and theft, the trial court adjudicated defendant a habitual criminal based on prior convictions for unlawful possession of a firearm by a convicted felon, attempted possession of a controlled substance, eluding a pursuing police vehicle, and robbery. Pursuant to Colo. Rev. Stat. § 181.3801(2) (2003), the trial court sentenced defendant to 24 years in custody, four times the maximum presumptive range sentence for robbery. The trial court found that the sentence was not disproportionate. On appeal, defendant contended that the convictions underlying the habitual offender charges were not grave and serious offenses. The appellate court disagreed. Defendant's triggering robbery conviction and his prior convictions for robbery and attempted possession of a controlled substance were all grave and serious offenses. Defendant's out-of-state conviction for eluding a pursuing police vehicle and defendant's federal conviction for possession of a gun by a convicted felon were also grave and serious offenses.


OUTCOME: The sentence was affirmed.
